Shirkah — Partnership
beginner
6 min
The Permissibility and Two Types of Partnership (Shirkah)
Opening of the Book of Partnership: permissibility and classification into co-ownership and contractual partnership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on partnership's permissibility and distinguish between shirkat al-amlak and shirkat al-uqud by their definitions, conditions, and rulings.

Core Idea
Partnership is permissible and has two types: co-ownership and contractual partnership.

Partnership is a foundational concept in Islamic commercial law. The Prophet ﷺ confirmed people's practice of partnership, making it an approved transaction. In this lesson, we explore the opening of the Book of Partnership, where the author declares its permissibility and divides it into two fundamental types. Understanding this classification is critical for further study of partnership rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling
The passage states that partnership is permissible (ja'iz). The basis is the Prophet's tacit approval (taqrir) of the practice among people.
2
Classify the two types
Partnership is divided into shirkat al-amlak (co-ownership of property) and shirkat al-uqud (contractual partnership). This is the foundational categorization.
Memorize the terms and their definitions.
3
Analyze shirkat al-amlak
Co-ownership arises from inheritance, joint purchase, gift, conquest, or mixing of assets. Each co-owner cannot dispose of the other's share without permission. Selling one's share to the co-owner is always allowed; selling to a third party requires permission only if the property is mixed and indistinguishable.
4
Analyze shirkat al-uqud
Contractual partnership is formed by offer and acceptance. Its essential condition is that the underlying transaction must be valid for agency (wakalah), so that profits and losses are shared through mutual agency.
5
Understand the practical significance
The condition of agency ensures that each partner acts as an agent for the other, making the partnership's operations valid and profits shared according to agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الشِّرْكَةِ
الشَّرْكَةُ جَائِزَةٌ لِأَنَّهُ بُعِثَ وَالنَّاسُ يَتَعَامَلُونَ بِهَا فَقَرَّرَهُمْ عَلَيْهِ قَالَ الشَّرْكَةُ ضَرْبَانِ: شِرْكَةُ أَمْلَاكٍ وَشِرْكَةُ عُقُودٍ فَشِرْكَةُ الْأَمْلَاكِ الْعَيْنُ يَرِثُهَا رَجُلَانِ أَوْ يَشْتَرِيَانِهَا فَلَا يَجُوزُ لِأَحَدِهِمَا أَنْ يَتَصَرَّفَ فِي نَصِيبِ الْآخَرِ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ وَكُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا فِي نَصِيبِ صَاحِبِهِ كَالْأَجْنَبِيِّ وَهَذِهِ الشِّرْكَةُ يَتَحَقَّقُ فِي غَيْرِ الْمَذْكُورِ فِي الْكِتَابِ كَمَا إِذَا اتَّهَبَ رَجُلَانِ عَيْنًا أَوْ مَلَكَاهَا بِالِاسْتِيلَاءِ أَوِ اخْتَلَطَ مَالُهُمَا مِنْ غَيْرِ قَصْدٍ أَوْ بِفِعْلِهِمَا خَلْطًا لَا يَتَمَيَّزُ أَوْ لَا يَتَحَلَّلُ إِلَّا بِحَرَجٍ وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ أَحَدِهِمَا نَصِيبَهُ مِنْ شَرِيكِهِ فِي جَمِيعِ الصُّوَرِ وَمِنْ غَيْرِ شَرِيكِهِ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِهِ إِلَّا فِي صُورَةِ الْخَلْطِ وَالِاخْتِلَاطِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ وَقَدْ بَيَّنَّا الْفَرْقَ فِي كِفَايَةِ الْمُنْتَهَى
وَالضَّرْبُ الثَّانِي شِرْكَةُ الْعُقُودِ وَرُكْنُهَا الْإِيجَابُ وَالْقَبُولُ وَهُوَ أَنْ يَقُولَ أَحَدُهُمَا شَارَكْتُكَ فِي كَذَا وَكَذَا وَيَقُولَ الْآخَرُ قَبِلْتُ وَشَرْطُهُ أَنْ يَكُونَ التَّصَرُّفُ الْمَعْقُودُ عَلَيْهِ عَقْدَ الشَّرِكَةِ قَابِلًا لِلْوَكَالَةِ لِيَكُونَ مَا يُسْتَفَادُ بِالتَّصَرُّفِ مُشْتَرَكًا بَيْنَهُمَا فَيَتَحَقَّقَ حُكْمُهُ الْمَطْلُوبُ مِنْه
Book of Partnership. Partnership is permissible because he (the Prophet) was sent while people were transacting with it, and he confirmed them upon it. He said: Partnership is of two types: co-ownership and contractual partnership. As for co-ownership, it is in a specific property that two men inherit or buy. So it is not permissible for one of them to dispose of the other's share except with his permission, and each of them regarding the share of his companion is like a stranger. And this type of partnership is realized in other than what is mentioned in the book, like when two men receive a gift of a specific property, or own it by conquest, or their wealth mixes without intention, or by their action a mix that is indistinguishable or cannot be separated except with difficulty. And the sale by one of them of his share from his partner is permissible in all scenarios, and from someone other than his partner without his permission, except in the case of mixture and mixing, for it is not permissible except with his permission. And we have explained the difference in Kifayah al-Muntaha. The second type is contractual partnership, and its pillar is offer and acceptance: that one of them says 'I partner with you in such and such' and the other says 'I accept.' Its condition is that the transaction covenanted upon in the partnership contract be valid for agency, so that what is gained by the transaction is shared between them, and thus its sought-after ruling is realized.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Partnership (Kitab al-Shirkah) with a statement on permissibility: partnership is permissible because the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) was sent while people were already practicing it, and he confirmed them in that practice, making it a sunnah taqririyyah (tacit approval). The author then quotes al-Quduri, who divides partnership into two fundamental types: (1) Shirkat al-Amwal (co-ownership of property) and (2) Shirkat al-Uqud (contractual partnership). Shirkat al-Amwal refers to joint ownership of a specific asset, whether acquired by inheritance, purchase, gift, conquest (istila'), or unintentional mixing. In such co-ownership, neither partner may dispose of the other's share without permission; each partner is considered a stranger regarding the other's share. The ruling on selling shares varies: selling to the co-owner is always permitted, but selling to a third party is allowed without permission only if the property is not mixed; if mixed (e.g., indistinguishable mixtures like grains), permission is required. The second type, Shirkat al-Uqud, is a contractual partnership formed by offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul), where both parties agree to share profits and losses. Its essential condition is that the underlying transaction must be valid for agency (wakalah), because the partnership operates through mutual agency, so that profits and losses are shared as agreed.

Key Terms
شَركة (shirkah): Partnership; a joint enterprise involving co-ownership or contractual agreement for profit.
شركة الأملاك (shirkat al-amlak): Co-ownership of property; joint ownership that arises from inheritance, purchase, gift, or mixing without separate contract.
شركة العقود (shirkat al-uqud): Contractual partnership formed by offer and acceptance where parties agree to share profits and losses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Shirkat al-Amwal (co-ownership), when may a co-owner sell his share to a third party without the permission of the other co-owner?
A) In all cases, as each co-owner owns his share absolutely.
B) Only if the property is not mixed with the other's share.
C) Only if the other co-owner is absent.
D) Never, a co-owner always needs permission.

Key Takeaway
Partnership is permissible and consists of two distinct types: co-ownership of property and contractual partnership, each with its own rules.

Shirkah — Partnership
beginner
8 min
Partnership: Ruling and Types
Defines partnership, its ruling, and two primary categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partnership and distinguish between shirkat al-amlak and shirkat al-uqud.

Core Idea
Partnership is permissible by prophetic taqrir; ownership partnership requires permission for disposal while contractual partnership requires offer and acceptance.

This lesson from Al-Hidayah opens the Book of Partnership with a fundamental ruling: partnership is permissible. The author then defines two broad categories: partnership in property (shirkat al-amlak) which arises from joint ownership, and contractual partnership (shirkat al-uqud) based on offer and acceptance. Understanding this classification is essential for all subsequent partnership rulings in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
Read the first sentence: 'Partnership is permissible because he (the Prophet) was sent while people were transacting with it, and he confirmed them upon it.' Recognize that the proof is prophetic tacit approval (taqrir).
Taqrir is a valid source of law; it indicates permissibility.
2
Define the two types
The text says partnership is of two types: shirkat al-amlak (ownership partnership) and shirkat al-uqud (contractual partnership). Note the defining characteristics of each.
Shirkat al-amlak requires no contract; shirkat al-uqud requires offer and acceptance.
3
Apply the rules of shirkat al-amlak
Consider a scenario where two people inherit a house. According to the text, each co-owner is like a stranger regarding the other's share. Therefore, one cannot sell the other's share without permission.
Mixing cases also fall under this type.
4
Recognize the condition for shirkat al-uqud
The text states that the transaction must be capable of being delegated (wakalah) so that profits are shared. This condition ensures the partnership achieves its purpose.
This condition excludes acts that cannot be delegated, like personal oaths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الشِّرْكَةِ
الشَّرْكَةُ جَائِزَةٌ لأَنَّهُ بُعِثَ وَالنَّاسُ يَتَعَامَلُونَ بِهَا فَقَرَّرَهُمْ عَلَيْهِ. قَالَ الشَّرْكَةُ ضَرْبَانِ: شِرْكَةُ أَمْلَاكٍ وَشِرْكَةُ عُقُودٍ. فَشِرْكَةُ الْأَمْلَاكِ الْعَيْنُ يَرِثُهَا رَجُلَانِ أَوْ يَشْتَرِيَانِهَا فَلَا يَجُوزُ لِأَحَدِهِمَا أَنْ يَتَصَرَّفَ فِي نَصِيبِ الْآخَرِ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ وَكُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا فِي نَصِيبِ صَاحِبِهِ كَالْأَجْنَبِيِّ. وَهَذِهِ الشِّرْكَةُ تَتَحَقَّقُ فِي غَيْرِ الْمَذْكُورِ فِي الْكِتَابِ كَمَا إِذَا اتَّهِبَ رَجُلَانِ عَيْنًا أَوْ مَلَكَاهَا بِالِاسْتِيلَاءِ أَوِ اخْتَلَطَ مَالُهُمَا مِنْ غَيْرِ قَصْدِ أَحَدِهِمَا أَوْ بِخَلْطِهِمَا خَلْطًا لاَ يَتَمَيَّزُ رَأْسًا أَوْ إِلَّا بِحَرَجٍ. وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ أَحَدِهِمَا نَصِيبَهُ مِنْ شَرِيكِهِ فِي جَمِيعِ الصُّوَرِ وَمِنْ غَيْرِ شَرِيكِهِ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِهِ إِلَّا فِي صُورَةِ الْخَلْطِ وَالِاخْتِلَاطِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ.

وَالضَّرْبُ الثَّانِي شِرْكَةُ الْعُقُودِ وَرُكْنُهَا الْإِيجَابُ وَالْقَبُولُ وَهُوَ أَنْ يَقُولَ أَحَدُهُمَا شَارَكْتُكَ فِي كَذَا وَكَذَا وَيَقُولُ الْآخَرُ قَبِلْتُ. وَشَرْطُهُ أَنْ يَكُونَ التَّصَرُّفُ الْمَعْقُودُ عَلَيْهِ عَقْدَ الشَّرِكَةِ قَابِلًا لِلْوَكَالَةِ لِيَكُونَ مَا يُسْتَفَادُ بِالتَّصَرُّفِ مُشْتَرَكًا بَيْنَهُمَا فَيَتَحَقَّقَ حُكْمُهُ الْمَطْلُوبُ مِنْهُ.

ثُمَّ هِيَ أَرْبَعَةُ أَوْجُهٍ: مُفَاوَضَةٌ وَعِنَانٌ وَشِرْكَةُ الصَّانِعِ وَشِرْكَةُ الْوُجُوهِ. فَأَمَّا شِرْكَةُ الْمُفَاوَضَةِ فَهِيَ أَنْ يَشْتَرِكَ الرَّجُلَانِ فَيَتَسَاوَيَا فِي مَالِهِمَا وَتَصَرُّفِهِمَا وَدَيْنِهِمَا لِأَنَّهَا شِرْكَةٌ عَامَّةٌ فِي جَمِيعِ التِّجَارَاتِ يُفَوِّضُ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا أَمْرَ الشَّرِكَةِ إِلَى صَاحِبِهِ عَلَى الْإِطْلَاقِ إِذْ هِيَ مِنَ الْمُسَاوَاةِ. قَالَ قَائِلُهُمْ شِعْرًا: لَا يَصْلُحُ النَّاسُ فَوْضَى لَا سَرَاةَ لَهُمْ وَلَا سَرَاةَ إِذَا جُهَّالُهُمْ سَادُوا أَيْ مُتَسَاوِينَ. فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ تَحْقِيقِ الْمُسَاوَاةِ ابْتِدَاءً وَانْتِهَاءً وَذَلِكَ فِي الْمَالِ وَالْمُرَادُ بِهِ مَا تَصِحُّ الشَّرِكَةُ فِيهِ وَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ التَّفَاضُلُ فِيمَا لَا يَصِحُّ الشَّرِكَةُ فِيهِ. وَكَذَا فِي التَّصَرُّفِ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ مَلَكَ أَحَدُهُمَا تَصَرُّفًا لَا يَمْلِكُهُ الْآخَرُ لَفَاتَتِ الْمُسَاوَاةُ. وَكَذَلِكَ فِي الدَّيْنِ لِمَا نُبَيِّنُ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ تَعَالَى. وَهَذِهِ الشَّرْكَةُ جَائِزَةٌ عِنْدَنَا اسْتِحْسَانًا وَفِي الْقِيَاسِ لَا يَجُوزُ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ وَقَالَ مَالِكٌ: لَا أَعْرِفُ مَا الْمُفَاوَضَةُ. وَجْهُ الْقِيَاسِ أَنَّهَا تَضَمَّنَتِ الْوَكَالَةَ بِمَجْهُولِ الْجِنْسِ وَالْكَفَالَةَ بِمَجْهُولٍ وَكُلُّ ذَلِكَ بِالْفِرَادَةِ فَاسِدٌ. وَوَجْهُ الِاسْتِحْسَانِ قَوْلُهُ ﷺ: «فَاوِضُوا فَإِنَّهُ أَعْظَمُ لِلْبَرَكَةِ» وَكَذَا النَّاسُ يَتَعَامَلُونَ بِهَا مِنْ غَيْرِ نَكِيرٍ وَبِهِ يُتْرَكُ الْقِيَاسُ وَالْجَهَالَةُ مُتَحَمَّلَةٌ تَبَعًا كَمَا فِي الْمُضَارَبَةِ. وَلَا تَنْعَقِدُ إِلَّا بِلَفْظَةِ الْمُفَاوَضَةِ لِبُعْدِ شَرَائِطِهَا عَنْ عِلْمِ الْعَوَامِّ حَتَّى لَوْ بَيَّنَا جَمِيعَ مَا يَقْتَضِيهِ يَجُوزُ لِأَنَّ الْمُعْتَبَرَ هُوَ الْمَعْنَى.
Book of Partnership. Partnership is permissible because he (the Prophet) was sent while people were transacting with it, and he confirmed them upon it. He said: Partnership is of two types: partnership in property and partnership by contract. Partnership in property is when a specific asset is inherited by two men or they purchase it. Then it is not permissible for one of them to dispose of the other's share without his permission, and each of them with respect to the other's share is like a stranger. And this partnership materializes in other than what is mentioned in the book, such as when two men are given a specific asset as a gift, or they take possession of it by force, or their wealth mixes without intention of either, or by their mixing in a way that it cannot be distinguished at all or only with difficulty. And it is permissible for one of them to sell his share to his partner in all forms, and to a non-partner without his permission except in the case of mixing and blending – then it is not permissible except with his permission.

The second type is contractual partnership. Its pillar is offer and acceptance, which is that one of them says 'I make you a partner in such-and-such' and the other says 'I accept.' Its condition is that the transaction upon which the partnership contract is based must be capable of being delegated, so that what is gained by the transaction is shared between them, thereby achieving its intended ruling.

Then it is of four types: mufawadah, inan, partnership of the artisan, and partnership of faces. As for mufawadah partnership, it is that two men enter a partnership and become equal in their capital, their transactions, and their debts, because it is a general partnership in all types of trade; each of them delegates the affair of the partnership to his partner absolutely, since it is derived from equality. One of their poets said: 'People are not fit when they are levelled – they have no leaders; and there is no leadership when their ignorant ones become leaders' – meaning equals. So equality must be realized from beginning to end. And that is in capital – meaning what partnership is valid in, and disparity is not considered in what partnership is not valid in. Similarly in transactions, because if one of them possessed a transaction that the other does not, equality would be lost. Similarly in debts, as we will explain if Allah wills. This partnership is permissible in our school by istihsan, and by qiyas it is not permissible – that is the saying of al-Shafi'i. Malik said: I do not know what mufawadah is. The basis of qiyas is that it includes agency for an unknown genus and guarantee for an unknown thing, and each individually is invalid. The basis of istihsan is his statement ﷺ: 'Enter into mufawadah for it is greater in blessing'; likewise people transact with it without disapproval, and thus qiyas is abandoned; the ignorance is tolerated as a subsidiary matter, as in mudarabah. It is not contracted except with the word mufawadah, because of the remoteness of its conditions from the knowledge of the common people; but if we explained all that it requires, it is valid – because the consideration is the meaning.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah opens the Book of Partnership. The author first states the ruling: partnership is permissible (ja'izah). The proof is the prophetic tacit approval (taqrir) – the Prophet ﷺ saw people practicing it and did not prohibit it, thus establishing its permissibility. Then the text defines two primary categories: Shirkat al-Amwal (partnership in property) and Shirkat al-Uqud (contractual partnership). Shirkat al-Amwal arises from joint ownership, such as inheritance or joint purchase. In such ownership, each partner is like a stranger regarding the other's share – no disposal without permission. This type also includes cases of mixing (ikhtilat) that are inseparable. The text details when selling one's share is allowed. Then comes Shirkat al-Uqud, which is based on offer and acceptance. Its condition is that the underlying transaction be amenable to agency (wakalah), so profits from dealings are shared. The author then lists the four types of contractual partnership: mufawadah, 'inan, partnership of artisans (sana'i'), and partnership of faces (wujuh). He elaborates on mufawadah, defining it as a general, equal partnership in capital, transactions, and debts – derived from the root 'fawaḍ' meaning equality. The text cites a proverb: society requires leaders, not pure equality – but in partnership, equality is stipulated. The Hanafi position is that mufawadah is valid by istihsan (juristic preference), even though qiyas (analogy) would invalidate it due to uncertainty in agency and guarantee. Imam al-Shafi'i rejects it on qiyas; Imam Malik professes ignorance. The Hanafi response cites a hadith (though with weak chain) and the practice of people; the uncertainty is tolerated as incidental, like in mudarabah. Conditions: it must be expressly worded 'mufawadah'; if the parties explain all conditions, it can be valid without the exact term.

Key Terms
شِرْكَةُ الْأَمْلَاكِ (shirkat al-amlak): Partnership in property arising from joint ownership, e.g., inheritance or purchase, not from contract.
شِرْكَةُ الْعُقُودِ (shirkat al-uqud): Contractual partnership based on offer and acceptance, aimed at trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the basis for the permissibility of partnership?
A) Explicit Quranic verse
B) Prophetic tacit approval (taqrir) of the people's practice
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy (qiyas) from sale

Key Takeaway
Partnership is permissible and is either ownership-based or contract-based; each type has distinct rules for disposal.

intermediate

Mufawadah Partnership: Equality and Istihsan
Defines mufawadah, sets conditions, and discusses the istihsan argument against qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the requirements of mufawadah partnership and justify its validity by istihsan in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Mufawadah requires equal capital, transactions, and debts; it is valid by istihsan despite containing uncertainty in agency and guarantee.

After classifying partnerships into four types, Al-Hidayah focuses on mufawadah, the most comprehensive form. The Hanafi school upholds its validity by istihsan, overriding a qiyas objection that would nullify it due to uncertainty. This lesson unpacks the conditions for mufawadah and the inter-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
List the four types
The text says contractual partnership is of four types: mufawadah, 'inan, partnership of the artisan, and partnership of faces. Memorize these.
Only mufawadah is detailed here.
2
Identify mufawadah's defining features
Mufawadah means equality (from 'fawd'). It requires equality in capital, transactions, and debts from start to end. Each partner delegates fully to the other.
Equality must be in what can be subject to partnership.
3
Reconstruct the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi rely on the hadith 'Fawidu fa innahu a'zam li al-barakah' and the continuous practice of people. This proof overrides the qiyas objection.
The hadith's chain is weak but supported by practice.
4
Analyze the opposing qiyas
The Shafi'i qiyas argues that mufawadah includes agency for an unknown genus and guarantee for unknown debts. Each is invalid alone, so the combination is invalid.
The uncertainty (jahalah) is considered excessive.
5
Explain istihsan
Hanafis argue that istihsan (juristic preference) overrides qiyas due to the hadith and practice. The jahalah is tolerated as subsidiary, similar to mudarabah.
Istihsan is a core Hanafi tool.

Source Text

كِتَابُ الشِّرْكَةِ
الشَّرْكَةُ جَائِزَةٌ لأَنَّهُ بُعِثَ وَالنَّاسُ يَتَعَامَلُونَ بِهَا فَقَرَّرَهُمْ عَلَيْهِ. قَالَ الشَّرْكَةُ ضَرْبَانِ: شِرْكَةُ أَمْلَاكٍ وَشِرْكَةُ عُقُودٍ. فَشِرْكَةُ الْأَمْلَاكِ الْعَيْنُ يَرِثُهَا رَجُلَانِ أَوْ يَشْتَرِيَانِهَا فَلَا يَجُوزُ لِأَحَدِهِمَا أَنْ يَتَصَرَّفَ فِي نَصِيبِ الْآخَرِ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ وَكُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا فِي نَصِيبِ صَاحِبِهِ كَالْأَجْنَبِيِّ. وَهَذِهِ الشِّرْكَةُ تَتَحَقَّقُ فِي غَيْرِ الْمَذْكُورِ فِي الْكِتَابِ كَمَا إِذَا اتَّهِبَ رَجُلَانِ عَيْنًا أَوْ مَلَكَاهَا بِالِاسْتِيلَاءِ أَوِ اخْتَلَطَ مَالُهُمَا مِنْ غَيْرِ قَصْدِ أَحَدِهِمَا أَوْ بِخَلْطِهِمَا خَلْطًا لاَ يَتَمَيَّزُ رَأْسًا أَوْ إِلَّا بِحَرَجٍ. وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ أَحَدِهِمَا نَصِيبَهُ مِنْ شَرِيكِهِ فِي جَمِيعِ الصُّوَرِ وَمِنْ غَيْرِ شَرِيكِهِ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِهِ إِلَّا فِي صُورَةِ الْخَلْطِ وَالِاخْتِلَاطِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ.

وَالضَّرْبُ الثَّانِي شِرْكَةُ الْعُقُودِ وَرُكْنُهَا الْإِيجَابُ وَالْقَبُولُ وَهُوَ أَنْ يَقُولَ أَحَدُهُمَا شَارَكْتُكَ فِي كَذَا وَكَذَا وَيَقُولُ الْآخَرُ قَبِلْتُ. وَشَرْطُهُ أَنْ يَكُونَ التَّصَرُّفُ الْمَعْقُودُ عَلَيْهِ عَقْدَ الشَّرِكَةِ قَابِلًا لِلْوَكَالَةِ لِيَكُونَ مَا يُسْتَفَادُ بِالتَّصَرُّفِ مُشْتَرَكًا بَيْنَهُمَا فَيَتَحَقَّقَ حُكْمُهُ الْمَطْلُوبُ مِنْهُ.

ثُمَّ هِيَ أَرْبَعَةُ أَوْجُهٍ: مُفَاوَضَةٌ وَعِنَانٌ وَشِرْكَةُ الصَّانِعِ وَشِرْكَةُ الْوُجُوهِ. فَأَمَّا شِرْكَةُ الْمُفَاوَضَةِ فَهِيَ أَنْ يَشْتَرِكَ الرَّجُلَانِ فَيَتَسَاوَيَا فِي مَالِهِمَا وَتَصَرُّفِهِمَا وَدَيْنِهِمَا لِأَنَّهَا شِرْكَةٌ عَامَّةٌ فِي جَمِيعِ التِّجَارَاتِ يُفَوِّضُ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا أَمْرَ الشَّرِكَةِ إِلَى صَاحِبِهِ عَلَى الْإِطْلَاقِ إِذْ هِيَ مِنَ الْمُسَاوَاةِ. قَالَ قَائِلُهُمْ شِعْرًا: لَا يَصْلُحُ النَّاسُ فَوْضَى لَا سَرَاةَ لَهُمْ وَلَا سَرَاةَ إِذَا جُهَّالُهُمْ سَادُوا أَيْ مُتَسَاوِينَ. فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ تَحْقِيقِ الْمُسَاوَاةِ ابْتِدَاءً وَانْتِهَاءً وَذَلِكَ فِي الْمَالِ وَالْمُرَادُ بِهِ مَا تَصِحُّ الشَّرِكَةُ فِيهِ وَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ التَّفَاضُلُ فِيمَا لَا يَصِحُّ الشَّرِكَةُ فِيهِ. وَكَذَا فِي التَّصَرُّفِ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ مَلَكَ أَحَدُهُمَا تَصَرُّفًا لَا يَمْلِكُهُ الْآخَرُ لَفَاتَتِ الْمُسَاوَاةُ. وَكَذَلِكَ فِي الدَّيْنِ لِمَا نُبَيِّنُ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ تَعَالَى. وَهَذِهِ الشَّرْكَةُ جَائِزَةٌ عِنْدَنَا اسْتِحْسَانًا وَفِي الْقِيَاسِ لَا يَجُوزُ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ وَقَالَ مَالِكٌ: لَا أَعْرِفُ مَا الْمُفَاوَضَةُ. وَجْهُ الْقِيَاسِ أَنَّهَا تَضَمَّنَتِ الْوَكَالَةَ بِمَجْهُولِ الْجِنْسِ وَالْكَفَالَةَ بِمَجْهُولٍ وَكُلُّ ذَلِكَ بِالْفِرَادَةِ فَاسِدٌ. وَوَجْهُ الِاسْتِحْسَانِ قَوْلُهُ ﷺ: «فَاوِضُوا فَإِنَّهُ أَعْظَمُ لِلْبَرَكَةِ» وَكَذَا النَّاسُ يَتَعَامَلُونَ بِهَا مِنْ غَيْرِ نَكِيرٍ وَبِهِ يُتْرَكُ الْقِيَاسُ وَالْجَهَالَةُ مُتَحَمَّلَةٌ تَبَعًا كَمَا فِي الْمُضَارَبَةِ. وَلَا تَنْعَقِدُ إِلَّا بِلَفْظَةِ الْمُفَاوَضَةِ لِبُعْدِ شَرَائِطِهَا عَنْ عِلْمِ الْعَوَامِّ حَتَّى لَوْ بَيَّنَا جَمِيعَ مَا يَقْتَضِيهِ يَجُوزُ لِأَنَّ الْمُعْتَبَرَ هُوَ الْمَعْنَى.
Book of Partnership. Partnership is permissible because he (the Prophet) was sent while people were transacting with it, and he confirmed them upon it. He said: Partnership is of two types: partnership in property and partnership by contract. Partnership in property is when a specific asset is inherited by two men or they purchase it. Then it is not permissible for one of them to dispose of the other's share without his permission, and each of them with respect to the other's share is like a stranger. And this partnership materializes in other than what is mentioned in the book, such as when two men are given a specific asset as a gift, or they take possession of it by force, or their wealth mixes without intention of either, or by their mixing in a way that it cannot be distinguished at all or only with difficulty. And it is permissible for one of them to sell his share to his partner in all forms, and to a non-partner without his permission except in the case of mixing and blending – then it is not permissible except with his permission.

The second type is contractual partnership. Its pillar is offer and acceptance, which is that one of them says 'I make you a partner in such-and-such' and the other says 'I accept.' Its condition is that the transaction upon which the partnership contract is based must be capable of being delegated, so that what is gained by the transaction is shared between them, thereby achieving its intended ruling.

Then it is of four types: mufawadah, inan, partnership of the artisan, and partnership of faces. As for mufawadah partnership, it is that two men enter a partnership and become equal in their capital, their transactions, and their debts, because it is a general partnership in all types of trade; each of them delegates the affair of the partnership to his partner absolutely, since it is derived from equality. One of their poets said: 'People are not fit when they are levelled – they have no leaders; and there is no leadership when their ignorant ones become leaders' – meaning equals. So equality must be realized from beginning to end. And that is in capital – meaning what partnership is valid in, and disparity is not considered in what partnership is not valid in. Similarly in transactions, because if one of them possessed a transaction that the other does not, equality would be lost. Similarly in debts, as we will explain if Allah wills. This partnership is permissible in our school by istihsan, and by qiyas it is not permissible – that is the saying of al-Shafi'i. Malik said: I do not know what mufawadah is. The basis of qiyas is that it includes agency for an unknown genus and guarantee for an unknown thing, and each individually is invalid. The basis of istihsan is his statement ﷺ: 'Enter into mufawadah for it is greater in blessing'; likewise people transact with it without disapproval, and thus qiyas is abandoned; the ignorance is tolerated as a subsidiary matter, as in mudarabah. It is not contracted except with the word mufawadah, because of the remoteness of its conditions from the knowledge of the common people; but if we explained all that it requires, it is valid – because the consideration is the meaning.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah opens the Book of Partnership. The author first states the ruling: partnership is permissible (ja'izah). The proof is the prophetic tacit approval (taqrir) – the Prophet ﷺ saw people practicing it and did not prohibit it, thus establishing its permissibility. Then the text defines two primary categories: Shirkat al-Amwal (partnership in property) and Shirkat al-Uqud (contractual partnership). Shirkat al-Amwal arises from joint ownership, such as inheritance or joint purchase. In such ownership, each partner is like a stranger regarding the other's share – no disposal without permission. This type also includes cases of mixing (ikhtilat) that are inseparable. The text details when selling one's share is allowed. Then comes Shirkat al-Uqud, which is based on offer and acceptance. Its condition is that the underlying transaction be amenable to agency (wakalah), so profits from dealings are shared. The author then lists the four types of contractual partnership: mufawadah, 'inan, partnership of artisans (sana'i'), and partnership of faces (wujuh). He elaborates on mufawadah, defining it as a general, equal partnership in capital, transactions, and debts – derived from the root 'fawaḍ' meaning equality. The text cites a proverb: society requires leaders, not pure equality – but in partnership, equality is stipulated. The Hanafi position is that mufawadah is valid by istihsan (juristic preference), even though qiyas (analogy) would invalidate it due to uncertainty in agency and guarantee. Imam al-Shafi'i rejects it on qiyas; Imam Malik professes ignorance. The Hanafi response cites a hadith (though with weak chain) and the practice of people; the uncertainty is tolerated as incidental, like in mudarabah. Conditions: it must be expressly worded 'mufawadah'; if the parties explain all conditions, it can be valid without the exact term.

Key Terms
مُفَاوَضَةٌ (mufawadah): A general, equal partnership in capital, trade, and debts; each partner delegates fully.
عِنَانٌ (inan): A limited partnership where partners may contribute unequally and trade in specific goods.
شِرْكَةُ الصَّانِعِ (shirkat al-sani): Partnership of artisans where each contributes skill and shares profits.
شِرْكَةُ الْوُجُوهِ (shirkat al-wujuh): Partnership based on creditworthiness without capital; profits from buying and selling on credit.
اسْتِحْسَانٌ (istihsan): Juristic preference over qiyas due to a stronger evidence (hadith, practice, necessity).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is mufawadah valid despite containing unknown elements?
A) Because it is a general practice
B) Because the unknowns are tolerated as subsidiary
C) Because it is analogous to mudarabah
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Mufawadah is a valid equal partnership by istihsan; its conditions of equality must be strictly observed.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate
10 min
Shirkat al-Mufawadah: Definition, Conditions, and Istihsan Ruling
Definition, conditions, and istihsan ruling of Shirkat al-Mufawadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Shirkat al-Mufawadah, state its three conditions (equality in capital, disposition, and debt), and explain why the Hanafi school validates it by istihsan despite the qiyas objection.

Core Idea
Shirkat al-Mufawadah is valid by istihsan: full delegation, equality in three realms, and ancillary ignorance tolerated.

In the Hanafi fiqh of partnerships, Shirkat al-Mufawadah is a unique contract where partners delegate full authority to each other and must be perfectly equal. This lesson unpacks its definition from Al-Hidayah, details the strict conditions of equality, and then examines why the Hanafi school upholds its validity through istihsan despite strong qiyas arguments against it. Understanding this ruling reveals how the Hanafi school uses custom and public interest to override strict analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the broader category
Recognize that Shirkat al-Mufawadah is one of four types of Shirkat al-Uqud (contractual partnerships). Understand that the pillar of any contractual partnership is offer and acceptance, and the condition is that the subject matter be capable of delegation.
This contextualizes Mufawadah within the fiqh of shirkah.
2
Define Mufawadah and its core conditions
From the text, Mufawadah is defined as a general partnership where partners must be equal in three areas: capital (mal), power of disposition (tasarruf), and debt liability (dayn). The term itself implies equality and delegation.
Equality must exist at the inception and throughout the partnership.
3
State the Hanafi ruling and its basis
The text states: 'This partnership is valid in our school by istihsan.' The default qiyas would render it invalid, but istihsan overrides due to a hadith and continuous practice.
The ruling is mufta bihi despite cross-madhhab disagreement.
4
Analyze the qiyas objection
The qiyas argument (attributed to al-Shafi'i) is that Mufawadah includes agency for an unknown type and suretyship for an unknown amount, each invalid individually. The text explains this objection clearly.
This is the central counter-proof.
5
Understand the istihsan justification
The istihsan relies on: (1) a hadith (though weak) commanding Mufawadah for blessing, (2) continuous practice of Muslims without disapproval, and (3) tolerance of ancillary ignorance, analogous to Mudarabah.
Also, the contract only requires the word 'Mufawadah' unless details are explained; meaning prevails over wording.

ترجمة والضرب الثاني الخ اور شرکت کی دوسری قسم شرکتہ العقود ہے۔ امینی عقد و معاملہ کر کے آپس میں ایک سے زائد آدمیوں : شرکت کرنا اس کا رکن ایجاب اور قبول ہے۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص یوں کہے کہ میں نے تم سے فلاں فلاں چیز میں شرکت کی اور دوسرا یوں کہے کہ میں نے یہ شرکت قبول کی۔ اس کی شرط یہ ہے کہ جس معاملہ اور تصرف میں اس شرکت کے معاملہ کو قبول کیا ہو وہ وکالت کے قابل ہوتا کہ اس میں تصرف اور الٹ پھیر سے جو کچھ حاصل ہو وہ ان دونوں میں مشترک ہو ۔ اس طرح عقد شرکت کرنے کا جو مقصد ہوتا ہے و متحقق ہو جائے۔
شرکت عقود کی اقسام اربعہ
ثُمَّ هِيَ أَرْبَعَةُ أَوْجُةٍ مُفَاوَضَةً وَعَنَانٌ وَشِرْكَةُ الصَّائِعِ وَشِرَكَةُ الْوُجُوهِ فَأَمَّا شِرْكَةُ الْمُفَاَوَضَةِ . ـرَكَةَ الْمُفَاوَضَةِ فَهيَ أَنْ يَشْتَرِكَ الرَّجُلَانِ فَيَتَسَاوَيَا فِى مَالِهَا وَ تَصَرُّفِهِمَا وَدَيْنِهِمَا لِأَنَّهَا شِرْكَةً عَامَّةُ فِى جَمِيعِ التِّجَارَاتِ يُفَوِّضُ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِّنْهَا أَمْرَ الشَّرُكَةِ إِلى صَاحِبِهِ عَلَى الْإِطْلَاقِ إِذْهِيَ مِنَ الْمُسَاوَاةِ قَالَ قَائِلُهُمْ شِعْر لَا يَصْلَحُ النَّاسُ فَوَضًا لا سَرَاةَ لَهُم وَلَاسَرَاةَ إِذْ جَهَالَهُمْ سَادُوا أَى مُتَسَاوِبِيْنَ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ تَحْقِيقِ الْمَسَاوَاةِ ابْتِدَاء وَانْتِهَاء وَذَالِكَ فِى الْمَالِ وَالْمُرَادُ بِهِ مَا تَصِحَ الشَّرُكَةُ فِيهِ وَلَا يُعتبرُ التَّفَاضُلُ فِيْمَا لَا يَصِحُ الشَّرُكَةُ فِيهِ وَكَذَا فِي التَّصَرُّفِ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ مَلَكَ أَحَدُهُمَا تَصَرُّفَ لَا يَمْلِكُهُ الْآخَرُ لَفَاتَ السَّسَاوِى وَكَذَالِكَ فِي الدَّيْنِ لِمَانُبَيِّنُ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَهَذِهِ الشَّرَكَةُ جَائِزَةٌ عِنْدَنَا اِسْتِحْسَانًا وَفِي الْقِيَاسِ لَا يَجُوزُ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الشَّافِعِي وَقَالَ مَالِكَ لَا أَعْرِفُ مَا الْمُفَاوَضَةُ وَجُهُ الْقِيَاسِ أَنَّهَـ
تَضَمَّنَتِ الْوَكَالَةَ بِمَجْهُولِ الْجِنْسِ وَالْكَفَالَةَ بِمَجْهُولٍ وَكُلُّ ذَالِکَ بِالْفِرَادِهِ فَاسِدوَجَّهُ الْاِسْتِحْسَانِ قَوْله فاوضوا فَإِنَّهُ أَعْظَمُ لِلبَرَكَةِ وَكَذَا النَّاسُ يُعَامِلُوْنَهَا مِنْ غَيْرِ نَكِيرِ وَبِ، يُشْرَكَ الْقِيَاسُ وَالْجَهَالَةَ مُتَحَمَّلَةٌ تَبْعًا كما فِى الْمُضَارَبَةِ وَ لَا تَنْعَقِدُ إِلَّا بِلَفْظَةِ الْمُفَاوَضَةِ لِبَعْدِ شَرائِطِهَا عَنْ عِلْمِ الْعَوَامِ حَتى لو بينا جَمِيعَ ما يَقْتَضِيهِ يَجُوزُ لِأَنَّ الْمُعْتَبَرَ هُوَ الْمَعْنى
ترجمہ پھر اس شرکت عقود کی چار قسمیں ہیں
(۱) اول شرکت مفاوضہ
(۳) سوم شرکت صنائع
(۲) دوم شرکت عنان
(۴ چهارم شرکت وجود
شرکت مفاوضہ کی صورت یہ ہوتی ہے کہ دو یا اس سے زائد آدمی آپس میں شرکت کے معاملہ کو قبول کریں اس طرح سے کہ ان میں یہ کہ یا مال اور معاملہ و تصرف کرنے میں سب برابر ہوں۔ کیونکہ یہ شرکت تجارت کی تمام صورتوں میں عام ہوتی ہے۔ اس طرح سے کہ ان شرکا ، میں سے ہر ایک شریک اپنے شریکوں کو پورا پورا اختیار حوالہ کر دیتا ہے۔ کیونکہ لفظ مفاوضہ مساوات کے معنی میں ہے ۔ چنانچہ کسی عربی شاعر ( الاقوه الا دوی) نے کہا ہے ۔ شعر کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ جب لوگ بالکل برابر اور ایک مرتبہ کے ہو جائیں اور ان میں کوئی بڑا سردار نہ رہے اور سرداری نہیں رہ سکتی ہے جبکہ اس قوم کے جاہل سردار بنا دئیے جائیں تو ان میں فتنہ وفساد بر پا رہے گا۔ پس شرکت مفاوضہ کی ابتداء وانتہاء میں مساوات ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اور یہ بات مال میں ثابت ہو گی۔ مال سے وہ مال مراد ہے جس میں شرکت صحیح ہو۔ اسی لئے جس مال میں شرکت صحیح نہیں ہوتی ہو اس میں ان کے آپس میں کمی و بیشی کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح معاملات میں تصرف کرنے کے اختیار میں بھی برابری کا حق ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ ان میں سے اگر کسی ایک کو ایسے تعریف کا اختیار ہو جو دوسرے شریک کو نہ ہو تو اس میں برابری باقی نہیں رہے گی ۔ اسی طرح قرض کے لین دین میں بھی مساوات شرط ہے۔ چنانچہ ہم اس کی دلیل انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ آئندہ بیان کریں گے۔ یہ شرکت ہمارے نزدیک بدلیل استحسان جائز ہے۔ اور قیاسا جائز نہیں دونوں موجود ہے جبکہ ایسی وکالت اور کفالت میں سے ہر ایک تنہا ہی فاسد ہوتی ہے۔ اور استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں مذکور ہے کہ تم لوگ مفاوضہ کرو ۔ کہ اس میں بڑی برکت ہے ) لیکن یہ حدیث نہیں ملی ہے بلکہ ابن ماجہ کی ایک حدیث میں ہے کہ تین چیزوں میں برکت ہے (۱) ادھار بیچنے میں لیکن وہ جس کی میعاد معلوم ہو اور (۲) مفاوضہ میں اور (۳) گھر کے خرچ کے لئے گیہوا ، کو جو کے ساتھ ملانے میں ۔ مگربیع کے لئے نہیں اور استحسان کی یہ بھی وجہ ہے کہ مفاوضہ کا معاملہ لوگوں میں بلا روک ٹوک کے جاری تھا۔ اور ایسے معاملات سے جو اتنے زیادہ پیمانہ کے ساتھ ہوئے ہوں قیاس چھوڑ دیا جاتا ہے۔ اور وکالت و کفالت میں جو جہالت ہے وہ تابع کر کے برداشت ہو سکتی ہے۔ جیسے مضاربت میں جائز ہے۔ واضح ہو کہ یہ شرکت سوائے لفظ مفاوضہ کے کسی دوسرے لفظ سے منعقد نہیں ہوتی ہے کیونکہ عوام کے سامنے اس کے صحیح مفہوم اور شرائط کو سمجھانا اور ان کا سمجھنا مشکل ہے۔ پھر بھی اگر اس کی شرطوں اور دوسری ضروری باتوں کو دوسری عبارتوں سے بیان کر دیا جائے تو شرکت معاوضہ مسیح ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اصل اعتبار معنی کا ہوتا ہے الفاظ کانہیں ہوتا ہے۔
Translation: And the second type... and the second type of partnership is Shirkat al-Uqud (contractual partnership). People enter into a contract and transaction among themselves, more than one person partnering. Its pillar is offer and acceptance. Its form is that one person says, 'I have entered into partnership with you in such and such thing,' and the other says, 'I have accepted this partnership.' Its condition is that the transaction and disposition in which this partnership is accepted must be such as can be validly delegated, so that whatever profit is obtained through disposition and exchange is shared between them. In this way, the objective of concluding the partnership contract is achieved. Then it (Shirkat al-Uqud) is of four types: Mufawadah, 'Inan, partnership of artisans (Sanai'), and partnership of credit (Wujuh). As for Shirkat al-Mufawadah, it is that two men enter into partnership such that they are equal in their capital, their power of disposition, and their debt liability, because it is a general partnership in all types of trade; each one of them delegates the matter of the partnership to his partner absolutely, since it (the term) is derived from equality. A poet said: 'People who are equal (fuwada) do not prosper without leaders, and there is no leadership when their ignorant ones become leaders' – meaning equal. Therefore, equality must be realized from beginning to end, and that is in capital. By capital is meant that in which partnership is valid; disparity is not considered in that in which partnership is not valid. Similarly in disposition, because if one of them possesses a power of disposition that the other does not, equality is lost. Likewise in debt, as we will explain, God willing. This partnership is valid in our school by istihsan, but by qiyas it is not valid. This is the view of al-Shafi'i. Malik said, 'I do not know what Mufawadah is.' The basis of qiyas is that it includes agency for an unknown type and suretyship for an unknown amount, each of which individually is invalid. The basis of istihsan is the saying 'Engage in Mufawadah, for it is greater in blessing.' Also, people practice it without disapproval, so qiyas is abandoned. The ignorance (of details) is tolerated as ancillary, just as in Mudarabah. It is only concluded with the word 'Mufawadah' because its conditions are beyond the knowledge of common people, but if they explain all that it entails, it is valid, because the consideration is the meaning, not the words. Urdu commentary: Then the four types of Shirkat al-Uqud: (1) Mufawadah, (2) 'Inan, (3) Sanai', (4) Wujuh. The form of Mufawadah is that two or more people accept the partnership contract such that they are equal in capital, transaction, and disposition. Because this partnership is general in all forms of trade, each partner delegates full authority to the other. The word Mufawadah means equality. A certain Arab poet said: ... (meaning of poem) ... So equality is necessary at the beginning and end. This applies in property, meaning property in which partnership is valid. For property in which partnership is not valid, their disparity is not considered. Similarly, in the authority to transact, equality is required; if one has authority the other does not, equality is lost. Similarly in debt transactions. We will give evidence later, God willing. This partnership is valid in our school by istihsan, not by qiyas. Imam Shafi'i holds this view. Imam Malik said he does not know what Mufawadah is. The qiyas argument: it contains agency for unknown type and suretyship for unknown, each invalid alone. The istihsan argument: a hadith says 'Engage in Mufawadah, for it has great blessing.' (But this hadith is not found; however, Ibn Majah has a hadith that blessing is in three things: credit sale with known term, Mufawadah, and mixing wheat with barley for household use, not for sale.) Also, people have always practiced it without objection, so qiyas is abandoned. The ignorance in agency and suretyship is tolerated as ancillary, like in Mudarabah. This partnership only contracts with the word 'Mufawadah' because the common people are unaware of its exact conditions; but if all its requirements are explained, it is valid because the meaning is what counts.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is from the beginning of Kitab al-Shirkah in Ashraf al-Hidayah, an Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah. It first explains the second type of partnership, Shirkat al-Uqud, which is a contractual partnership formed by offer and acceptance. The pillar (rukn) is the offer and acceptance, and the condition is that the subject matter be capable of delegation so that profits are shared. Then it introduces the four types of Shirkat al-Uqud: Mufawadah, 'Inan, Sanai' (artisans), and Wujuh (credit). The focus then shifts to Shirkat al-Mufawadah. The definition is given: two partners must be equal in three areas: capital (mal), power of disposition (tasarruf), and debt (dayn). The term 'Mufawadah' is derived from equality (musawah), and a line of poetry is cited to illustrate that equality is essential. The conditions are detailed: equality in capital means the contributed capital must be of a type in which partnership is valid (e.g., currency, goods). If one contributes something that cannot form a valid partnership (like services), inequality is overlooked. Equality in disposition means each partner must have identical legal capacity to transact; if one is a slave or minor, equality is lost. Equality in debt liability will be explained later. The ruling is that this partnership is valid (ja'izah) by istihsan in the Hanafi school, but invalid by qiyas. Al-Shafi'i holds it invalid by qiyas, while Malik dismisses it as unknown. The qiyas argument is that Mufawadah combines agency (wakalah) for an unknown type of transaction and suretyship (kafalah) for an unknown amount, each of which is individually invalid. The istihsan argument relies on a hadith (though its authenticity is questioned) commanding Mufawadah for blessing, and on the continuous practice of the people without disapproval. The ignorance in the details of agency and suretyship is tolerated because it is ancillary, similar to the toleration of ignorance in Mudarabah. Finally, the contract is only concluded with the word 'Mufawadah' unless the parties explicitly state all conditions, in which case the meaning governs over the term.

Key Terms
شركة المفاوضة (Shirkat al-Mufawadah): A partnership between two or more persons where they are equal in capital, power of disposition, and debt liability, with full delegation of authority.
استحسان (Istihsan): A legal method preferring a ruling based on equity, public interest, or custom over strict qiyas.
مفاوضة (Mufawadah): Derived from tafwid (delegation) and musawah (equality); the contract requires delegation and equality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the three areas in which partners must be equal in Shirkat al-Mufawadah?
A) Capital, profit, and liability
B) Capital, power of disposition, and debt
C) Capital, labor, and credit
D) Power of disposition, credit, and profit

Key Takeaway
Shirkat al-Mufawadah is a unique Hanafi institution validated by istihsan; it requires equality in capital, disposition, and debt, and tolerates ancillary ignorance.

Shirkah — Partnership
beginner
6 min
Conditions for Valid Shirkat al-Mufawadah: Between Whom
States the parties between whom Mufawadah is valid or invalid based on equality of legal capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid and invalid party pairings for Shirkat al-Mufawadah and explain the condition of equality of legal capacity.

Core Idea
Mufawadah requires equal legal capacity; only free, adult Muslims or dhimmis qualify; slaves and minors do not.

Shirkat al-Mufawadah is a full partnership where each partner has unlimited authority and suretyship. Therefore, equality in legal capacity is essential. This lesson identifies who can form such a partnership according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the valid pairs
List the combinations explicitly stated as valid: two free adult Muslims, two dhimmis, or a Kitabi and a Majusi.
The text also mentions equality (musawah) as the reason.
2
Identify the invalid pairs
List the invalid combinations: free with slave, adult with minor.
Even if permission is given, it is invalid because inherent capacity differs.
3
Understand the reasoning
Equality requires both parties to have independent tasarruf (disposition) and the ability to give kafalah (suretyship). Slaves and minors lack one or both.
Non-Muslims are considered equal in capacity for financial contracts.
4
Apply to a new scenario
Given a pair, determine if Mufawadah is valid based on the conditions.
Check freedom, adulthood, and legal capacity for suretyship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَيَجُوزُ بَيْنَ الْحُرَيْنِ الْكَبِيرَيْنِ مُسْلِمَيْنِ أَوْ دَمِيْنِ لِتَحَقِّقِ التَّسَاوِى وَإِنْ كَانَ أَحَدُهُمَا كِتَابِيًّا وَالْآخَرُ مَجُوسِيًّا يَجُوزُ أَيْضًا لِمَا قُلْنَا
ترجمه ( قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ ) یہ عقد معاملہ ایسے دو مردوں میں جائز ہوگا کہ دونوں آزاد بالغ مسلمان یا ذمی ہوں کیونکہ دونوں میں برابری ثابت ہے۔ اور اگر دونوں میں سے ایک کتابی اور دوسرا مجوسی ہو تو بھی جائز ہوگا ۔کیونکہ سارے کفار ایک ہی ملت پر رہنے کی وجہ سے دونوں میں برابری ثابت ہوگی۔
شرکت مفاوضہ کن کے درمیان صحیح نہیں
وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْنَ الْحُرِّ وَالْمَمْلُوكِ وَ لَا بَيْنَ الصّبرِ وَالْبَالِغ لِأَنْعِدَامِ الْمُسَاوَاةِ لِأَنَّ الْحُرَّ الْبَالِغَ يَمْلِكُ التَّصَرُّفَ وَالْكَفَالَةِ وَالْمَمْلُوكُ لَا يَمْلِكَ وَاحِدَ امِنها إِلا بِإِذْنِ الْمَوْلى وَالصَّبِيُّ لَا يَمْلِكُ الْكَفَالَةَ وَلَا يَمْلِكُ التَّصَرُّفَ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ الْوَلِي
ترجمہ اور آزاد اور غلام اور بالغ و نابالغ کے درمیان مفاوضہ جائز نہیں ہے ۔ کیونکہ ان میں مساوات نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ آزاد بالغ کو تصرف اور کفالت کا اختیار ہوتا ہے۔ اور غلام کو ان دونوں باتوں میں سے ایک کا بھی اختیار نہیں ہوتا ہے جب تک کہ مولی اجازت نہ
He (al-Quduri) said: It is valid between two free, adult men, both Muslims or dhimmis, because equality is realized. If one of them is a Kitabi (Scriptuary) and the other a Majusi (Zoroastrian), it is also valid for what we said. Urdu commentary: This contract will be valid between two men who are free, adult, Muslim or dhimmi, because equality is established between them. If one is Kitabi and the other Majusi, it is also valid, because all non-Muslims are on one millah, so equality is established. Between whom Mufawadah is not valid: It is not valid between a free person and a slave, nor between a child and an adult, due to lack of equality. Because a free adult possesses the power of disposition and suretyship, whereas a slave does not possess either except with the master's permission. A child does not possess suretyship and does not possess disposition except with the guardian's permission. Urdu commentary: Mufawadah between free and slave, and between adult and minor, is not valid because equality is absent. A free adult has authority to transact and give surety; a slave has neither unless permitted by his master; a child has no surety and no disposition except with guardian's permission.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage specifies the conditions of the parties for a valid Shirkat al-Mufawadah. The matn (al-Quduri's text) states it is valid between two free, adult, Muslim or dhimmi men. The equality required is in legal capacity: both must be fully competent to transact and to give surety, because Mufawadah entails delegation of full authority and mutual suretyship. If one is a Kitabi and the other a Majusi, it is still valid because all non-Muslims are considered of one 'millah' (religious community) for the purpose of legal capacity in financial matters; they are equally capable of giving surety. The passage then lists invalid combinations: free with slave, and adult with minor. A slave lacks independent authority to transact or give surety; he is dependent on his master. A minor lacks full capacity for suretyship and disposition without a guardian. Hence, equality is absent, and Mufawadah cannot be formed. The underlying principle is 'tahqiq al-musawah' (realization of equality). This lesson is a memorization anchor for the conditions of the parties.

Key Terms
ذمي (Dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject of an Islamic state who enjoys protection and pays jizya.
مجوسي (Majusi): A Zoroastrian; considered ahl al-kitab by some Hanafi opinions for legal purposes.
كفالة (Kafalah): Suretyship; a contract guaranteeing a debt or obligation of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Mufawadah between which of the following is valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) A free adult Muslim and a free adult dhimmi
B) A free adult and a slave
C) An adult and a minor
D) A Muslim and a non-Muslim without dhimmi status

Key Takeaway
Mufawadah is only valid when both parties are free, adult, and possess full legal capacity for disposition and suretyship, ensuring true equality.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for Valid Mufawadah Partnership and the Hanafi Proof
Defining Mufawadah and its conditions of validity with proofs and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid mufawadah partnership, explain the Hanafi proof of istihsan that overrides qiyas, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding Muslim-dhimmi mufawadah.

Core Idea
Mufawadah is valid by istihsan despite jahalah, requiring equality in legal capacity, not just capital.

This lesson examines the unique Hanafi contract of Shirkat al-Mufawadah, an equal partnership where partners are each other's agents and sureties. The text from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the strict conditions—free, adult, Muslim—and explains why the Hanafi school accepts it by istihsan while other schools reject it by qiyas. A key intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on Muslim-dhimmi partnership highlights the centrality of equal transaction capacity.

Guided Path
1
Define Mufawadah and its core requirements
Identify the three elements of mufawadah: equal capital, equal authority in transactions, and mutual kafalah. Note that it is a distinct partnership type requiring complete equality.
2
Analyze the proof structure: qiyas vs istihsan
Understand that qiyas would invalidate mufawadah due to jahalah in wakalah and kafalah, but istihsan overrides based on widespread practice ('urf) and the hadith of Ibn Majah on three blessings.
The hadith is from Sunan Ibn Majah.
3
List the conditions for validity
From the text: both partners must be free, adult (baligh), and Muslim or dhimmi (or Kitabi and Majusi together). Equality in tasarruf and kafalah is essential.
The contract must use the word 'mufawadah' or clearly express its meaning.
4
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on Muslim-dhimmi
Compare Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (invalid due to unequal transaction capacity) with Abu Yusuf (valid but makruh, arguing equality in wakalah/kafalah suffices). Determine the mufta bihi position.
The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہی میں شرکت صحیح نہیں ہوتی ہو اس میں ان کے آپس میں کمی و بیشی کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح معاملات میں تصرف کرنے کے اختیار میں بھی برابری کا حق ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ ان میں سے اگر کسی ایک کو ایسے تعریف کا اختیار ہو جو دوسرے شریک کو نہ ہو تو اس میں برابری باقی نہیں رہے گی ۔ اسی طرح قرض کے لین دین میں بھی مساوات شرط ہے۔ چنانچہ ہم اس کی دلیل انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ آئندہ بیان کریں گے۔ یہ شرکت ہمارے نزدیک بدلیل استحسان جائز ہے۔ اور قیاسا جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا یہی قول ہے۔ امام مالک رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ میں نہیں جانتا ہوں کہ مفاوضہ کیا چیز ہے۔ قیاس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس میں مجہول جنس کی وکالت اور مجہول کی کفالت دونوں موجود ہے جبکہ ایسی وکالت اور کفالت میں سے ہر ایک تنہا ہی فاسد ہوتی ہے۔ اور استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں مذکور ہے کہ تم لوگ مفاوضہ کرو ۔ کہ اس میں بڑی برکت ہے ) لیکن یہ حدیث نہیں ملی ہے بلکہ ابن ماجہ کی ایک حدیث میں ہے کہ تین چیزوں میں برکت ہے (۱) ادھار بیچنے میں لیکن وہ جس کی میعاد معلوم ہو اور (۲) مفاوضہ میں اور (۳) گھر کے خرچ کے لئے گیہوا ، کو جو کے ساتھ ملانے میں ۔ مگربیع کے لئے نہیں اور استحسان کی یہ بھی وجہ ہے کہ مفاوضہ کا معاملہ لوگوں میں بلا روک ٹوک کے جاری تھا۔ اور ایسے معاملات سے جو اتنے زیادہ پیمانہ کے ساتھ ہوئے ہوں قیاس چھوڑ دیا جاتا ہے۔ اور وکالت و کفالت میں جو جہالت ہے وہ تابع کر کے برداشت ہو سکتی ہے۔ جیسے مضاربت میں جائز ہے۔ واضح ہو کہ یہ شرکت سوائے لفظ مفاوضہ کے کسی دوسرے لفظ سے منعقد نہیں ہوتی ہے کیونکہ عوام کے سامنے اس کے صحیح مفہوم اور شرائط کو سمجھانا اور ان کا سمجھنا مشکل ہے۔ پھر بھی اگر اس کی شرطوں اور دوسری ضروری باتوں کو دوسری عبارتوں سے بیان کر دیا جائے تو شرکت معاوضہ صحیح ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اصل اعتبار معنی کا ہوتا ہے الفاظ کا نہیں ہوتا ہے۔
شرکت مفاوضہ کن کے درمیان درست ہے
قَالَ فَيَجُوزُ بَيْنَ الْحُرَيْنِ الْكَبِيرَيْنِ مُسْلِمَيْنِ أَوْ دَمِيْنِ لِتَحَقِّقِ التَّسَاوِى وَإِنْ كَانَ أَحَدُهُمَا كِتَابِيًّا وَالْآخَرُ مَجُوسِيًّا يَجُوزُ أَيْضًا لِمَا قُلْنَا
ترجمه ( قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ ) یہ عقد معاملہ ایسے دو مردوں میں جائز ہوگا کہ دونوں آزاد بالغ مسلمان یا ذمی ہوں کیونکہ دونوں میں برابری ثابت ہے۔ اور اگر دونوں میں سے ایک کتابی اور دوسرا مجوسی ہو تو بھی جائز ہوگا ۔کیونکہ سارے کفار ایک ہی ملت پر رہنے کی وجہ سے دونوں میں برابری ثابت ہوگی۔
شرکت مفاوضہ کن کے درمیان صحیح نہیں
وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْنَ الْحُرِّ وَالْمَمْلُوكِ وَ لَا بَيْنَ الصَّبِيِّ وَالْبَالِغ لِأَنْعِدَامِ الْمُسَاوَاةِ لِأَنَّ الْحُرَّ الْبَالِغَ يَمْلِكُ التَّصَرُّفَ وَالْكَفَالَةِ وَالْمَمْلُوكُ لَا يَمْلِكَ وَاحِدَ آمِنها إِلا بِإِذْنِ الْمَوْلى وَالصَّبِيُّ لَا يَمْلِكُ الْكَفَالَةَ وَلَا يَمْلِكُ التَّصَرُّفَ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ الْوَلِي
ترجمہ اور آزاد اور غلام اور بالغ و نابالغ کے درمیان مفاوضہ جائز نہیں ہے ۔ کیونکہ ان میں مساوات نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ آزاد بالغ کو تصرف اور کفالت کا اختیار ہوتا ہے۔ اور غلام کو ان دونوں باتوں میں سے ایک کا بھی اختیار نہیں ہوتا ہے جب تک کہ مولی اجازت نہ دے۔ اسی طرح نابالغ کو بھی ان میں سے کسی کا اختیار نہیں ہوتا ہے جب تک اس کا ولی اجازت نہ دے۔
کافر اور مسلمان کے درمیان شرکت مفاوضہ درست نہیں
قَالَ وَلَا بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِ وَالْكَافِرِ وَهُذَا قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةً وَمُحَمَّدٍ وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ يَجُوزُ لِلسَّسَاوِي بَيْنَهُمَا فِي الْوَكَالَة وَهَدَاقَولُ وَالْكَفَالَةِ وَلَا مُعْتَبَرَ بِزِيَادَةِ تَصَرُّفٍ يَمْلِكُهُ أَحَدُهُمَا كَالْمُفَاوَضَةِ بَيْنَ الشَّفْعَوِي وَالْحَنْفِي فَإِنَّهَا جَائِزَةٌ وَيَتَفَاوَتَانِ فِى التَّصَرُّفِ فِى مَتَرُوكِ التَّسْمِيَّةِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ يُكْرَهُ لأَنَّ الذِي لَا يَهْتَدِى إِلَى الْجَائِزِ مِنَ الْعُقُودِ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ لَا تَسَاوِيَ فِى التَّصَرُّفِ فَإِنَّ الدِّمِّي لَوِ اشْتَرى بِرَأْسِ الْمَالِ حُمُورًا أَوْ خَنَازِيرَ صَحَ وَلَوِ اشْتَرَاهَا مُسْلِمُ لَا يَصِحُ
ترجمہ وَلَا بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِ الخ قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ مسلمان اور کافر کے درمیان بھی مفاوضہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ یہ قول امام ابو حنیفہ ومحمد رحمہما اللہ کا ہے اور ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ وکالت اور کفالت میں دونوں برابر ہیں اور جس زیادہ تصرف کا ایک مالک ہے اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہے جیسے شافعی و حنفی کے درمیان مفاوضہ جائز ہے۔ حالانکہ جانور پر ان کے ذبح کرتے وقت قصد بسم اللہ نہیں کہا گیا ہو اس کے حلال ہونے میں ان دونوں کے درمیان اختلاف ہے کہ شافعی کے نزدیک وہ حلال ہے لیکن حنفی کے نزدیک حلال نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح مسلمان اور کافر کے درمیان بھی جائز ہے لیکن مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ ذمی کومفاوضہ کے معاملات جائز ہونے کے مسائل اور اس کی راہ پورے طور پر معلوم نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اور ابو حنیفہ ومحمد رحمہما اللہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دونوں میں تصرف کرنے میں برابری کا ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر ذمی نے اصل مال ( راس المال) سے سور یا شراب خریدی تو جائز ہے اور اگر مسلمان نے خریدی تو صحیح
نہیں ہے۔
دو غلاموں ، دو بچوں اور دو مکاتبوں کے درمیان شرکت مفاوضہ درست نہیں
وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْنَ الْعَبْدَينِ وَ لَا بَيْنَ الصَّبِيَّيْنِ وَ لَا بَيْنَ الْمُكَاتِبِينِ لِاِنْعِدَامٍ صحةِ الْكَفَالَةِ وَ فِى كُلّ مَوْضِع لَمْ تَصِـ الْمُفَاَوَصَةُ لِفَقْدِشَرطِهَا وَلَا يَشْتَرِطُ ذَالِكَ فِي الْعَنَانِ كَانَ عَنَانًا لِاسْتِجُمَاعِ شَرَائِطِ الْعَنَانِ إِذْهُوَ قَدْ يَكُونَ خا مَّا وَقَدْ يَكُونُ عَامًا
ترجمہ وَلَا يَجُوزُ الخ اور دوغلاموں میں مفاوضہ جائز نہیں ہے اسی طرح دو نا بالغوں میں اور دو مکاتبوں میں بھی جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان کی کفالت صحیح نہیں ہوتی ہے اور واضح ہو کہ جس جگہ شرط کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مفاوضہ صحیح نہ ہواور وہ شرط ایسی ہو کہ شرکت عنان میں اس کی شرط نہ ہو تو وہی شرکت مفاوضہ شرکت عنان ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ شرکت عنان کی سب شرطیں اس وقت پائی جاتی ہیں شرکت عنان کبھی خاص ہوتی ہے ۔ اور کبھی عام ہوتی ہے ۔ جیسے ایک بالغ اور دوسرے نابالغ نے یا ایک آزاد اور دوسرے غلام یا مکاتب نے آپس میں عقد مفاوضہ کیا یا برابر کے دو آزاد آدمیوں نے مفاوضہ کرتے ہوئے یہ شرط لگائی کہ كفالت نہیں ہے تو ہر صورت میں كفالت نہ ہونے سے شرکت عنان ہو جائے گی ۔ اور یہ شرکت عنان عام ہو جائے گی۔ جیسے شرکت مفاوضہ ہمیشہ عام ہوتی ہے۔
Book of Partnership. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume 7. In this, partnership is not valid if there is any inequality between them in increase or decrease. Similarly, in the authority to conduct transactions, equality must exist. Because if one of them has the authority for a certain type of transaction that the other partner does not, then equality is not maintained. Similarly, equality is a condition in lending and borrowing. We will mention its proof later, Allah willing. This partnership is valid by the evidence of istihsan in our view, and not valid by qiyas. Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) holds the same view. Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) said: I do not know what mufawadah is. The evidence of qiyas is that in it there is an unknown type of agency (wakalah) and an unknown type of surety (kafalah), whereas each of these alone is invalid. And the evidence of istihsan is that it is mentioned in a hadith: 'Engage in mufawadah, for there is great blessing in it.' But this hadith is not found; rather, in a hadith of Ibn Majah it is: 'There is blessing in three things: (1) selling on credit with a known term, (2) mufawadah, and (3) mixing wheat with barley for household expenses, not for sale.' Another reason for istihsan is that the practice of mufawadah continued among people without prohibition, and qiyas is abandoned in matters that have been widely practiced. And the ignorance (jahalah) in agency and surety can be tolerated as subsidiary, just as it is permitted in mudarabah. It is clear that this partnership is only contracted with the word 'mufawadah' and not with any other word, because explaining its correct meaning and conditions to the common people and their understanding it is difficult. However, if its conditions and other necessary matters are explained with other expressions, then the mufawadah partnership becomes valid, because the primary consideration is meaning, not words.

"Between whom is mufawadah valid?"
He (al-Quduri) said: It is valid between two free, mature men, both Muslim or both dhimmi, because equality is established. If one of them is a Kitabi and the other a Majusi, it is also valid for what we have said.
Translation: (al-Quduri said:) This transaction is valid between such two men, both free, adult, Muslim or dhimmi, because equality is established between them. And if one of them is a Kitabi and the other a Majusi, it is also valid, because all disbelievers are on one religion, so equality is established between them.

"Between whom is mufawadah not valid?"
And it is not valid between a free person and a slave, nor between a minor and an adult, because equality is absent. Because a free adult has the authority to transact and to give surety, while a slave does not possess either of these unless with the master's permission, and a minor does not possess the ability to give surety nor the authority to transact unless with the guardian's permission.
Translation: And mufawadah is not valid between a free person and a slave, nor between an adult and a minor, because there is no equality between them. Because a free adult has the authority to transact and surety, while a slave does not have authority over either of these matters unless the master permits. Similarly, a minor does not have authority over any of these unless his guardian permits.

"Mufawadah between a Muslim and a disbeliever is not valid."
He said: And not between a Muslim and a disbeliever. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said it is valid due to equality between them in agency (wakalah) and surety (kafalah), and no consideration is given to the additional authority that one possesses, like the mufawadah between a Shafi'i and a Hanafi, for it is valid, even though they differ in transactions regarding animals slaughtered without the basmalah, except that it is disliked (makruh) because the one who does not understand the permissible contracts. Their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) proof is that there is no equality in transactions, because if a dhimmi buys donkeys or pigs with the capital, it is valid, but if a Muslim buys them, it is not valid.
Translation: "And not between a Muslim and a disbeliever" etc. Al-Quduri said that mufawadah between a Muslim and a disbeliever is not valid. This is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said it is valid, because they are equal in agency and surety, and the additional authority that one possesses is not considered, just as mufawadah between a Shafi'i and a Hanafi is valid, even though they differ in the ruling of an animal slaughtered without intentionally saying Bismillah – the Shafi'i considers it halal but the Hanafi does not. Similarly, between a Muslim and a disbeliever it is valid but disliked (makruh), because the dhimmi does not fully know the issues and path of permissible contracts of mufawadah. The proof of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is that equality in transactions is necessary, because if a dhimmi buys pigs or wine with the capital, it is valid, but if a Muslim buys them, it is not valid.

"Mufawadah between two slaves, two children, and two mukatabs is not valid."
And it is not valid between two slaves, nor between two minors, nor between two mukatabs, because the validity of surety (kafalah) is absent. And in every case where mufawadah is not valid due to the absence of its condition, and that condition is not required in 'inan partnership, it becomes 'inan, because all conditions of 'inan are present. For 'inan may be specific and may be general.
Translation: And mufawadah is not valid between two slaves, nor between two minors, nor between two mukatabs, because their surety is not valid. And it is clear that where mufawadah is not valid due to the absence of a condition, and that condition is not required in 'inan partnership, then that mufawadah becomes 'inan partnership, because all conditions of 'inan are present then. 'inan partnership may be specific and may be general. For example, if an adult and a minor, or a free person and a slave or mukatab, contract mufawadah, or if two equal free men contract mufawadah with the condition that there is no surety, then in every case, due to the absence of surety, it becomes 'inan partnership, and this 'inan partnership will be general, just as mufawadah is always general.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the Hanafi ruling on Shirkat al-Mufawadah (equal partnership). It begins by defining mufawadah as a partnership where partners have equal capital, equal authority in transactions, and mutual surety. The author states that this partnership is valid by istihsan (juristic preference) but not by qiyas (analogy), because qiyas would deem it invalid due to the presence of unknown agency (wakalah bi majhul) and unknown surety (kafalah bi majhul), both of which are invalid on their own. However, istihsan overrides qiyas because of the widespread practice among people ('urf) and a hadith from Ibn Majah that mentions blessing in mufawadah. The passage then details the strict conditions for validity: both partners must be free, adult (baligh), and Muslim or dhimmi (or both Kitabi and Majusi together). Mufawadah is invalid between a free person and a slave, an adult and a minor, because the latter lack full legal capacity for tasarruf and kafalah. A major intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that mufawadah between a Muslim and a disbeliever is invalid due to lack of equality in transactions (e.g., a dhimmi can legally buy pork/wine, a Muslim cannot). Abu Yusuf argues it is valid because equality exists in wakalah and kafalah, and differences in tasarruf are tolerated (similar to mufawadah between a Shafi'i and a Hanafi), though he considers it makruh tanzihi. The passage concludes that if mufawadah fails due to missing conditions (like absence of kafalah), it automatically becomes Shirkat al-'Inan (general partnership), which has less stringent requirements. A crucial point: mufawadah is only contracted with the word 'mufawadah', but if the conditions are clearly stated in other words, the meaning takes precedence and the contract becomes valid mufawadah (or 'inan as the case may be).

Key Terms
مفاوضہ (Mufawadah): A type of partnership where partners have equal capital, equal authority in transactions, and mutual surety (kafalah) for each other's debts. It requires complete equality in freedom, adulthood, religion, and legal capacity.
شرکت عنان (Shirkat al-'Inan): A general partnership where partners may contribute unequal capital and have unequal authority; there is no mutual surety (kafalah). It does not require equality.
کفالت (Kafalah): Surety or guarantee, where each partner is liable for the debts incurred by the other in the partnership. In mufawadah, mutual kafalah is a necessary condition.
استحسان (Istihsan): Juristic preference, a secondary source of law in Hanafi fiqh used to override qiyas (analogy) when a more compelling proof (like 'urf, necessity, or hadith) suggests a different ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, why is Mufawadah between a Muslim and a dhimmi invalid?
A) Because the dhimmi cannot engage in trade with a Muslim
B) Because the dhimmi can legally buy pork and wine with partnership capital, while the Muslim cannot, thus lacking equality in transactions
C) Because a Muslim cannot enter into a partnership with a non-Muslim under any circumstances
D) Because the dhimmi has no legal capacity for surety (kafalah)

Key Takeaway
Mufawadah is a Hanafi-distinctive partnership valid by istihsan, requiring strict equality in legal capacity; failure converts it to 'inan.

Mufawadah Invalid Between Slaves, Minors, and Mukatabs
Ruling on prohibited partner categories for Mufawadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which categories of partners render Mufawadah invalid and explain the automatic conversion to 'Inan when its conditions are met.

Core Idea
Mufawadah fails if a partner lacks capacity for surety; but the contract becomes 'Inan if its conditions are present.

This lesson clarifies that Shirkat al-Mufawadah, with its mutual surety requirement, cannot be formed by partners who lack full legal capacity — like slaves, minors, and mukatabs. However, the contract is not entirely void; it converts to a valid Shirkat al-'Inan if the basic requirements of 'Inan are satisfied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited categories
List the three types of partners for whom Mufawadah is invalid: two slaves, two minors, two mukatabs.
Each pair must be of the same category.
2
Understand the rationale
The reason is the absence of validity of kafalah (suretyship) — these individuals lack full legal capacity to guarantee each other.
Kafalah is a fundamental condition of Mufawadah.
3
Note the conversion to 'Inan
If Mufawadah fails due to a missing condition, but all conditions for 'Inan are present, the contract becomes a valid 'Inan partnership.
'Inan does not require mutual surety.
4
Distinguish between Mufawadah and 'Inan
Recall that Mufawadah requires equal capital, full mutual agency, and surety; 'Inan may be specific (limited) or general, but lacks the surety element.
This distinction is crucial for determining the legal effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْنَ الْعَبْدَينِ وَ لَا بَيْنَ الصَّبِيَّيْنِ وَ لَا بَيْنَ الْمُكَاتِبِينِ لِاِنْعِدَامٍ صحةِ الكَفَالَةِ وَ فِى كُلّ مَوْضِع لَمْ تَصِـ الْمُفَاَوَصَةُ لِفَقْدِشَرطِهَا وَلَا يَشْتَرِطُ ذَالِكَ فِي الْعَنَانِ كَانَ عَنَانًا لِاسْتِجُمَاعِ شَرَائِطِ الْعَنَانِ إِذْهُوَ قَدْ يَكُونَ خا مَّا وَقَدْ يَكُونُ عَامًا
And it is not permissible between two slaves, nor between two minors, nor between two mukatabs, due to the absence of validity of surety (kafalah). And in every place where Mufawadah is not valid due to the lack of its condition, and that condition is not required in 'Inan, it becomes 'Inan because all the conditions of 'Inan are present, for it may be specific and it may be general.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage states a general ruling: Shirkat al-Mufawadah is invalid between two slaves, two minors (not having reached puberty), or two mukatabs (slaves who have contracted to purchase their freedom). The reason is that kafalah (suretyship) is a fundamental pillar of Mufawadah, and these individuals lack full legal capacity to undertake surety. However, if a contract of Mufawadah fails because such a condition is missing, but all conditions for Shirkat al-'Inan (limited partnership) are present, then the contract automatically becomes 'Inan, not void. 'Inan has variations: it may be specific (limited to certain transactions) or general (similar to Mufawadah but without mutual surety).

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitabah to purchase his freedom in installments.
عنان ('Inan): A limited partnership where partners contribute capital but are not each other's guarantors unless specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Mufawadah invalid between two minors?
A) Minors cannot own property.
B) Minors cannot give valid surety (kafalah).
C) Minors cannot engage in trade.
D) Minors cannot appoint agents.

Key Takeaway
Mufawadah is invalid between slaves, minors, and mukatabs due to their lack of capacity for surety, but the contract automatically becomes a valid 'Inan partnership if its conditions are satisfied.

Seller's Right to Demand Price from Either Partner in Mufawadah
Ruling on creditor's recourse against partners in Mufawadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that the seller may claim the price from either partner in Mufawadah and explain the surety partner's right of recourse.

Core Idea
In Mufawadah, the seller can demand the price from either partner because each is a surety for the other.

This passage clarifies a practical consequence of the mutual surety (kafala) inherent in Mufawadah partnership. When one partner buys goods on credit, the seller has a choice whom to approach for payment. The partner who pays as surety can later reclaim from the actual buyer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key parties and their roles
Recognize that there are two partners in a Mufawadah contract: the buyer (who purchases goods) and the other partner (surety). The seller is the creditor.
In Mufawadah, each partner is both principal and surety for the other.
2
State the seller's option
The seller may demand the full price from either partner directly, not just from the buyer. This is because the surety partner is jointly liable.
The seller does not need to sue both jointly; he can choose the one who is more solvent.
3
Explain the surety's right of recourse
If the surety partner pays the seller, he can later claim the amount from the buyer-partner. This is because the debt was originally owed by the buyer, and the payment came from joint wealth, but the surety is entitled to reimbursement.
The right of recourse prevents the surety from bearing the burden alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلِلْبَائِعِ أَنْ يَأَخُذُ بِالشَّمَنِ أَيُّهُمَا شَاءَ الْمُشْتَرِئَ بِالْإِ صَالَةِ وَصَاحِبَهُ بِالْكَفَالَةِ وَيَرْجِعُ الْكَفَيلُ عَلَى الْمُشْتَرِى بِحِقَتِهِ بِمَا أدى لأنَّهُ قَضَى دَيْنًا عَلَيْهِ مِنْ مَّالٍ مُشْتَرَك بَيْنَهُمَا
And the seller has the right to take the price from whichever of them he wishes: from the buyer directly (as principal) and from his partner by surety. And the surety (the partner who paid) may recourse against the buyer for his claim (the amount he paid) because he paid a debt owed by him from joint wealth between them.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage states a straightforward ruling arising from the nature of Mufawadah. Since both partners are sureties for each other, a seller who sold goods to one partner has the option to demand the full price from either partner. He can claim from the actual buyer as the principal debtor, or from the other partner as a surety. If the surety partner pays, he has the right to claim reimbursement from the buyer-partner, because the payment was made from wealth that is jointly owned but the debt was the buyer's personal obligation. This ensures fairness: the paying partner does not bear the loss alone.

Key Terms
كفيل (kafil): The partner who acts as surety and pays the debt; he can later reclaim from the actual buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one partner (A) buys goods on credit in Mufawadah, who can the seller demand payment from?
A) Only from partner A.
B) Only from the other partner B.
C) From either partner A (as buyer) or partner B (as surety).
D) From the partnership fund only.

Key Takeaway
In Mufawadah, the seller has the right to demand payment from either partner, and the paying partner has the right to be reimbursed by the actual buyer.

Conditions of Shirkat al-Mufawadah: Agency and Guarantee
Ruling on the basis of mufawadah contract on agency and guarantee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions required for Shirkat al-Mufawadah and explain why each is necessary.

Core Idea
Shirkat al-Mufawadah requires both mutual agency and guarantee to ensure equality and shared purpose.

In this passage, al-Quduri establishes two foundational conditions for a valid Shirkat al-Mufawadah (general partnership). While seemingly administrative, agency and guarantee are not optional extras—they are the very mechanism that makes the partnership legally distinct from mere co-ownership. Understanding their rationale will help you appreciate the Hanafi emphasis on equality and mutual liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the sentence that states how the contract of mufawadah is concluded. The Arabic says 'تَنْعَقِدُ عَلَى الْوَكَالَةِ وَالْكَفَالَةِ'.
2
Recognize the two conditions
The ruling names two essential components: wakalah (agency) and kafalah (guarantee). Both must be present for the contract to be a true mufawadah.
3
Understand the rationale for agency
Agency is required to fulfill the main purpose of the contract: partnership in wealth. Each partner acts as agent for the other, so that all trade activities are shared.
Without agency, each partner would only trade for himself, defeating the mutual benefit.
4
Understand the rationale for guarantee
Guarantee ensures equality in obligations: both partners are equally liable for debts arising from trade, so that third parties can claim from either.
This maintains the 'equality' (musawat) that defines mufawadah.
5
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
Other schools may not require both agency and guarantee for a general partnership. The Hanafi position is strict on equality in all aspects.
This distinction affects how partnerships are structured in different legal traditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَتَنْعَقِدُ عَلَى الْوَكَالَةِ وَالْكَفَالَةِ أَمَّا الْوَكَالَةُ فَلِتَحَقَّقِ الْمَقْصُودِ وَ هُوَ الشّرْكَةُ فِى المال على ما بيناه و اما الْكَفَالَ لِتَحَقُّقِ الْمُسَاوَاةِ فِيْمَا هُوَ مِنْ مَوَاجِبِ التَّجَارَاتِ وَهُوَ تَوَجَّهُ الْمُطَالَبَةِ نَحْوَهُمَا جَمِيعًا ترجمه قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ عقد مفاوضہ وکالت اور کفالت پر معتقد ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی دو ساتھیوں میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے دوسرے کا وکیل اور کفیل ہونا لازم ہوتا ہے۔ وکیل ہونا تو اس لئے لازم ہوتا ہے کہ اس عقد کا جو اصل مقصد ہے یعنی مال میں شرکت کا ہونا وہ پایا جاتا ہے تا کہ اس معاملہ سے جو کچھ بھی مالی فائدہ حاصل ہو اس میں دونوں کا حصہ ہو۔ اور کفیل ہونا اس لئے لازم ہوتا ہے کہ اس تجارت کے لئے جتنی چیزیں لوازمات میں سے ہیں ان سب میں دونوں کی برابری پائی جائے یعنی اس کی وجہ سے جو مطالبات سامنے آئیں ان کا تعلق ان دونوں سے ہو ۔ سب ان کے ذمہ دار ہوں ۔
He said: It (the contract of mufawadah) is concluded upon agency and guarantee. As for agency, it is for realizing the objective, which is partnership in wealth as we explained. As for guarantee, it is for realizing equality in what is from the obligations of trade, which is the direction of demand towards both of them jointly.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn (Quduri) explaining that Shirkat al-Mufawadah (general partnership) requires two components: mutual agency (wakalah) and mutual guarantee (kafalah). Agency allows each partner to act on behalf of the other in trade, ensuring that profits and losses are shared. Guarantee makes each partner liable for debts incurred by the other in the course of trade, ensuring equality in obligations. The commentary explains that agency serves the purpose of partnership in wealth, while guarantee ensures that both are equally subject to claims from third parties, maintaining the equality that is essential for mufawadah.

Key Terms
مفاوضہ (mufāwaḍah): A type of partnership where partners are equal in capital, profit, and liability, and each acts as agent and guarantor for the other.
وکالت (wakālah): Agency; each partner authorizes the other to act on his behalf in trade.
کفالت (kafālah): Guarantee; each partner is liable for debts incurred by the other in the course of partnership business.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is kafalah (guarantee) necessary in Shirkat al-Mufawadah?
A) To ensure partners share profits equally
B) To ensure that third parties can claim from either partner, maintaining equality in obligations
C) To allow partners to trade without capital
D) To prevent partners from acting independently

Key Takeaway
Shirkat al-Mufawadah is only valid if both partners act as agents and guarantors for each other.
