⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَايَجُوزُ الشِّرْكَةُ بِمَاسِوى ذَالِكَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَتَعَامَلَ النَّاسُ بِالتَّبْرِ وَ التَّقْوَرَةِ فَتَصِحُ الشَّرْكَةُ بِهِمَا هُكَدَادَ كَرَ فِي الكِتاب
ترجمہ اور قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ مذکورہ مالوں کے سواد دوسری کسی چیز سے شرکت مفاوضہ جائز نہیں ہے مگر اس صورت میں کہ وہاں کے لوگ پتھروں یا پگھلائی ہوئی چاندی سے آپس میں شرکت مفاوضہ کا معاملہ کرتے ہوں تو ان دونوں چیزوں سے بھی شرکت جائز ہوگی (یعنی اگر لوگوں میں ڈھلے ہوئے سکوں کے بغیر صرف چاندی اور سونے کی ڈلی اور ٹکڑوں سے بھی شرکت مفاوضہ کا معاملہ ہوتا ہو ) الا تو جائز ہوگا ، صاحب قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے اپنی کتاب مختصر القدوری میں ایسا ہی بیان کیا ہے۔ ( یہ بات بظاہر جامع صغیر کے قول کے مخالف ہے۔ اسی لئے انہوں نے فرمایا ہے)۔
وفِى الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ وَلَا يَكُونُ الْمُفَاوَضَةُ بِمَثَاقِيلِ ذَهَبِ أَوْ فِضَّةٍ وَمُرَادُهُ التبرُ فَعَلى هَذِهِ الرِّوَايَةِ اليَبْرُ سِلْعَةُ من بِالتَّعَينَ فَلَا يَصْلَحُ رَأْسَ الْمَالِ فِى الْمُضَارَبَاتِ وَالشَّرَكَاتِ وَذَكَرَ فِى كِتَابِ الصَّرْفِ أَنَّ التَّقْرَةَ لَا يَتَعَين لَا يَنفَسخُ الْعَقْدُ بِهَلَاكِ، قَبْلَ التَّسْلِيمِ فَعَلَى تِلْكَ الرِّوَايَةِ يَصْلَحُ رَاسَ الْمَالِ فِيْهِمَا وَهَذَا لِمَاعُرِفَ أَنَّهُمَا
ترجمہ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ سونے یا چاندی کے متوالوں سے شرکت مفاوضہ نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اس جگہ امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی مشتقال سے مراد تبر (ٹکڑے) ہیں۔ اس بناء پر تبر ایسا اسباب ہے جو معین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے مضاربت یا شرکت کے معاملات میں یہ راس المال نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ اور جامع صغیر کی کتاب الصرف میں مذکور ہے کہ گائی اور پگھلائی ہوئی چاندنی جو ڈھلی ہوئی اور سکہ کی شکل میں نہ ہو وہ بھی متعین نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر بیع میں حوالہ کرنے سے پہلے وہ ضائع ہو جائے تو عقد بیع نہیں ہوگی ۔ پس اس روایت کے مطابق اگلائی ہوئی ہو یا ڈلی کی شکل میں ہم سب شرکت اور مضاربت میں اصل پونچی یا راس المال ہو سکتے ہیں۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ سونا اور چاندی میں فطری اور خلقی طور سے شمعیت رکھی گئی ہے۔ خواہ ان کے سکے بنے ہوئے ہوں یا نہ ہوں لیکن پہلی روایت اصح ہے۔ کیونکہ سونا اور چاندی اگر چہ اپنی اصلی خلقت میں تجارت کے لئے مخلوق ہیں۔ لیکن شمن اور قیمت کے طور پر ان کا استعمال ان کے سکہ ڈھل جانے پر ہی مخصوص ہے (یعنی ڈھال کر دور ہم دینار وغیرہ بنا دئیے جانے کے بعد ہی ہوتا ہے ) کیونکہ ایسی حالت میں بظاہر ان کو دوسرے کسی کام میں نہیں لایا جاتا ہے۔ پھر بھی بالغرض اگر لوگوں میں سکے میں ڈھالے بغیر ڈلی کی شکل ہی میں بطور ثمن ان کا استعمال ہونے لگے تو ان کے اس استعمال اور رواج ہی کو مسئلہ کے حکم میں فرض کر لیا جائے گا۔ اور اس وقت یہ مطلقا من ہو جائیں گے ۔ اور راس المال ہونے کے لائق ہو جائیں گے۔
He said: 'Partnership is not valid with other than that unless people customarily deal with tabr and naqrah, then partnership with both is valid.' Thus wrote al-Qudūrī in his book. Translation: And al-Qudūrī (may Allah have mercy on him) said that Mufāwaḍa partnership is not valid with anything other than the mentioned properties except if the people there customarily transact with [uncoined] gold or [melted] silver, then partnership with both is valid. (That is, if people without minted coins only use lumps and pieces of gold and silver for Mufāwaḍa partnership transactions, then it is valid). Al-Ṣāḥib al-Qudūrī stated similarly in his book Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī. (This apparently contradicts the statement of Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr. Therefore he said:) And in Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr: 'And Mufāwaḍa is not valid with mithqāls of gold or silver.' And what is meant by it is tibr. According to this narration, tibr is a commodity that becomes specified by specification, so it is not suitable as capital in Muḍāraba and partnerships. And it is mentioned in Kitāb al-Ṣarf of Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr that naqrah does not become specified; the contract is not voided by its destruction before delivery. So according to that narration, it is suitable as capital in both. And this is because it is known that they are... Translation: And in Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr it is stated that Mufāwaḍa is not valid with mithqāls of gold or silver. Here Imām Muḥammad means by 'mithqāl' tibr (pieces). Accordingly, tibr is a good that becomes specified by specification, so it cannot be capital in Muḍāraba and partnerships. And in Kitāb al-Ṣarf of Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr it is mentioned that naqrah (uncoined silver) is not specified; if it is destroyed before delivery in a sale, the contract is not rescinded. So according to that narration, it can be capital in both. The reason is that gold and silver possess thamanīyah (value as currency) by nature, whether coined or not. But the first narration is more correct (aṣaḥ). Because gold and silver, though created originally for trade, their use as a currency is specific to being minted (coined). However, if people customarily use them as currency even in lumps, then that custom takes the ruling of minting, and they become absolute thaman and suitable as capital.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of using tibr (uncoined gold) and naqrah (uncoined silver) as capital in Shirkat al-Mufāwaḍa and Muḍāraba. The text cites two primary sources: Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī and Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr. According to al-Qudūrī, partnership with tibr and naqrah is valid if people customarily deal with them (ta‘āmul). This is based on the principle that custom (‘urf) can give an item the ruling of thaman. However, Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr (a work of Imām Muḥammad) states that Mufāwaḍa is not valid with mithqāls (weights) of gold or silver—meaning tibr. The commentator explains that this narration treats tibr as a commodity (sil‘a) that becomes specified by identification (ta‘yīn), thus unsuitable as capital. Yet there is another narration from Kitāb al-Ṣarf (within Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr) that naqrah does not become specified, meaning it can be capital. The commentator notes a tension: gold and silver inherently possess thamanīyah (monetary value), so they should be like dirhams/dinars. However, the first narration (treating tibr as commodity) is deemed aṣaḥ (more correct) because the actual use as currency is tied to coinage. Nevertheless, if custom establishes their use as a medium of exchange (even uncoined), that custom takes precedence, and they become absolute thaman. Thus, the ruling depends on prevailing custom.

Key Terms
تبر (tibr): Uncoined gold, generally in nugget or dust form.
نقره (naqrah): Uncoined silver, often in melted or lump form.
مثقال (mithqāl): A unit of weight; here referring to a weight of gold or silver, i.e., uncoined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what determines whether tibr and naqrah can be used as capital in Mufāwaḍa?
A) Their weight and purity.
B) Whether they are considered currency by custom (ta‘āmul).
C) The presence of a formal minting process.
D) Agreement of both partners.

Key Takeaway
Custom (‘urf) can transform the legal status of an item from commodity to currency, overriding the default classification in Hanafi partnership law.

Shirkah — Partnership

Partnership in Measured, Weighed, and Counted Items
Intra-Hanafi dispute on contractual partnership after mixing fungibles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the views of Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad on the validity of contractual partnership after mixing fungibles, and identify the mufta bihi position according to Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
After mixing identical fungibles, the majority Hanafi view rejects contractual partnership; it remains mere joint ownership.

The previous chapter established that Shirkat al-Mufāwaḍa is not valid with non-silver/gold items before mixing. But what if two people mix their wheat, oil, or eggs together and then jointly trade? Can a contractual partnership arise from the mixed heap? This passage presents an intra-madhab disagreement between Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad al-Shaybani on exactly that point, and it clarifies the authoritative position according to Zahir al-Riwayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the default ruling
Before mixing, it is settled (lā khilāfa) that Shirkat al-Mufāwaḍa with makīl, mawzūn, or adadī mutaqārib is not valid. Each partner retains his share and bears its loss. Note this as the baseline.
The prohibition before mixing is unanimous among Hanafis.
2
Recognise the scenario after mixing
The text posits that they mix identical goods (e.g., wheat with wheat) and then purchase something jointly. The ruling now becomes disputed between Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad.
Assume the goods are of the same genus and are fungibles (mithlī).
3
Contrast the two positions
Abū Yūsuf: even after mixing, it remains shirkat milk (co-ownership), not a contractual partnership. Reason: mixing specifies each particle (tʿayyun), removing ambiguity. Muḥammad: contractual partnership can be valid because such goods have a thamanī aspect—they can be sold as a debt on the dhimma—so they are not fully specified.
The difference appears practically when capitals are equal but profit share is unequal.
4
Identify the tarjīḥ (preferred ruling)
The text declares: 'Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah mā qālahu Abū Yūsuf' — the Zahir al-Riwayah is the view of Abū Yūsuf. Thus the muftā bihī is that the partnership after mixing is only shirkat milk.
The reasoning for Abū Yūsuf: specification occurs after mixing just as before.
5
Note the exception: different genera
If the two goods are of different types (e.g., wheat and barley, oil and butter), even Muḥammad agrees the contractual partnership is invalid, because jahāla (uncertainty) arises as the mixture becomes of different value-types.
This is a key qualifier: the dispute only applies to same-genus fungibles.

ثُمَّ قَولُهُ وَلَا يَجُوزُ بِمَا سِوَى ذَالِكَ يَتَنَاوَلُ الْمَكِيلَ وَالْمُوزُونَ وَالْعَدَدِى الْمُتَقَارِبَ وَلَا خِلَافَ فِيهِ بَينَا قَبْلَ الْخَلط وَلِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا رِبُعُ مَتَاعِهِ وَعَلَيْهِ وَضَيعَتُهُ وَإِن خَلَطَا ثُمَّ اشْتَرَ كَا فَكَذَالِكَ فِي قَوْلِ أَبِي يُوسُفَ وَالشَّرَكَةِ شِرْكَةُ مِلْك لاشركَةُ عَقْدٍ وَعِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ تَصِحُ شِرْكَةُ الْعَقْدِ وَثَمَرَةُ الْاِخْتِلَافِ تَظْهَرُ عِنْدَ التَّسَاوِى فِي الْمَالَيْنِ وَاشْتِرَاطُ التَّفَاضُلِ في الربح فظاهرُ الرِّوَايَة مَا قَالَهُ ابويُوسُفَ لِأَنَّهُ تُتَعَيَّنَ بِالتَّعيين بَعْدَ الخَلْطِ كَمَا يَتَعَيَّنُ قَبْلَهُ وَلِمُحَمَّدٌ أَنَّهَا ثَمَنَّ مِنْ وَجْهِ حَتَّى جَازَ الْبَيْعُ بِهَا دَيْنا فِى الدّمَةِ وَبَيْعُ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنه يَتَعَيَّنُ بِالتَّعبير فَعَمِلْنَا بِالشَّبْهَيْنِ بِالْإِضَافَةِ إِلَى الْحَالَيْنِ بِخِلَافِ الْعُرُوضِ لَّانَّهَا لَيْسَتْ ثَمَنَّا بِحَالٍ وَلَوِ اخْتَلَفَاجِنِّسًا كَالْحِنْطَةِ وَالشَّعِيرِ وَالزَّيْتِ وَالسَّمَن فَخَلَطَا لَا يَنَعْقِدُ الشَّرَكَةُ بِهَا بِالْإِنْفَاقِ وَالْفَرَقُ لِلمُحَمَّد أَنَّ المَخْلُوطَ مِنْ جِنْسِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ ذَوَاتِ الْأَمْثَالِ وَ مِنْ جِنْسَينِ مِنْ دَوَاتِ الْقِيمِ فَتَمَكَّنَ الْجَهَالَةُ كَمَا فِي الْعُرُوضِ إِذَا لَمْ تَصِحُ الشَّرُكَةُ فَحُكُم الخَلْطِ قدبَّيْنَاهُ فِي كِتَابِ الْقَضَاءِ
Then his saying: 'And it is not valid with other than that' includes makīl (measured by volume), mawzūn (weighed), and ‘adadī mutaqārib (counted items of similar size). There is no disagreement about it before mixing. Each of them has a portion of his goods and bears its loss. And if they mix then they buy, it is the same in the view of Abū Yūsuf: the partnership is a partnership of ownership (shirkat milk), not a contract. And according to Muḥammad, the contract partnership (shirkat ‘aqd) is valid. The consequence of the difference appears when the two capitals are equal and they stipulate disparity in profit. The Zahir al-Riwayah is what Abū Yūsuf said, because it becomes specified by specification after mixing just as it becomes specified before mixing. And for Muḥammad is that it is thaman (currency) from one aspect, so much so that selling it as a debt on the dhimma is valid, and it becomes specified by specification. So we act on both similarities with respect to the two states, unlike goods (‘urūḍ) because they are not thaman in any state. And if the two are of different genus, like wheat and barley, oil and clarified butter, and they mix, the partnership is not concluded by agreement. The distinction for Muḥammad is that the mixture of one genus is of things that are fungible (dhawāt al-amthāl), and of two genera is of things with value (dhawāt al-qiyam), so ignorance (jahāla) occurs, as in goods when partnership is not valid. And the ruling of mixing we have explained in Kitāb al-Qaḍā’.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage deals with Shirkat al-Mufāwaḍa using items that are measured (makīl e.g., wheat), weighed (mawzūn e.g., gold), or counted (adadī but of similar size e.g., eggs or walnuts). The text first states that there is no disagreement that such partnership is invalid before mixing; each partner retains ownership over his share and bears its loss. If they mix their identical goods together and then jointly purchase something, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Abū Yūsuf holds that after mixing, it remains a partnership of ownership (shirkat milk), not a contractual partnership (shirkat ‘aqd), because the goods become specified (muta‘ayyin) by the mixing, just as they were specified before mixing. Thus the contract of Mufāwaḍa is not established. Muḥammad argues that such items (especially grain, etc.) have a resemblance to currency (thaman) in that they can be sold as debts on the dhimma, so they are not fully specified after mixing; thus the contractual partnership can be valid. The practical consequence (thamarah) appears when the two partners contribute equal amounts and stipulate unequal profit-sharing—Abū Yūsuf would not allow this in a contract partnership, while Muḥammad would allow it. The text states that the Zahir al-Riwayah (the authoritative transmission) is the view of Abū Yūsuf. However, if the two goods are of different genus (e.g., wheat and barley), then even Muḥammad agrees that the partnership is not valid due to jahāla (ignorance) because the mixture becomes of different kinds and thus akin to ‘urūḍ (non-fungible goods). The discussion ends with a reference to Kitāb al-Qaḍā’ for the ruling on mixing.

Key Terms
مکیل (makīl): Items sold by volume measure, e.g., wheat, dates.
موزون (mawzūn): Items sold by weight, e.g., gold, silver, rice.
عددی متقارب (adadī mutaqārib): Items sold by count where units are similar in value, e.g., eggs, walnuts.
شِركة الملك (shirkat milk): A partnership of joint ownership without a contractual agreement for profit-sharing from trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah in this passage, what kind of partnership results when two people mix identical makīl items and then jointly buy something?
A) Shirkat al-‘aqd (contractual partnership).
B) Shirkat milk (ownership partnership).
C) Shirkat al-mufāwaḍa (unlimited partnership).
D) No partnership at all.

Key Takeaway
After mixing identical fungible goods, the mufta bihi (Abū Yūsuf) is that only joint ownership arises; a contractual partnership is not formed, and any unequal profit stipulation is unenforceable.

Ruling on Uncoined Gold/Silver as Capital in Partnership
Ruling statement on tibr as capital

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on uncoined gold/silver (tibr) as capital in partnership and identify the condition of customary usage that changes the ruling.

Core Idea
Uncoined gold/silver is not capital unless custom treats it as currency.

This passage resolves a key question in partnership law: can raw gold or silver nuggets be used as the capital contribution? The Hanafi school has two narrations, but the relied-upon view is that tibr is not suitable unless people customarily use it as a medium of exchange. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the role of custom in determining the legal status of assets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two riwayat
Note that Imam Muhammad reports two conflicting narrations: one from Jami' al-Saghir prohibits tibr as capital; another permits it. Determine which is preferred and why.
The first riwayah is declared asah (more correct).
2
Understand the basis of the first riwayah
The first view treats tibr as a specific commodity (ayn) that becomes specified by identification, unlike coined money which is non-specified. Thus it cannot be capital.
Minted coins are not specified because they are fungible.
3
Analyze the second riwayah's reasoning
The second view argues that gold and silver inherently possess thamaniyyah (pricehood) even if uncoined, so they should be capital.
This reasoning relies on the natural quality of the metal.
4
Apply the condition of custom (ta'amul)
The text concludes that if people customarily use tibr as currency, custom can substitute for minting, making it suitable as capital.
Custom (ta'amul) is given legal weight equivalent to minting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۲۳
كتاب الشركة
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هفتم خلْقًا ثَمَنَيْنِ فِي الْأَصْلِ إِلَّا إِنَّ الْأَوَّلَ أَصَحُ لأنَّهَا وَإِنْ خُلِقَتْ لِلتِّجَارَةِ فِي الأصل لكِنَّ الثَّمَنِيَّةَ تَخْتَصُّ بِالضَّرُبِ الْمَخْصُوص لِأَنَّ عِنْدَ ذَالِكَ لَا يُصْرَفُ إلى شَى اخَرَ ظَاهِرًا إِلَّا أَنْ يَجْرِيَ التَّعَامُلُ بِاسْتِعْمَالِهِمَا ثَمَنًا فَيَنْزِلُ التَّعَامُلُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الضّرب فَيَكُونُ ثَمَنًا وَيَصْلُحُ رَأْسَ الْمَالِ
ترجمہ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ سونے یا چاندی کے متوالوں سے شرکت مفاوضہ نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اس جگہ امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی مشتقال سے مراد تبر (ٹکڑے) ہیں۔ اس بناء پر تبر ایسا اسباب ہے جو معین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے مضاربت یا شرکت کے معاملات میں یہ راس المال نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ اور جامع صغیر کی کتاب الصرف میں مذکور ہے کہ گائی اور پگھلائی ہوئی چاندنی جو ڈھلی ہوئی اور سکہ کی شکل میں نہ ہو وہ بھی متعین نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر بیع میں حوالہ کرنے سے پہلے وہ ضائع ہو جائے تو عقد بیع نہیں ہوگی ۔ پس اس روایت کے مطابق اگلائی ہوئی ہو یا ڈلی کی شکل میں ہم سب شرکت اور مضاربت میں اصل پونچی یا راس المال ہو سکتے ہیں۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ سونا اور چاندی میں فطری اور خلقی طور سے شمعیت رکھی گئی ہے۔ خواہ ان کے سکے بنے ہوئے ہوں یا نہ ہوں لیکن پہلی روایت اصح ہے۔ کیونکہ سونا اور چاندی اگر چہ اپنی اصلی خلقت میں تجارت کے لئے مخلوق ہیں۔ لیکن شمن اور قیمت کے طور پر ان کا استعمال ان کے سکہ ڈھل جانے پر ہی مخصوص ہے (یعنی ڈھال کر دور ہم دینار وغیرہ بنا دئیے جانے کے بعد ہی ہوتا ہے ) کیونکہ ایسی حالت میں بظاہر ان کو دوسرے کسی کام میں نہیں لایا جاتا ہے۔ پھر بھی بالغرض اگر لوگوں میں سکے میں ڈھالے بغیر ڈلی کی شکل ہی میں بطور ثمن ان کا استعمال ہونے لگے تو ان کے اس استعمال اور رواج ہی کو مسئلہ کے حکم میں فرض کر لیا جائے گا۔ اور اس وقت یہ مطلقا من ہو جائیں گے ۔ اور راس المال ہونے کے لائق ہو جائیں گے۔
Page 223 Book of Partnership. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume Seven. Created as two prices (thamanayn) in origin, but the first is more correct (asah) because even though they were created for trade originally, the quality of being a price (thamaniyyah) is specific to the specific minted form (darb), because then they are not turned to other things apparently, unless customary dealing (ta'amul) of using them as price occurs, then the custom takes the place of minting, making them a price and suitable for capital. Translation: In Jami' al-Saghir it is stated that partnership (mufawada) with pieces (mutawwalat) of gold and silver is not valid. Here Imam Muhammad's 'mutawwalat' means tibr (nuggets). On this basis, tibr is a commodity that becomes specified by specification. Therefore it cannot be capital in mudarabah or partnership transactions. And in Jami' al-Saghir's Book of Sarf it is mentioned that smelted and melted silver that is not molded and not in coin form is also not specified. So that if it is lost before transfer in a sale, the sale contract is not concluded. According to this narration, smelted or in nugget form, they can all be original capital in partnership and mudarabah. The reason is that gold and silver inherently have the quality of being price (thaman), whether they are coined or not. But the first narration (riwayah) is more correct. Because gold and silver, though created for trade in their original nature, the usage as price and value is specific to after they are coined (i.e., after being minted into dinars etc.). Because in that state they are apparently not used for other things. However, if people customarily use them in nugget form as price without coining, then their usage and custom will be considered equivalent to the ruling, and they will become absolutely thaman and suitable for capital.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement concerning whether uncoined gold and silver (tibr) can serve as capital (ra's al-mal) in partnership (shirkah) and mudarabah. The text opens by noting that in the original nature (khalqan), gold and silver are created as thamanayn (two prices), but the first of two narrations is considered more correct (asah). The first narration, from Jami' al-Saghir, holds that tibr cannot be capital because it is a commodity that becomes specified by specification (ta'yin), unlike minted coins which are non-specified. The second narration allows it because gold and silver inherently possess the attribute of thamaniyyah. The author then provides an analysis: thamaniyyah is specific to coined forms (darb) because coined money is not normally used for other purposes. However, if people customarily (ta'amul) use tibr as thaman, then custom takes the place of minting, and it becomes suitable as capital. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the first narration is asah, but custom can override it by making tibr function as thaman. Thus, the ruling is context-dependent on customary practice.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): The quality of being a standard medium of exchange (price).
تبر (tibr): Uncoined gold or silver in the form of nuggets or ingots.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct report (asah), what condition must be met for uncoined gold/silver to be used as capital in partnership?
A) It must be minted into coins.
B) It must be treated as thaman by custom.
C) It must be mixed with other goods.
D) It must be measured by volume.

Key Takeaway
Uncoined gold/silver can only be partnership capital if local custom treats it as currency.

Shirkat al-Mufawada with Mixed Items: Abu Yusuf vs Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on mixed capital

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's positions on contractual partnership after mixing makil/mawzun/adadi items, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) regarding profit-sharing conditions.

Core Idea
After mixing same-genus makil items, Abu Yusuf denies contractual partnership; Muhammad allows it.

This passage navigates a nuanced intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: when partners mix weighed, measured, or counted items of the same genus and then enter a Shirkat al-Mufawada, does a contractual partnership (shirkat al-aqd) form? Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani differ based on whether mixed items retain specification or acquire a dual character as price (thaman) and commodity. Understanding their proofs and the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is critical for correctly structuring such partnerships in practice.

Guided Path
1
Establish the common ground
Identify the undisputed rule: before mixing, no contractual partnership is valid with makil/mawzun/adadi items. Each partner retains profit and loss of his own goods.
This applies regardless of genus or similarity.
2
Locate the point of dispute
After mixing items of the same genus, does a Shirkat al-Aqd become possible? Abu Yusuf says no; Muhammad says yes.
The dispute hinges on the legal character of the mixture.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf argues that mixed items become specified by specification (ta'yin) just as before mixing, so they remain commodities (mabi') and cannot transform into price (thaman). Hence, only shirkat al-milk exists.
Specification prevents the mixture from being treated as unspecific thaman.
4
Analyze Muhammad's proof
Muhammad contends that such items have a dual nature: they can be thaman (sold on credit as debt) and also become specified. Therefore, before mixing they are commodities, after mixing they function as thaman, allowing contractual partnership.
Muhammad gives effect to both resemblances (shabahayn) based on the state.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical consequence appears when capitals are equal but profit-sharing is unequal (e.g., 2/3 vs 1/3). Abu Yusuf's view invalidates such condition; Muhammad's validates it. The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is Abu Yusuf's.
For fatwa, follow Abu Yusuf's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مکیلی موزونی اور عددی چیزوں میں شرکت مفاوضہ درست نہیں
ثُمَّ قَولُهُ وَلَا يَجُوزُ بِمَا سِوَى ذَالِكَ يَتَنَاوَلُ الْمَكِيلَ وَالْمُوزُونَ وَالْعَدَدِى الْمُتَقَارِبَ وَلَا خِلَافَ فِيهِ بَينَا قَبْلَ الْخَلط وَلِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا رِبُعُ مَتَاعِهِ وَعَلَيْهِ وَضَيعَتُهُ وَإِن خَلَطَا ثُمَّ اشْتَرَ كَا فَكَذَالِكَ فِي قَوْلِ أَبِي يُوسُفَ وَالشَّرَكَةِ شِرْكَةُ مِلْك لاشركَةُ عَقْدٍ وَعِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ تَصِحُ شِرْكَةُ الْعَقْدِ وَثَمَرَةُ الْاِخْتِلَافِ تَظْهَرُ عِنْدَ التَّسَاوِى فِي الْمَالَيْنِ وَاشْتِرَاطُ التَّفَاضُلِ في الربح فظاهرُ الرِّوَايَة مَا قَالَهُ ابويُوسُفَ لِأَنَّهُ تُتَعَيَّنَ بِالتَّعيين بَعْدَ الخَلْطِ كَمَا يَتَعَيَّنُ قَبْلَهُ وَلِمُحَمَّدٌ أَنَّهَا ثَمَنَّ مِنْ وَجْهِ حَتَّى جَازَ الْبَيْعُ بِهَا دَيْنا فِى الدّمَةِ وَبَيْعُ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنه يَتَعَيَّنُ بِالتَّعبير فَعَمِلْنَا بِالشَّبْهَيْنِ بِالْإِضَافَةِ إِلَى الْحَالَيْنِ بِخِلَافِ الْعُرُوضِ لَّانَّهَا لَيْسَتْ ثَمَنَّا بِحَالٍ وَلَوِ اخْتَلَفَاجِنِّسًا كَالْحِنْطَةِ وَالشَّعِيرِ وَالزَّيْتِ وَالسَّمَن فَخَلَطَا لَا يَنَعْقِدُ الشَّرَكَةُ بِهَا بِالْإِنْفَاقِ وَالْفَرَقُ لِلمُحَمَّد أَنَّ المَخْلُوطَ مِنْ جِنْسِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ ذَوَاتِ الْأَمْثَالِ وَ مِنْ جِنْسَينِ مِنْ دَوَاتِ الْقِيمِ فَتَمَكَّنَ الْجَهَالَةُ كَمَا فِي الْعُرُوضِ إِذَا لَمْ تَصِحُ الشَّرُكَةُ فَحُكُم الخَلْطِ قدبَّيْنَاهُ فِي كِتَابِ الْقَضَاءِ
ترجمہ اور قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا یہ کہنا کہ ان کے علاوہ دوسری چیزوں سے شرکت جائز نہیں ہے تو اس میں کیلی اور روزنی چیزیں اور جو گن کر فروخت ہوتی ہیں اور آپس میں تقریباً برابر ہوتی ہیں جیسے انڈے، اخروٹ) یہ سب چیزیں بھی داخل ہیں یعنی یہ چیزیں شرکت مفاوضہ کے لئے راس المال نہ ہوں گی )۔ اس مسئلہ میں ہمارے علماء کے درمیان کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ جبکہ خلط سے پہلے ہو ۔ یعنی ماں کے ملا دینے سے پہلے شرکت کا عقدان چیزوں پر نہیں ہوسکتا ہے۔
اور دونوں شرکاء میں سے ہر ایک کے سامان کا نفع اس کے لئے مخصوص ہوگا ۔ اور اگر اس میں نقصان ہو تو وہ بھی اسی کا ہوگا ۔ اور اگر دونوں نے اپنا اپنا مال ملا کر ایک کر دیا اور پھر اسکے شرکت کے معاملہ کو طے کیا تو بھی امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک یہی حکم ہوگا ۔ یہ شرکت ملک کہلائے گی ۔ یعنی دونوں کی ملکیت آپس میں ملی ہوئی ہے۔ اس لئے یہ شرکت عقد نہ ہوگی ۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک شرکت عقد بھی صحیح ہے۔ اس اختلاف کا نتیجہ اس شکل میں ظاہر ہوگا کہ دونوں شر کا ء کا مال آپس میں برابر ہولیکن نفع میں ایک کے لئے کچھ زیادہ اور دوسرے کے لئے کچھ کم ہونے کی شرط لگائی گئی ہو۔ مثلاً ایک کے لئے نفع میں دو تہائی اور دوسرے کے لئے ایک تہائی ہونے کی شرط لگائی گئی ہو تو امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک یہ شرکت جائز نہ ہوگی بلکہ ہر ایک کو اسی کے مال کا نفع ملے گا اور یہی ظاہر الروایہ ہے کیونکہ یہ مال ملا دینے کے بعد بھی معین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتا ہے۔ جیسے ملانے سے پہلے متعین ہو جاتا ہے اور مام حمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایسا مال ایک اعتبار سے شمن ہے یہاں تک کہ اس کے عوض میں اپنے ذمہ قرض رکھ کر بیچ کرنا جائز ہے ( مثلاً کسی شخص نے کسی سے کوئی چیز مرغی کے دس انڈوں یا پانچ سیر گیہوں یا تین سیر لوہے کے عوض خریدی اس طرح پر کہ یہ انڈے یا گیہوں یا لوہا مشتری کے ذمہ ادھار ہے تو یہ قرض جائز ہوا اس بناء پر یہ چیزیں شمن ہوں گی ۔ ) اور دوسرے اعتبار سے یہی چیزیں بیچ ہیں۔ کہ معین کرنے سے یہ متعین بھی ہو جاتی ہیں۔ پس ان میں دوہری مشابہت ہوئی ۔ اس لئے ہم نے دونوں مشابہتوں پر عمل کیا یہ کہہ کر ملانے سے پہلے ان کو مبیع کہا اور یہ کہ اس میں شرکت جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور ملانے کے بعد ان کو شمن قرار دیا اور یہ کہ ان میں شرکت جائز ہے۔ بخلاف دوسرے اسباب ( مثلا تخت و کرسی و صندوق وغیرہ کے کہ یہ چیزیں کسی حال میں بھی ثمن نہیں بن سکتی ہیں۔ (پھر اختلاف کی یہ صورتیں اس وقت ہیں جبکہ وہ کیلی و وزنی و عددی دونوں کے پاس ایک ہی جنس کی ہوں) کیونکہ اگر دونوں کی جنس مختلف ہو جیسے ایک کے پاس گیہوں اور دوسرے کے پاس جو ہوں یا ایک کے پاس روغن زیتون اور دوسرے کے پاس گھی ہو۔ پھر اگر دونوں نے سب مال ملا دیا تو بھی بالا تفاق عقد شرکت نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ امام مالک رحمتہ اللہ علیہ و امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ بھی اس پر متفق ہیں (پس امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک ایک جنس ہونے سے خلط کے بعد شرکت جائز ہے۔ لیکن مختلف جنس ہونے سے جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس میں فرق یہ ہے کہ ایک ہی جنس کے مخلوط ہو جانے سے وہ پشنی مشکلی چیزوں میں سے ہے ۔ یعنی اگر کوئی شخص اسے برباد کر دے تو اس کی جیسی مثلی چیز اس کا قائم مقام ہو سکتی ہے اور دو جنسوں کی ملی ہوئی مخلوط چیز مشکلی نہیں بلکہ قیمتی ( قیمت والی ) ہے اس کے برباد کر دینے والے پر اس کا مثل نہیں بلکہ اس کی قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اس بناء پر اس میں جہالت پیدا ہو گئی۔ (یعنی ہر شریک کو اس کی تقسیم کے وقت اس کا اصل مال مل سکتا ہے جیسے اسباب میں ہوتا ہے)۔ اور جب شرکت صحیح نہ ہوئی تو خلط کا جو حکم ہے وہ ہم نے کتاب القضاء میں بیان کیا ہے۔ بلکہ کتاب الود یعت میں بیان کیا ہے ) الغایہ یا کفایۃ المنتہی میں ملاخط ہو ۔
Shirkat al-Mufawada is not valid with measurable, weighable, and countable (similar) items. Then his statement: 'And it is not allowed with other than that' includes makil, mawzun, and adadi mutaqarib, and there is no dispute about that before mixing. And each of the two has the profit of his own goods and bears its loss. If they mix and then contract partnership, it is the same according to Abu Yusuf: the partnership is a partnership of ownership (shirkat al-milk), not a contractual partnership (shirkat al-aqd). According to Muhammad, a contractual partnership is valid. The fruit of the difference appears when the two capitals are equal and they stipulate disparity in profit. The zahir al-riwayah is what Abu Yusuf said, because after mixing it becomes specified by specification just as before mixing. Muhammad's argument: it is thaman from one aspect, such that selling with it as a debt in the dhimma is permissible, and from another aspect it is a commodity in that it becomes specified by specification. So we give effect to both resemblances relative to the two states. Unlike 'urud (goods) because they are not thaman in any state. If they differ in genus, like wheat and barley, oil and ghee, and they mix, the partnership is not contracted by agreement. The difference according to Muhammad is that the mixture of a single genus is among things of the same kind (mithliyyat), and of two genera is among things of value (qimiyyat), so ignorance (jahalah) occurs, as in 'urud when partnership is not valid. The ruling of mixing we have explained in Kitab al-Qada' (Book of Judgements).
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding the validity of Shirkat al-Mufawada (general partnership) with capital consisting of makil (measured), mawzun (weighed), and adadi (counted) items, such as grains, oils, eggs, and nuts. The text begins by affirming that there is no dispute among Hanafi scholars that before mixing (qabl al-khalat), partnership is not valid with such items. Each partner retains the profit and loss of his own goods. The dispute arises after they mix their goods and then formally agree on a partnership. Abu Yusuf holds that even after mixing, the partnership remains a shirkat al-milk (ownership partnership), not a contractual partnership (shirkat al-aqd). Consequently, any stipulation of unequal profit-sharing (tafadul fi al-ribh) is invalid. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that a contractual partnership (shirkat al-aqd) is valid after mixing, allowing unequal profit shares. The text states that the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is Abu Yusuf's view, because the mixed items become specified upon specification (ta'yin) just as before mixing. Muhammad's argument is that such items have a dual nature: from one perspective they are thaman (price) because they can be sold on credit as debt (dayn fi al-dhimma), and from another they are commodity (mabi') because they become specified. Therefore, we treat them differently based on the state: before mixing as mabi' (disallowing partnership), after mixing as thaman (allowing partnership). The text then distinguishes between same genus and different genus: if both partners have items of the same genus (e.g., both wheat), Muhammad allows contractual partnership after mixing; if different genera (e.g., wheat and barley), there is no dispute that partnership is invalid due to ignorance (jahalah) from the mixing of values (qimiyyat). The passage also references the ruling on mixing detailed in Kitab al-Qada'.

Key Terms
مکیل (makil): Items sold by measure, such as grains.
موزون (mawzun): Items sold by weight, such as oils and metals.
عددی (adadi): Items sold by count, such as eggs and nuts.
شبھ (shabah): Resemblance; in this context, the mixed commodity resembles both thaman and commodity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the mixing of makil/mawzun/adadi items after mixing, whose view is considered Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) Abu Yusuf.
B) Muhammad.
C) Both agree.
D) None of the above.

Key Takeaway
After mixing same-genus makil/mawzun/adadi items, the mufta bihi (Abu Yusuf) holds that only shirkat al-milk exists, so any unequal profit-sharing condition is invalid.

Shirkah — Partnership

6 min
Hila for Partnership with 'Urud (Non-Monetary Goods)
Providing a legal stratagem to form partnership with goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hila for entering a partnership with 'urud and identify the condition required for its validity.

Core Idea
A mutual sale of equal-value goods transforms 'urud into shirkat al-milk, enabling partnership.

In the Hanafi school, 'urud (goods other than gold and silver) cannot serve as capital in a contractual partnership (shirkat al-aqd). However, if two parties wish to pool their goods, a legal stratagem (hila) is available: they first exchange half of each other's goods via a mutual sale, thereby creating joint ownership, then they contract a partnership over this jointly owned property. This lesson unpacks the conditions and reasoning behind this hila.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibition
Understand that 'urud cannot be capital in shirkat al-aqd because they are not thaman (price). This creates a need for a stratagem.
2
State the hila steps
Each partner sells half of his goods to the other for half of the other's goods. This creates joint ownership (shirkat al-milk).
3
Classify the resulting partnership
The resulting partnership is shirkat al-milk (partnership of ownership), not shirkat al-aqd (contractual partnership).
4
Identify the condition
The hila is valid only if the values of the two goods are equal. This ensures the mutual sale is fair and not usurious.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسباب میں شرکت مفاوضہ کے جواز کا حیلہ
قَالَ وَإِذَا أَرَادَ الشّرْكَةَ بِالْعَرُوضِ بَاعَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا نِصْفَ مَالِهِ بِنِصْفِ مَالِ الْآخِرِ ثُمَّ عَقَدَ الشَّرْكَةَ قَالَ وَهَذِهِ شِرْكَةُ مِلْكِ لِمَابَيَّنَا أَنَّ الْعَرُوضَ لَا تَصِحُ رَأسَ مَالِ الشَّرْكَةِ وَتَأْوِيلُهُ إِذَا كَانَ قِيْمَةٌ مَتَا عِهِمَا عَلَى السَّوَاءِ
Stratagem for the validity of partnership with goods (urud). He said: And if he intends partnership with goods, each of them sells half of his property for half of the other's property, then he contracts the partnership. He said: And this is a partnership of ownership (shirkat al-milk) because we have explained that goods are not valid as capital of partnership. And its interpretation is when the value of their goods is equal.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement presenting a legal stratagem (hila) to enter into a valid partnership when the capital consists of 'urud (goods other than gold and silver, such as furniture, cloth, etc.). Since the Hanafi school holds that 'urud cannot be capital in a contractual partnership (shirkat al-aqd) because they are not thaman, the stratagem works as follows: each partner sells half of his goods to the other in exchange for half of the other's goods (a mutual sale). This transforms their respective ownership into a joint ownership (shirkat al-milk) of the combined goods. Then they formally contract a partnership (shirkat al-milk) over this jointly owned property. The text emphasizes that this is a partnership of ownership, not a contractual one. The condition for the stratagem to work is that the values of both partners' goods are equal (yuhawiyyat al-sawa'). If they are not equal, the hila would not be valid because the mutual sale would involve an exchange of unequal values. This hila is a practical solution to engage in partnership with non-monetary assets while adhering to the rules of the madhhab.

Key Terms
حیلہ (hila): Legal stratagem to achieve a permissible outcome despite apparent prohibition.
عروض ('urud): Goods other than gold and silver, such as furniture and cloth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition is required for the hila of partnership with 'urud to be valid?
A) The goods must be of the same genus.
B) The values of the two goods must be equal.
C) The partners must mix the goods first.
D) The goods must be measured by weight.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hila for partnership with 'urud requires a mutual sale of equal-value halves, resulting in shirkat al-milk, not a contractual partnership.

Dispute on Validity of Mufawadah with Commodities
Discusses intra-Hanafi dispute on partnership in commodities after mixing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the validity of Shirkat al-Mufawadah after mixing commodities, and explain how the dispute affects profit distribution in such partnerships.

Core Idea
Mixing mithli goods after contract allows a valid partnership per Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf holds it remains shirkat al-milk; the Zahir al-Riwayah follows Abu Yusuf.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute about the nature of commodities as capital in a Mufawadah partnership. While all Hanafis agree that unmixed commodities cannot form such a partnership, a disagreement arises when partners mix their goods first and then agree to a partnership. The disagreement between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad turns on whether mixed mithli goods can become thaman (price) and thus valid capital. Understanding this dispute requires examining the dual nature of mithli goods and the distinction between contractual partnership (shirkat al-'aqd) and partnership of ownership (shirkat al-milk).

Guided Path
1
State the undisputed ruling
Identify what all Hanafi scholars agree upon: before mixing, commodities cannot be capital for Mufawadah; each partner's profit and loss belong exclusively to his own goods.
This is the starting point of the passage.
2
Identify the point of disagreement
The disagreement concerns what happens after the partners physically mix their goods of the same type (mithli) and then form a contract. Does this create a valid contractual partnership?
The dispute is between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, with Malik also mentioned as agreeing with Muhammad on one point.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Abu Yusuf holds that even after mixing, the goods become specified by determination (ta'yin) and thus retain their original ownership. Therefore, the partnership is only one of ownership, not a contractual partnership. He cites that the goods remain mithli and can be identified even after mixing.
This is declared Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Analyze Muhammad's position and proof
Muhammad argues that mithli goods have a dual nature: they can be thaman (price) in one respect and mabi' (sold commodity) in another. After mixing, they become thaman, allowing a valid contractual partnership. He uses the example that such goods can be sold on credit, indicating they function as price.
Muhammad's view applies only when the goods are of the same type and are mithli.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical consequence: if unequal profit distribution is stipulated, Abu Yusuf invalidates the partnership (each gets profit from his own goods), while Muhammad validates it. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Yusuf's, as it is Zahir al-Riwayah.
The passage also notes that for goods of different types (qimi), even Muhammad agrees the partnership is invalid due to jahalah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشركة
مفاوضہ کے لئے راس المال نہ ہوں گی )۔ اس مسئلہ میں ہمارے علماء کے درمیان کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ جبکہ خلط سے پہلے ہو ۔ یعنی ماں کے ملا دینے سے پہلے شرکت کا عقدان چیزوں پر نہیں ہوسکتا ہے۔
اور دونوں شرکاء میں سے ہر ایک کے سامان کا نفع اس کے لئے مخصوص ہوگا ۔ اور اگر اس میں نقصان ہو تو وہ بھی اسی کا ہوگا ۔ اور اگر دونوں نے اپنا اپنا مال ملا کر ایک کر دیا اور پھر اسکے شرکت کے معاملہ کو طے کیا تو بھی امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک یہی حکم ہوگا ۔ یہ شرکت ملک کہلائے گی ۔ یعنی دونوں کی ملکیت آپس میں ملی ہوئی ہے۔ اس لئے یہ شرکت عقد نہ ہوگی ۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک شرکت عقد بھی صحیح ہے۔ اس اختلاف کا نتیجہ اس شکل میں ظاہر ہوگا کہ دونوں شر کا ء کا مال آپس میں برابر ہولیکن نفع میں ایک کے لئے کچھ زیادہ اور دوسرے کے لئے کچھ کم ہونے کی شرط لگائی گئی ہو۔ مثلاً ایک کے لئے نفع میں دو تہائی اور دوسرے کے لئے ایک تہائی ہونے کی شرط لگائی گئی ہو تو امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک یہ شرکت جائز نہ ہوگی بلکہ ہر ایک کو اسی کے مال کا نفع ملے گا اور یہی ظاہر الروایہ ہے کیونکہ یہ مال ملا دینے کے بعد بھی معین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتا ہے۔ جیسے ملانے سے پہلے متعین ہو جاتا ہے اور مام حمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایسا مال ایک اعتبار سے شمن ہے یہاں تک کہ اس کے عوض میں اپنے ذمہ قرض رکھ کر بیچ کرنا جائز ہے ( مثلاً کسی شخص نے کسی سے کوئی چیز مرغی کے دس انڈوں یا پانچ سیر گیہوں یا تین سیر لوہے کے عوض خریدی اس طرح پر کہ یہ انڈے یا گیہوں یا لوہا مشتری کے ذمہ ادھار ہے تو یہ قرض جائز ہوا اس بناء پر یہ چیزیں شمن ہوں گی ۔ ) اور دوسرے اعتبار سے یہی چیزیں بیچ ہیں۔ کہ معین کرنے سے یہ متعین بھی ہو جاتی ہیں۔ پس ان میں دوہری مشابہت ہوئی ۔ اس لئے ہم نے دونوں مشابہتوں پر عمل کیا یہ کہہ کر ملانے سے پہلے ان کو مبیع کہا اور یہ کہ اس میں شرکت جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور ملانے کے بعد ان کو شمن قرار دیا اور یہ کہ ان میں شرکت جائز ہے۔ بخلاف دوسرے اسباب ( مثلا تخت و کرسی و صندوق وغیرہ کے کہ یہ چیزیں کسی حال میں بھی ثمن نہیں بن سکتی ہیں۔ (پھر اختلاف کی یہ صورتیں اس وقت ہیں جبکہ وہ کیلی و وزنی و عددی دونوں کے پاس ایک ہی جنس کی ہوں) کیونکہ اگر دونوں کی جنس مختلف ہو جیسے ایک کے پاس گیہوں اور دوسرے کے پاس جو ہوں یا ایک کے پاس روغن زیتون اور دوسرے کے پاس گھی ہو۔ پھر اگر دونوں نے سب مال ملا دیا تو بھی بالا تفاق عقد شرکت نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ امام مالک رحمتہ اللہ علیہ و امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ بھی اس پر متفق ہیں (پس امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک ایک جنس ہونے سے خلط کے بعد شرکت جائز ہے۔ لیکن مختلف جنس ہونے سے جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس میں فرق یہ ہے کہ ایک ہی جنس کے مخلوط ہو جانے سے وہ پشنی مشکلی چیزوں میں سے ہے ۔ یعنی اگر کوئی شخص اسے برباد کر دے تو اس کی جیسی مثلی چیز اس کا قائم مقام ہو سکتی ہے اور دو جنسوں کی ملی ہوئی مخلوط چیز مشکلی نہیں بلکہ قیمتی ( قیمت والی ) ہے اس کے برباد کر دینے والے پر اس کا مثل نہیں بلکہ اس کی قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اس بناء پر اس میں جہالت پیدا ہو گئی۔ (یعنی ہر شریک کو اس کی تقسیم کے وقت اس کا اصل مال مل سکتا ہے جیسے اسباب میں ہوتا ہے)۔ اور جب شرکت صحیح نہ ہوئی تو خلط کا جو حکم ہے وہ ہم نے کتاب القضاء میں بیان کیا ہے۔ بلکہ کتاب الود یعت میں بیان کیا ہے ) الغایہ یا کفایۃ المنتہی میں ملاخط ہو ۔
Book of Partnership. For Mufawadah, capital cannot be goods. In this issue there is no disagreement among our scholars when before mixing. That is, before mixing the goods, a partnership contract cannot be made on these things. And the profit of each partner's goods belongs specifically to him, and if there is loss, it also belongs to him. And if both mix their goods together and then settle the partnership matter, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, the same ruling applies. This is called partnership of ownership, i.e., their ownership is intermixed. Therefore, it is not a contractual partnership. According to Imam Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, the contractual partnership is also valid. The result of this difference appears in the form that both partners' goods are equal to each other, but profit is stipulated more for one and less for the other. For example, if profit is stipulated as two-thirds for one and one-third for the other, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf, this partnership is not valid; rather, each gets profit from his own goods, and this is Zahir al-Riwayah, because these goods, even after mixing, become specified by determination, just as they become specified before mixing. Imam Muhammad's proof is that such goods, in one respect, are thaman (price), to the extent that it is permissible to sell something on credit in exchange for them (e.g., a person buys something from someone in exchange for ten eggs of a hen, or five seers of wheat, or three seers of iron, on condition that these eggs, wheat, or iron are a debt on the buyer; this loan is valid because these things are thaman). And in another respect, these same things are mabi' (sold commodity), because they become specific by determination. Thus, they have a dual resemblance. So we acted on both resemblances: before mixing we called them mabi' and said partnership is not valid in them; after mixing we considered them thaman and said partnership is valid in them. Unlike other goods (e.g., bed, chair, chest, etc.) which can never become thaman. Then, these forms of difference apply when the goods are of the same type, measurable, weighable, or countable, present with both, because if the type is different—e.g., one has wheat and the other barley, or one has olive oil and the other ghee—then even if both mix all goods, according to consensus, a partnership contract cannot be concluded, to the extent that Imam Malik and Imam Muhammad also agree on this. So according to Imam Muhammad, partnership after mixing is valid if the type is the same, but not if the type is different. The difference is that when goods of the same type are mixed, they become from among mithli items; i.e., if a person destroys them, a similar mithli thing can substitute for them. But a mixture of two different types is not mithli but qimi (value-based); upon the destroyer, the like is not obligatory, but its value is obligatory. On this basis, ignorance (jahalah) arises. (i.e., each partner at the time of division can get his original goods, as happens with goods). And when the partnership is not valid, the ruling of mixing is what we stated in Kitab al-Qada, rather in Kitab al-Wadi'ah. Check in al-Ghayah or Kifayat al-Muntaha.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage opens with the ruling on Shirkat al-Mufawadah (partnership of investment) when the capital consists of commodities (urud) rather than cash. The passage first establishes that before any mixing of goods, there is no dispute: partnership cannot be formed with commodities as capital. Each partner retains exclusive rights to profit and loss from his own goods. The central dispute arises when the partners first mix their goods and then agree to a partnership. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that even after mixing, the partnership is not a contractual partnership (shirkat al-'aqd) but merely a partnership of ownership (shirkat al-milk); therefore, if they stipulate unequal profit shares, it is invalid because each partner's share remains tied to his original property. Imam Muhammad holds that after mixing, the goods become thaman (price) and thus can serve as capital for a valid contractual partnership, allowing unequal profit shares. The passage then delves into the reasoning: goods like wheat, eggs, etc. have a dual nature—they can be thaman in one context (e.g., as a price for a debt) and mabi' (sold commodity) in another. This dual resemblance permits valid partnership after mixing. Conversely, items like furniture can never be thaman and thus cannot form partnership capital even after mixing. The discussion further distinguishes between mithli (fungible) goods of the same type, which can be mixed to form a valid partnership, and qimi (non-fungible) goods of different types, which cannot, because mixing different types introduces ignorance (jahalah) about each partner's exact share. The passage concludes by referring to other books for rulings on mixing when partnership is invalid. The Zahir al-Riwayah position is that of Imam Abu Yusuf, as explicitly stated.

Key Terms
شركة المفاوضة (shirkat al-mufawadah): A partnership where both partners invest equal capital and have equal authority to act, with mutual agency and suretyship.
خلط (khalṭ): Physical mixing of goods belonging to different partners so that they become indistinguishable.
ثمن (thaman): Price; used as capital in partnership; includes cash and fungible goods that can serve as price in a sale.
مثلی (mithlī): Fungible goods for which substitute of the same type and quality exists (e.g., wheat, eggs).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the Zahir al-Riwayah position on the validity of Shirkat al-Mufawadah when partners mix their goods before forming the contract?
A) It is valid as a contractual partnership with equal profit.
B) It is valid only if the goods are of the same type.
C) It is not valid as a contractual partnership; it is merely a partnership of ownership.
D) It is valid regardless of the type of goods.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi Mufawadah, commodities cannot serve as capital; after mixing, only mithli goods of the same type can potentially become capital, but the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) from Abu Yusuf holds that even then, the partnership remains one of ownership, not contract.

Shirkah — Partnership
beginner

Legal Stratagem for Partnership in Commodities (Hila)
Provides a hila for valid partnership in commodities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the steps of the Hanafi legal stratagem for forming a valid partnership using commodities (urud) and apply it to cases of equal and unequal values.

Core Idea
Commodities cannot be partnership capital; sell half to each other first to convert them into thaman.

This lesson presents a classic Hanafi hila (legal stratagem) that allows two parties to form a valid partnership when their capital consists of commodities. By first exchanging halves of their goods, they transform the capital into thaman (price), making the subsequent partnership contract valid. The conditions for this stratagem are precise, especially when the values are unequal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Understand why commodities cannot directly serve as partnership capital in Hanafi law. The capital for a valid partnership must be in the form of thaman (currency or fungible items) to avoid uncertainty (gharar).
This is a key principle from earlier discussions in the text.
2
Describe the Basic Hila
Each partner sells half of his goods to the other in exchange for half of the other's goods. This transfers ownership such that the commodities become thaman (price) owned by the other party.
The sale must be a valid contract with offer and acceptance.
3
Resulting Ownership
After the exchange, each partner owns half of the combined goods. The partnership formed is shirkat al-milk (partnership of ownership) because the mixing occurred through sale, not through a contractual partnership.
Shirkat al-milk is distinct from shirkat al-‘aqd (contractual partnership).
4
Handle Unequal Values
If the values of the goods are unequal, the partner with lesser value must sell a portion of his goods to the other to equalize the shares. The proportion sold should be such that the total shares after mixing reflect the original value ratio.
Example: 400 and 100 dirhams → lesser partner sells 4/5 of his goods for 1/5 of the other’s, making total shares 5, with lesser owning 1/5.
5
Apply to a Given Scenario
Given two sets of commodity values, compute the sale required and then the profit-sharing ratio. Practice with the provided example.
Profit is shared according to ownership shares after the exchange.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسباب میں شرکت مفاوضہ کے جواز کا حیلہ
قَالَ وَإِذَا أَرَادَ الشّرْكَةَ بِالْعَرُوضِ بَاعَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا نِصْفَ مَالِهِ بِنِصْفِ مَالِ الْآخِرِ ثُمَّ عَقَدَ الشَّرْكَةَ قَالَ وَهَذِهِ شِرْكَةُ مِلْكِ لِمَابَيَّنَا أَنَّ الْعَرُوضَ لَا تَصِحُ رَأسَ مَالِ الشَّرْكَةِ وَتَأْوِيلُهُ إِذَا كَانَ قِيْمَةٌ مَتَا عِهِمَا عَلَى السَّوَاءِ
ترجمہ اور جب کوئی شخص کسی کے ساتھ اسباب میں شرکت کا معاملہ کرنا چاہے تو ہر ایک شخص اپنے آدھے مال کو دوسرے کے آدھے مال کے عوض فروخت کر دے اس کے بعد عقد شرکت طے کرے ۔ مصنف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ یہ شرکت ملک کی ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ ہم نے یہ بتا دیا ہے کہ شرکت کا راس المال یہ اسباب نہیں ہوسکتا ہے۔ اور جو مسئلہ ابھی مذکور ہوا اس کی تاویل یہ ہے کہ دونوں کے اسباب کی قیمت برابر ہو۔ اور اگر قیمت میں فرق یعنی کمی اور زیادتی ہو تو کم قیمت والا اپنے مال میں سے دوسرے کے اسباب سے اسی فرق کے اندازہ کے عوض فروخت کر دے ۔ تاکہ شرکت ثابت ہو جائے ( ۔ مثلاً اس شریک کے اسباب کی قیمت چار سو درہم اور دوسرے کے اسباب کی قیمت صرف ایک سو درہم ہوں۔ تو دوسرا شخص اپنے اسباب کے پانچ حصوں میں سے چار حصے دوسرے کے پانچویں حصے کے عوض فروخت کر دے۔ اس طرح خلط کر دینے سے کل اسباب کے پانچ حصے ہوں گے ۔ جن میں ایک حصہ کم مال والے کا ہوگا۔ اس لیئے اسے نفع کا بھی پانچواں حصہ ہی ملے گا ؟
Legal Stratagem for Permissibility of Partnership in Commodities. He (al-Quduri) said: And when he desires partnership by means of commodities (urud), each one of them sells half of his goods for half of the goods of the other, then he makes the partnership contract. He said: This is a partnership of ownership (shirkat milk) because we have explained that commodities cannot be capital for partnership. Its interpretation is when the value of their goods is equal. And if there is a difference between them, the one with less sells from his goods to the other to the extent that establishes partnership. Translation: And when a person wants to transact partnership in goods with someone, each person sells half of his goods in exchange for half of the other's goods, then makes the partnership contract. The author (al-Quduri) said: This will be a partnership of ownership, because we have explained that goods cannot be the capital of partnership. And the interpretation of the issue just mentioned is that the value of both's goods should be equal. And if there is a difference in value, i.e., decrease or increase, then the one with lower value sells from his goods to the other's goods to the measure of that difference, so that partnership is established. For example, one partner's goods are worth four hundred dirhams, and the other's only one hundred dirhams. Then the latter sells four-fifths of his goods in exchange for one-fifth of the other's. Thus, by mixing, total goods become five shares, among which one share belongs to the one with less. Hence, he will get only one-fifth of the profit.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage presents a legal stratagem (hila) for forming a partnership when the available capital consists of commodities, which cannot directly serve as partnership capital in Shirkat al-Mufawadah according to the Hanafi school. The method: each partner sells half of his goods to the other in exchange for half of the other's goods. This sale transforms the commodities into thaman (price) because they are now owned by the other partner as consideration for the sale. After this exchange, the partners own half of each other's goods; then they can form a partnership contract. The resulting partnership is characterized as shirkat al-milk (partnership of ownership) because the ownership is intermixed through the exchange, not through the partnership contract itself. The author notes that this stratagem works when the values of the goods are equal. If values are unequal, the partner with lesser value must sell enough of his goods to the other to equalize the values before forming the partnership. An example is given: if one has goods worth 400 dirhams and the other worth 100, the latter sells 4/5 of his goods to the former for 1/5 of the former's goods, making total shares 5, with the poorer partner owning 1/5. Then profit is shared proportionally. This hila ensures that the commodities are no longer 'commodities' in the legal sense for the partnership capital, but rather each partner's contribution is now in thaman (exchange value).

Key Terms
حيلة (ḥīlah): A legal stratagem or indirect method to achieve a permissible end while adhering to the letter of the law, here used to form a valid partnership with commodities.
شركة ملك (shirkat al-milk): Partnership of ownership where property is jointly owned without a contractual partnership agreement; here resulting from the sale-exchange.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the legal stratagem for partnership in commodities, what must each partner do before forming the partnership contract?
A) Deposit their goods with a trusted third party.
B) Sell half of their goods to the other partner in exchange for half of the other's goods.
C) Convert their goods into cash by selling them in the market.
D) Appoint each other as agents (wakil) for mutual trading.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi legal stratagem for partnership in commodities involves a sale-exchange to convert goods into valid capital, ensuring the partnership is sound.

Definition of Shirkat al-'Inan and Its Basis on Wakala
Defines Shirkat al-'Inan as a partnership based on agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Shirkat al-'Inan and explain why it is based on wakala rather than kafala.

Core Idea
Shirkat al-'Inan is a partnership founded on mutual agency, not suretyship — each partner acts as agent, not guarantor.

This lesson introduces Shirkat al-'Inan, the second major type of partnership in Hanafi fiqh. Understanding its foundation on wakala (agency) is essential for distinguishing it from Shirkat al-Mufawadah and for correctly applying its rulings. The text from al-Quduri provides both the definition and a linguistic reasoning rooted in the word 'inan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type
Recognize that the passage defines Shirkat al-'Inan, one of the two main partnership types in Hanafi law.
The other type is Mufawadah (general partnership with mutual suretyship).
2
State its basis
Note that the contract is concluded on wakala (agency) and not on kafala (suretyship). This is the defining feature.
Partners act as agents for each other but do not guarantee each other's liabilities.
3
Understand the scope
The partnership may be limited to a specific type of trade (e.g., cloth or food) or general in all trades.
The partners do not mention kafala in their agreement.
4
Examine the linguistic proof
The word 'inan is derived from 'i'rad (turning away), implying no liability for the other. This negates kafala.
The phrase 'anna lahu means 'he turned away from him'.
5
Apply the principle
Rulings cannot contradict the linguistic meaning of the contract name. Thus, 'Inan cannot include kafala.
This is a classic Hanafi usul principle: al-hukm yadurr ma'a al-'illah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرکت معنان کی تعریف
قَالَ وَأَمَّاشِرُكَةُ الْعَنَانِ فَتَنْعَقِدُ عَلَى الْوَكَالَةِ دُونَ الْكَفَالَةِ وَهِي أَنْ تَشْتَرِكَ إِثْنَانِ فِي نَوْعِ بُرَا وَطَعَامٍ أَو يَشْتَرِك في عُمُومِ التِّجَارَاتِ وَلَا يَذْكُرَانِ الْكَفَالَةَ وَإِنْعِقَادُهُ عَلَى الْوَكَالَةِ لِتَحَقَّقِ مَقْصُودِهِ كَمَا بَيَّنَّاهُ وَلَا يَنعَقِدُ عَلَى الْكَفَالَةِ لِأَنَّ اللَّفْظَ مُشْتَقٌ مِنَ الْإِعْرَاضِ يُقَالُ عَنَّ لَهُ أَى أَعْرَضَ وَهَذا لا ينهى عَنِ الْكَفَالَةِ وَحُكْمُ التصرف لَا يَنْتُ بِخِلَافَ مُقْتَضَى اللَّفْظِ
ترجمه قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے عقد شرکت کی دوسری قسم عنان کے بارے میں فرمایا کہ وہ وکالت پر منعقد ہوتی ہے۔ اور کفالت پر منعقد نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اس طور سے کہ دو شخص کپڑے یا غلہ کی تجارت میں شرکت کریں یا عموماً ہر قسم کی تجارت میں شرکت کریں اور کفالت کا ذکر نہ کریں ۔ اس میں وکالت پر انعقاد اس لئے ہے کہ شرکت کا مقصود حاصل ہو جائے ۔ جیسا کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں لیکن یہ کفالت سے منعقد نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ عنان کے معنی ہیں منہ موڑنا ۔ محاورہ میں بولا جاتا ہے عَن لَہ ۔ جبکہ کسی سے منہ موڑا ہو۔ اس ترجمہ سے کفالت کا پایا جانا بالکل ظاہر نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اور لفظ کے مقتضاء کے خلاف کوئی حکم ثابت نہیں ہوتا ہے۔
Definition of Shirkat al-'Inan. He said: As for Shirkat al-'Inan, it is concluded on the basis of agency (wakala) not suretyship (kafala). It is that two persons partner in a type of cloth or food, or they partner in general trades, and they do not mention suretyship. Its conclusion on agency is for the fulfillment of its purpose, as we have explained. And it is not concluded on kafala because the word is derived from 'i'rad (turning away). It is said: 'anna lahu' meaning he turned away from him. This does not indicate kafala. And the ruling of actions does not proceed contrary to the requirement of the word. Translation: Al-Quduri, may Allah have mercy on him, said regarding the second type of partnership contract, 'Inan, that it is concluded on wakala and not on kafala. In the manner that two persons partner in the trade of cloth or grain, or they partner in all kinds of trade, and they do not mention kafala. Its conclusion on wakala is so that the purpose of partnership is achieved, as we have explained. But it is not concluded on kafala because the meaning of 'inan is turning away. In idiom, it is said 'anna lahu' when one turns away from someone. From this translation, the presence of kafala is not apparent at all. And no ruling can be established contrary to the requirement of the word.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage defines Shirkat al-'Inan, the second major type of partnership in the Hanafi school. The defining characteristic is that it is based on mutual agency (wakala), not on mutual suretyship (kafala). That means each partner is an agent for the other in making purchases and sales, but neither guarantees the other's transactions beyond the capital invested. The partnership can be limited to a specific trade (e.g., cloth or grain) or general in all types of trade. The author provides a linguistic reasoning: the word 'inan derives from 'i'rad (turning away), as in the phrase 'anna lahu (he turned away from him), which does not convey the idea of guarantee or responsibility for another's liability. Therefore, the contract of 'Inan cannot include kafala because that would contradict the inherent meaning of the term. This distinction is crucial because in Mufawadah, both agency and suretyship are present. In 'Inan, only agency exists. The practical consequence is that in 'Inan, partners are not liable for each other's debts beyond the partnership capital.

Key Terms
شركة عنان (shirkat al-‘inān): A partnership where partners contribute capital and work together, with mutual agency for trade but no mutual suretyship.
وكالة (wakālah): Agency; each partner acts as agent for the other in commercial transactions within the scope of the partnership.
كفالة (kafālah): Suretyship; guaranteeing another's liability which is present in Mufawadah but absent in 'Inan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is Shirkat al-'Inan not concluded on the basis of kafala (suretyship)?
A) Because kafala is forbidden in all partnerships.
B) Because the word 'inan is derived from 'i'rad (turning away), which does not imply suretyship.
C) Because the partners must explicitly exclude kafala in the contract.
D) Because kafala would make the partnership invalid.

Key Takeaway
Shirkat al-'Inan is a valid Hanafi partnership based solely on mutual agency, not suretyship, as affirmed by the linguistic derivation of its name.

Inequality of Capital and Profit in 'Inan Partnership
States Hanafi validity of unequal capital/profit, rebuts Zufar/Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on unequal profit shares in 'Inan, identify the opposing position, and explain the Hanafi proof from hadith and analogy to mudarabah.

Core Idea
Profit in 'Inan can be divided by agreement, not only by capital proportion.

In Shirkat al-'Inan, a common question is whether partners must have equal capital and profit shares. The Hanafi school permits both unequal capital and unequal profit by mutual agreement. This lesson examines the ruling, the objection raised by Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i, and the Hanafi response based on a prophetic hadith and the analogy of mudarabah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State the Hanafi position: it is valid (ja'iz) for partners in 'Inan to have unequal capital and/or unequal profit.
The matn explicitly states this.
2
Locate the dissenting view
Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold it invalid if profit exceeds capital proportion.
Zufar is a Hanafi scholar who disagreed on this point.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
Their argument: profit should correspond to ownership/guarantee; excess profit is like profit on unguaranteed wealth.
They require mixing of capital to establish joint ownership.
4
Examine the Hanafi dalil
Hadith: 'Profit is according to their stipulation, loss according to capital.' Also, profit can be earned through labor (mudarabah).
The hadith is clear and does not restrict the stipulation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi allows any profit split by agreement; Shafi'i restricts to proportional.
This affects many business arrangements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرکت عنان میں مال اور منافع میں تساوی ضروری ہے
وَيَصِحُ التَّفَاضُلُ فِى الْمَالِ لِحَاجَةٍ إِلَيْهِ وَلَيْسَ مِنْ فَضَّيَّةِ اللَّفْظِ الْمَسَاوَاةِ وَيَصحُ أنْ يَتَسَاوَيَا فِى الْمَال و يَتَفَاضَلَا فِي الربْحِ وَقَالَ زُفَرَ وَالشَّافِعِي لَا يَجُوزُ لِأَنَّ التَّفَاضُلَ فِيهِ يُؤَدِّى إلى رِبْحِ مَالَمْ يَضْمَن فَإِنَّ الْمَالَ إِذَا كَانَ يَصْفَيْنِ وَالرِّبْحُ أَثْلَاثًا فَصَاحِبُ الزِيَادَةِ يَسْتَحِقَّهَا بِلَاضَمَانِ إِذِ الصَّمَانُ بِقَدْرِ رَأسِ الْمَالِ وَلأنَّ الشَّرُكَة عِندَهُما في الربح لشركَةٍ فِى الأَصل وَلِهَذَا يَشْتَرِ طَانِ الْخَلْطَ فَصَارَ رِيحُ الْمَالِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ بِمَاءِ الْأَعْيَانِ فَيَسْتَحِقُ بِقَدْرِ الْمِلْكِ فِي الْأَصْلِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ الرِّبْحُ عَلَى مَاشَرَ طَاوَ الْوَضِعَةُ عَلَى قَدْرِ الْمَالين وَلَمْ يُفَضِّل شَرَطَ وَلِأَنَّ الرِّبْحَ كَمَا يُسْتَحَقُّ بِالْمَالِ يُسْتَحَقِّ بِالْعَمَلِ كَمَا فِى الْمُصَارَبَةِ وَ قَدْ يَكُونُ أَحَدُهُمَا أَحْدَقَ وَأَهْدَى أو
Necessity of equality in capital and profit in 'Inan partnership. And it is valid to have difference in capital due to need for it, and it is not from the excessiveness of the word that equality [is required]. And it is valid that they be equal in capital and differ in profit. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible, because difference in it leads to profit of wealth not guaranteed. For when the capital is halves and profit is thirds, the one with increase deserves it without guarantee, for guarantee is according to the capital. And because, according to them, partnership in profit is due to partnership in the original [capital], and therefore they require mixing. So profit of wealth becomes like the growth of assets, and one deserves according to ownership in the original. And we have the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Profit is according to what they stipulate, and loss is according to the capital.' And he did not make the stipulation an extra. And because profit, just as it is earned through capital, is also earned through labor, as in mudarabah. And one of them may be more skilled and more guided... [text cuts off]
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage addresses a key ruling in Shirkat al-'Inan: whether partners must have equal capital and equal profit shares. The Hanafi position, as stated by al-Quduri, is that it is valid for partners to contribute unequal capital (e.g., one more than the other) and also to agree on unequal profit shares, even if capital is equal. The text first states that difference in capital is permissible due to need (e.g., one partner may have more resources) and that the word 'Inan does not require equality. Then it notes that even if capital is equal, profit may be divided unequally. This is opposed by Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i, who argue that any excess profit beyond the capital proportion is akin to earning profit on wealth one did not guarantee (since guarantee is only to the extent of capital). They argue that profit should follow ownership: if capital is half, profit should be half, not one-third. They require mixing of capital to ensure joint ownership. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, a hadith of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) is cited: 'Profit is according to what they stipulate, and loss is according to the capital.' This hadith grants partners the freedom to agree on profit shares by mutual consent, as long as loss is borne proportionate to capital. Second, profit can be earned through labor (as in mudarabah), so a partner who is more skilled or contributes more effort can legitimately receive a larger share of profit even if capital contribution is smaller. The Hanafi school thus upholds contractual freedom within the limits of fairness.

Key Terms
تفاضل (tafāḍul): Difference or inequality in capital contribution or profit share between partners.
مضاربة (muḍārabah): A partnership where one provides capital and the other labor, and profit is shared according to agreement. Used as analogy for 'Inan.
ضمان (ḍamān): Guarantee; liability for loss; in partnership, each partner's guarantee is limited to his capital investment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith do the Hanafis use to justify unequal profit shares in Shirkat al-'Inan?
A) 'The trust is on the one who is trusted.'
B) 'Profit is according to what they stipulate, and loss is according to the capital.'
C) 'The partners are in profit and loss together.'
D) 'There is no partnership except with mixing.'

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, partners in 'Inan may freely agree on profit shares, as supported by hadith and analogy to mudarabah.

Definition and Nature of Shirkat al-‘Inan
Definition of Shirkat al-‘Inan and its basis on wakalah, not kafalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Shirkat al-‘Inan and explain its legal basis on wakalah without kafalah.

Core Idea
Shirkat al-‘Inan is a partnership based on mutual agency, not suretyship.

What exactly is Shirkat al-‘Inan? This lesson unpacks its definition and legal foundation. Understanding this distinction is crucial because it determines the extent of liability between partners. The passage from Al-Hidayah lays out the core principle: it is founded on agency (wakalah) alone, not on suretyship (kafalah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Name the contract being defined: Shirkat al-‘Inan. The ruling is that it is a valid (sahih) contract.
The passage opens with 'He said: As for Shirkat al-‘Inan...'
2
Locate the legal basis
Find the statement that the contract is concluded on wakalah, not kafalah. This is the core legal nature.
The text explicitly says 'it is concluded on the basis of agency (wakalah) without suretyship (kafalah).'
3
Understand the linguistic derivation
The author explains that the word 'inan comes from 'i'rad (turning away), implying independence. Each partner is not bound by the other's obligations beyond agency.
Linguistic analysis reinforces the legal structure.
4
Apply the distinction
Recognize that because the contract is based on wakalah, partners are agents for each other but not guarantors. This affects liability.
Contrast with Shirkat al-Mufawadah, which includes kafalah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَأَمَّا شِرُكَةُ الْعَنَانِ فَتَنْعَقِدُ عَلَى الْوَكَالَةِ دُونَ الْكَفَالَةِ وَهِيَ أَنْ يَشْتَرِكَ اثْنَانِ فِي نَوْعٍ مِنَ الْبُرِّ وَالطَّعَامِ أَوْ يَشْتَرِكَا فِي عُمُومِ التِّجَارَاتِ وَلَا يَذْكُرَانِ الْكَفَالَةَ وَانْعِقَادُهُ عَلَى الْوَكَالَةِ لِتَحَقُّقِ مَقْصُودِهِ كَمَا بَيَّنَّاهُ وَلَا يَنْعَقِدُ عَلَى الْكَفَالَةِ لِأَنَّ اللَّفْظَ مُشْتَقٌ مِنَ الْإِعْرَاضِ يُقَالُ عَنَّ لَهُ أَيْ أَعْرَضَ وَهَذَا لَا يَنْهَى عَنِ الْكَفَالَةِ وَحُكْمُ التَّصَرُّفِ لَا يَثْبُتُ بِخِلَافِ مُقْتَضَى اللَّفْظِ
He said: As for Shirkat al-‘Inan, it is concluded on the basis of agency (wakalah) without suretyship (kafalah). It is that two persons enter into partnership in a type of wheat or food, or in general trades, and they do not mention kafalah. It is concluded on wakalah to achieve its purpose, as we have explained. It is not concluded on kafalah because the word is derived from turning away; it is said 'anna lahu' meaning 'he turned away', and this does not prohibit kafalah, and the ruling of a disposition does not establish contrary to the import of the word.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage defines the second type of partnership in Hanafi fiqh: Shirkat al-‘Inan. It clarifies the legal nature: it is based on mutual agency (wakalah), meaning each partner acts as an agent for the other in trade, but they are not guarantors for each other's liabilities (kafalah). The author explains the linguistic derivation: 'inan comes from 'i'rad (turning away), implying that each partner has the freedom to act independently within the scope of the agency. The ruling is that since the contract is founded on agency, the partners do not bear joint liability beyond their own actions. This distinguishes it from Shirkat al-Mufawadah, which includes elements of both agency and suretyship.

Key Terms
شركة العنان (shirkat al-‘inān): A limited partnership where each partner is an agent for the other but not a guarantor.
وكالة (wakālah): Agency, a contract where one person authorizes another to act on his behalf.
كفالة (kafālah): Suretyship, a contract where one person guarantees the obligation of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal basis of Shirkat al-‘Inan according to the Hanafi school?
A) Kafalah (suretyship) only.
B) Both wakalah and kafalah.
C) Wakalah (agency) without kafalah.
D) Neither wakalah nor kafalah.

Key Takeaway
Shirkat al-‘Inan is a partnership founded on mutual agency, not suretyship; partners are not liable for each other's debts.

Disparity in Capital and Profit in Shirkat al-‘Inan
Hanafi ruling and dispute on permissible inequality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on disparity in capital and profit in Shirkat al-‘Inan, identify the opposing view, and apply the key textual evidence.

Core Idea
Profit shares are based on mutual agreement, not solely on capital proportion — a partnership can be unequal.

This passage delves into a key question in partnership law: Must profit shares always match capital contributions? The Hanafi school says no, allowing flexibility based on mutual agreement and labor. Imams Zufar and al-Shafi'i disagree. Let's explore the proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify that the Hanafi school permits disparity in capital and also disparity in profit even if capital is equal.
2
Identify the opposing view
Zufar and al-Shafi'i argue it is invalid because it leads to profit without liability.
3
Examine the opponent's proof
They argue profit should mirror capital and is like growth of assets; mixing of assets is required.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Cite the hadith: 'Profit is according to their stipulation, loss according to capitals.' Also analogy to mudarabah, where profit is earned by labor.
5
Distinguish from extremes
Note that if all profit goes to one party, the contract becomes a loan or consignment, which is invalid. Disparity is within bounds.
