وَيَصِحُ التَّفَاضُلُ فِي الْمَالِ لِحَاجَةٍ إِلَيْهِ وَلَيْسَ مِنْ صَغِيَّةِ اللَّفْظِ الْمُسَاوَاةُ وَيَصِحُ أَنْ يَتَسَاوَيَا فِي الْمَالِ وَيَتَفَاضَلَا فِي الرِّبْحِ وَقَالَ زُفَرُ وَالشَّافِعِي لَا يَجُوزُ لِأَنَّ التَّفَاضُلَ فِيهِ يُؤَدِّي إِلَى رِبْحِ مَا لَمْ يَضْمَن فَإِنَّ الْمَالَ إِذَا كَانَ مِائَتَيْنِ وَالرِّبْحُ أَثْلَاثًا فَصَاحِبُ الزِّيَادَةِ يَسْتَحِقُّهَا بِلَا ضَمَانٍ إِذِ الضَّمَانُ بِقَدْرِ رَأْسِ الْمَالِ وَلِأَنَّ الشَّرِكَةَ عِنْدَهُمَا فِي الرِّبْحِ لِشَرِكَةٍ فِي الْأَصْلِ وَلِهَذَا يَشْتَرِطَانِ الْخَلْطَ فَصَارَ رِبْحُ الْمَالِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ نَمَاءِ الْأَعْيَانِ فَيَسْتَحِقُّ بِقَدْرِ الْمِلْكِ فِي الْأَصْلِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ الرِّبْحُ عَلَى مَا اشْتَرَطَا وَالْوَضِيعَةُ عَلَى قَدْرِ الْمَالَيْنِ وَلَمْ يُفَضِّلْ شَرْطٌ وَلِأَنَّ الرِّبْحَ كَمَا يُسْتَحَقُّ بِالْمَالِ يُسْتَحَقُّ بِالْعَمَلِ كَمَا فِي الْمُضَارَبَةِ وَقَدْ يَكُونُ أَحَدُهُمَا أَحْدَقَ وَأَهْدَى أَوْ أَكْثَرَ عَمَلًا وَأَقْوَى فَلَا يَرْضَى بِالْمُسَاوَاةِ فَمَسَّتِ الْحَاجَةُ إِلَى التَّفَاضُلِ بِخِلَافِ اشْتِرَاطِ جَمِيعِ الرِّبْحِ لِأَحَدِهِمَا لِأَنَّهُ يَخْرُجُ الْعَقْدُ بِهِ مِنَ الشَّرِكَةِ وَمِنَ الْمُضَارَبَةِ أَيْضًا إِلَى قَرْضٍ بِاشْتِرَاطِهِ لِلْعَامِلِ أَوْ إِلَى بِضَاعَةٍ بِاشْتِرَاطِهِ لِرَبِّ الْمَالِ وَهَذَا الْعَقْدُ يَشْبَهُ الْمُضَارَبَةَ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنَّهُ يَعْمَلُ فِي مَالِ الشَّرِيكِ وَيَشْبَهُ الشَّرِكَةَ اسْمًا وَعَمَلًا فَإِنَّهُمَا يَعْمَلَانِ فَعَمِلْنَا فِيهِ الْمُضَارَبَةَ وَقُلْنَا يَصِحُّ اشْتِرَاطُ الرِّبْحِ مِنْ غَيْرِ ضَمَانٍ وَبِشِبْهِ الشَّرِكَةِ حَتَّى لَا يُبْطَلَ بِاشْتِرَاطِ الْعَمَلِ عَلَيْهِمَا
And disparity in capital is permissible due to need, and equality is not a requirement of the word. And it is valid for them to be equal in capital and differ in profit. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: This is not permissible, because disparity in it leads to profit without liability. For if the capital is two hundred and the profit is in thirds, then the owner of the increase receives it without liability, while liability is according to the capital. And also because according to them, partnership in profit is due to partnership in the original capital; for this reason they stipulate mixing (of assets). So profit of the capital becomes like growth of assets, so one deserves according to ownership in the original. Our proof: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Profit is according to what they stipulate, and loss is according to the two capitals.' He did not specify a condition. And also because profit, just as it is earned through capital, is also earned through work, as in mudarabah. And one of them may be more skilled, more guided, or more work and stronger, so he is not satisfied with equality. Thus need arises for disparity. Unlike stipulating all profit for one of them, because that takes the contract out of shirkah and also out of mudarabah into a loan if stipulated for the worker, or into a consignment if stipulated for the capital owner. And this contract resembles mudarabah in that he works with the partner's money, and resembles shirkah in name and work, for both work. So we applied (the ruling of) mudarabah in it and said: stipulating profit without liability is valid, and by the resemblance to shirkah it is not invalidated by stipulating work on both.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed intra- and inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of unequal capital and profit-sharing in Shirkat al-‘Inan. Abu Hanifa (and the Hanafi school) hold that it is permissible: capital may be unequal, and even if capital is equal, profit may be divided disproportionately (e.g., two-thirds for one, one-third for the other). Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i argue it is invalid because such disparity leads to profiting without liability (gharar). They argue that since partnership in profit is based on partnership in the capital itself, profit should be proportional to capital. The Hanafi response cites the hadith: 'Profit is according to their agreement, and loss is according to the capital.' They also present a rational argument: profit is earned both through capital and through labor (as in mudarabah). Since one partner may be more skilled, it is necessary to allow disparity in profit to avoid hardship. The passage also distinguishes this from a contract that allocates all profit to one party, which would be invalid because it transforms the contract into a loan or a mere consignment (bida'ah). The ruling is based on a combination of textual evidence and istihsan (juristic preference).

Key Terms
تفاضل (tafāḍul): Disparity, i.e., inequality in the amount of capital or profit shares.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability, specifically the responsibility for losses proportional to capital.
مضاربة (muḍārabah): A partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, profits shared as agreed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary textual evidence for the Hanafi position allowing disparity in profit beyond the proportion of capital?
A) Quranic verse on justice
B) Hadith: 'Profit is according to what they stipulate, loss according to the capitals'
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy to sale of currency

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, partners may agree to any profit-sharing ratio regardless of capital, based on the hadith and the need to account for labor.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate

Unequal Profit Shares in Shirkat al-‘Inan
Ruling on unequal profit shares with rebuttal of opponents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on unequal profit shares in Shirkat al-‘Inan and evaluate the counter-arguments of Zufar and Shafi‘i.

Core Idea
Profit in partnership is by agreement, not solely by capital – work and skill justify unequal shares.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi position on partnership law: when two partners contribute equal capital, can they agree on unequal profit shares? The Hanafi school permits it, but Imams Zufar and Shafi‘i disagree. We will analyse the proofs on both sides and trace the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Abu Hanifa rules regarding unequal profit shares when capital is equal.
The ruling is that it is permissible (sahih).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Determine which scholars oppose and what they argue.
Zufar (intra-Hanafi) and Shafi‘i hold it invalid.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the reasoning that profit must correspond to liability.
Since liability is equal, profit must be equal.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut the opponent's argument?
They cite a hadith and analogy with mudarabah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in application?
Hanafis allow unequal shares; Shafi‘is require proportionality.

اثر یہ ہوگا کہ ہم نے یہ کہا کہ بغیر ضمانت کے بھی نفع کی شرط کرنا صحیح ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح مضاربت میں مال امانت کے طور پر ہوتا ہے لیکن ضمانت کے بغیر بھی اس میں نفع کی شرط جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اسی طرح شرکت عنان میں ایک شریک کے لئے زائد نفع کا ہونا جائز ہوتا ہے۔ اور دوسری شرکت، مفاوضہ ہونے کا اثر یہ ہوگا کہ دونوں شریکوں پر کام کی شرط ہونے سے شرکت عنان باطل نہیں ہوتی ہے۔
He who does more work and is stronger is not satisfied with equality, and need arises for differentiation, unlike stipulating all profit for one of them because that takes the contract out of partnership and also out of mudarabah into a loan if stipulated for the worker, or into a sleeping partnership if stipulated for the capital owner. This contract resembles mudarabah in that he works in the partner's money, and resembles partnership in name and action since both work. So we combined both: we applied the aspect of mudarabah and said that stipulating profit without liability is valid, and the aspect of partnership so that it is not invalidated by stipulating work on both.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of stipulating unequal profit shares in Shirkat al-‘Inan when both partners contribute equal capital. Imam Abu Hanifa and the Hanafi school hold that it is permissible, based on need and a hadith from ‘Ali (ra). Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi‘i hold it invalid because profit should correspond to capital contribution and liability. The Hanafis argue that profit can be earned through work as well as capital, so a partner who does more work or has greater skill may receive more profit. They also cite the hadith: 'Profit is according to their agreement, but loss is according to the capital.' This hadith, though narrated only in Hanafi books, supports the permissibility of unequal profit even when capital is equal. The passage also distinguishes between stipulating all profit for one partner, which would invalidate the contract (turning it into a loan or sleeping partnership), and merely stipulating an unequal share.

Key Terms
شَرِكَة الْعِنَان (shirkat al-‘inān): A partnership where each partner contributes some capital and work, but they are not agents or guarantors of each other.
رِبْح (ribḥ): Profit generated from the partnership capital.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Shirkat al-‘Inan, if both partners contribute equal capital, can they agree that one partner receives two-thirds of the profit?
A) Yes, according to Abu Hanifa.
B) No, according to all scholars.
C) Yes, but only if the partner with less profit also does more work.
D) No, because profit must be equal to capital.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, profit shares in Shirkat al-‘Inan are determined by agreement, not necessarily by capital; unequal shares are valid as long as profit is a fraction and loss is proportional to capital.

Shirkah — Partnership

Partial Capital Contribution in Shirkat al-‘Inan
Ruling statement with brief justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on partial capital contribution in Shirkat al-‘Inan and explain why equality of capital is not a condition.

Core Idea
In ‘Inan partnership, partners may contribute only part of their wealth; equality is irrelevant.

This lesson addresses a key flexibility in Shirkat al-‘Inan: partners are not required to invest all their wealth, nor must they contribute equal amounts. The concise ruling from Al-Quduri clarifies that the contract’s language does not demand equality, distinguishing it from the more stringent Mufawada partnership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first part: 'يجوز أن يعقد كل واحد منهما ببعض ماله دون البعض' – it is permissible for each partner to contract with part of his wealth, not all. The ruling is permissibility (jawaz).
The contract itself is valid even with partial contribution.
2
Extract the reason
The text provides the rationale: 'لأن المساواة في المال ليس بشرط فيه' – equality in capital is not a condition. The word 'عنان' does not imply equal contribution.
Contrast with Mufawada, which does require equality.
3
Note the capital requirement
The last part states that the partnership is only valid with the type of capital that would make Mufawada valid (i.e., dirhams, dinars, or current currency). This implies that any mal mutaqawwim (valuable property) suitable for trade is acceptable.
The same currency requirement applies as in Mufawada.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider two individuals: one has 1000 dirhams and the other has 500 dirhams. They form an ‘Inan partnership where the first contributes 500 dirhams and the second 500 dirhams. This is valid because equality is not required, and partial contribution is allowed.
The first could have contributed only part of his wealth.

قَالَ وَ يَجُوزُ أن يَعْقِدَ هَا كُل وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا يَبَعْضِ مَالِهِ دُونَ الْبَعْضِ لِأَنَّ المَساواة فِي الْمَالِ لَيْسَ بِشَرِطٍ فِيهِ إِذ اللَّفْطُ لَا يَقْتَضِيهِ وَلَا يَصِحُ الإِيمَابَيَّنَا أَنَّ الْمُفَاوَضَةَ تَصِحَ بِهِ لِلْوَجْهِ الَّذِى ذَكَرَنَاهُ. ترجمہ اور ( قدور می رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ ) شرکت عنان میں یہ بات جائز ہے کہ ہر شریک اپنے تھوڑے مال کو شرکت کے مال میں ملا دے اور باقی کو نہ ملائے ۔ کیونکہ اس شرکت میں مال کی برابری شرط نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ عنان کے معنی میں ایسی کوئی بات نہیں ہے اور نہ ہی برابری کا تقاضا ہے۔ البتہ شرکت اس مال سے صحیح ہو گی جسے ہم نے پہلے بیان کر دیا ہے یعنی درہم و دینار اور رائج الوقت کے یعنی جن سے شرکت مفاوضہ صحیح ہوتی ہے۔ اس کی وجہ بھی وہی ہے جسے وہاں بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
He said: It is permissible that each of them enters into the contract with part of his wealth without the rest, because equality in capital is not a condition in it, since the word does not require it. And it is not correct except as we have clarified that the muqawada is valid with it for the reason we mentioned.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from Al-Quduri: In Shirkat al-‘Inan, it is permissible for each partner to contribute only a portion of his wealth, not necessarily all. The reason is that equality of capital amounts is not a condition in this type of partnership. The term '‘Inan' itself does not imply equal contribution. The passage also notes that the partnership is only valid with capital that is considered valid for Shirkat al-Mufawada (i.e., dirhams and dinars or current currency). This follows the same reasoning as previously mentioned.

Key Terms
مُفَاوَضَة (mufāwaḍah): Full partnership where partners are agents and guarantors for each other, requiring equal capital and full authority.
شِرْكَة العِنَان (shirkat al-‘inān): A partnership where partners may contribute different amounts and have limited liability; equality not required.
جَائِز (jā’iz): Permissible; legally valid and allowed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because equality of capital is not a condition.
B) No, all wealth must be contributed.
C) Yes, but only if the other partner also contributes half.
D) No, because the word ‘Inan implies equal contribution.

Key Takeaway
In Shirkat al-‘Inan, partners may contribute only part of their wealth; equality of capital is irrelevant.

Different Currencies in Shirkat al-‘Inan
Ruling on mixing different currencies in partnership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits Shirkat al-‘Inan with different currencies and evaluate the opposing view of Imam Zufar and al-Shafi‘i.

Core Idea
In Hanafi Shirkat al-‘Inan, mixing is not required; different currencies are permissible as thaman.

This lesson addresses a key point of difference between the Hanafi school and Imam Zufar and al-Shafi‘i: whether partners contributing different currencies (dinars and dirhams) can form a valid Shirkat al-‘Inan. The dispute hinges on whether physical mixing (khalṭ) of capital is a condition for partnership. The Hanafi position, based on the nature of the contract as mutual agency, allows it without mixing.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Abu Hanifa and the Hanafi school rule regarding partnership with different currencies.
2
Identify the opposing view
Name the scholars who disagree (Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi‘i) and their ruling.
Zufar was a student of Abu Hanifa but differed here.
3
Trace the root of the dispute
Understand that the disagreement is about whether mixing (khalṭ) of capital is a condition for a valid Shirkat al-‘Inan.
4
Follow the Hanafi response
Explain why the Hanafi school does not require mixing: the contract is based on mutual agency (wakalah), not physical commingling.
The term 'Inan does not imply mixing.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Describe the practical consequence: Hanafis allow different currencies; Shafi‘is require same type and mixing.
This affects the flexibility of forming partnerships.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ أنْ يَشْتَرِ كَاوَ مِنْ جِهَةِ أَحَدِهِمَا دَنَانِيرُ وَ مِنَ الآخَرِ دَرَاهِمُ وَكَذَا مِنْ أَحَدِهِمَا دَرَاهِمُ بِيضُ وَمِنَ الآخر سُودٌ وَقَالَ زُفَرَ وَالشَّافِعِي لَا يَجُوزُ وَ هَدَا بِنَاء عَلَى اشْتِرَاطِ الْخَلْطِ وَعَدَمِهِ فَإِنَّ عِنْدَهُمَا شَرط وَ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ ذَالِكَ فِى مُخْتَلِفَى الجنس وَسَبَيّنَهُ مِنْ بَعْدُ إِنْشَاءَ اللهُ تَعَالَى. ترجمہ اور (یہ بھی کہا ہے کہ ) شرکت عنان میں یہ بھی جائز ہے کہ ایک شریک کی طرف سے دینا ر ہوں اور دوسرے کی طرف سے درہم ہوں ۔ اس طرح یہ بھی جائز ہے کہ اس کی طرف سے سفید درہم ہوں اور دوسرے کی طرف سے سیاہ درہم ہوں ۔ مگر امام زفر و شافعی رحمہما اللہ نے کہا ہے کہ یہ جائز نہیں ہوگا۔ دراصل یہ اختلاف اس بنیاد پر ہے کہ دونوں کے مالوں کو ایک دوسرے میں ملانے کی شرط ہے یا نہیں ۔ چنا نچہ فر رحمتہ اللہ علیہ و شافعی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک ملا دینا شرط ہے۔ حالانکہ جمعیت میں مختلف دو چیزیں ایک دوسرے میں مکمل طور سے مختلط نہیں ہو سکتی ہیں۔ اس مسئلہ کو ہم انشاء اللہ اس کے بعد پھر بیان کریں گے۔
And it is permissible that from one of them come dinars and from the other dirhams, and likewise from one of them white dirhams and from the other black dirhams. Zufar and al-Shafi‘i said it is not permissible. This is based on stipulating mixing or not. For according to them (Zufar and Shafi‘i), mixing is a condition, but that is not fully realized with different types. And he will explain it later, God willing.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of Shirkat al-‘Inan when one partner contributes dinars (gold) and the other dirhams (silver), or different varieties of the same currency (e.g., white and black dirhams). Imam Abu Hanifa allows it, while Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi‘i disallow it. The root of the dispute is whether mixing (khalṭ) of the capitals is a condition for a valid partnership. The Hanafis do not require actual mixing; rather, the partnership is valid as long as the capital is of a type that can be legally transacted (thaman muqawwam). Zufar and Shafi‘i require actual mixing, which is impossible with different currencies because they are distinct substances. The Hanafis argue that the term ‘Inan does not imply mixing, so different currencies are permissible. The passage promises further explanation.

Key Terms
خَلْط (khalṭ): Physical mixing of the capital contributions of the partners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, can one partner contribute gold dinars and the other silver dirhams to a Shirkat al-‘Inan?
A) Yes, because mixing is not a condition.
B) No, because they are different currencies.
C) Yes, but only if they have the same value.
D) No, because the capital must be from the same type.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits Shirkat al-‘Inan with different currencies because mixing is not a requirement; the contract is valid as long as the capital is thaman.

Individual Liability for Purchases in Shirkat al-‘Inan
Ruling that each partner is individually liable for his own purchases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule of individual liability in Shirkat al-‘Inan and distinguish it from the joint liability in Shirkat al-Mufawada using the concepts of agency and guarantee.

Core Idea
In Shirkat al-‘Inan, each partner bears his own purchase liability – agency applies, not guarantee.

A common question in partnership transactions is who is responsible for paying the seller when goods are bought for the partnership. The classical Hanafi text of Al-Qudurī gives a clear answer for Shirkat al-‘Inan: only the partner who actually made the purchase can be sued for the price. This lesson unpacks that ruling and explains the legal reasoning rooted in the nature of the partnership contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that for Shirkat al-‘Inan, when one partner buys something for the partnership, he alone is pursued for its price, not the other partner.
Focus on the phrase 'يُطَالَبُ بِثَمَنِهِ دُونَ الآخَرَ'.
2
Understand the legal basis
The ruling is based on the principle that Shirkat al-‘Inan includes mutual agency (wakālah) but not mutual guarantee (kafālah). The agent (the buyer) is the principal in rights and obligations.
The text says: 'لِمَا بَيَّنَّا أَنَّهُ يَتَضَمَّنُ الْوَكَالَةَ دُونَ الْكَفَالَة'.
3
Contrast with Shirkat al-Mufawada
In Shirkat al-Mufawada, the partnership includes both agency and guarantee, so each partner is jointly liable for purchases made by either.
This contrast is not in the passage but helps contextualise the rule.
4
Apply the rule to a hypothetical
Consider partner A buys inventory on credit for the partnership. The seller can only demand payment from A, not from partner B. If A defaults, B is not liable from the partnership contract itself.
This reinforces the individual liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَ مَا اشْتَرَاهُ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا الشَّرَكَةَ طُولِبَ يَتَمَنِهِ دُونَ الآخَرَ لِمَا بَيْنَا أَنَّهُ يَتَضَمَّنُ الْوَكَالَةَ دُونَ الْكَفَالَة وَالْوَكِيلُ هُوَ الْأَصْلُ فِي الْحُقوقِ. ترجمہ اور قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ ) شرکت عنان کے دونوں شریکوں میں سے جس کسی نے جو کچھ کاروبار میں شرکت کے لئے خریدا ہے۔ اس کی قیمت کا مطالبہ صرف اس سے ہوگا اور دوسرے سے نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ہم نے پہلے بتا دیا ہے کہ شرکت عنان میں ہر شریک دوسرے کا وکیل ہوتا ہے، ضامن نہیں۔ اور وکیل حقوق کا اصل ہوتا ہے۔
He said: And whatever each of them buys for the partnership, he will be demanded for its price, not the other, because we have clarified that it includes agency, not guarantee. And the agent is the origin in rights.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from Al-Quduri: In Shirkat al-‘Inan, if one partner purchases goods for the partnership, he alone is liable for the price. The seller can only demand payment from the buyer partner, not from the other partner. The reason is that Shirkat al-‘Inan implies mutual agency (wakala) but not mutual guarantee (kafala). Each partner is an agent for the other in transactions, but not a guarantor for debts. Therefore, the partner who actually buys is the one responsible for the payment. This distinguishes Shirkat al-‘Inan from Shirkat al-Mufawada, where each partner is both agent and guarantor.

Key Terms
وَكَالَة (wakālah): Agency; the authority of one partner to act on behalf of the other in commercial transactions.
كَفَالَة (kafālah): Guarantee; the obligation of one partner to be liable for debts incurred by the other.
شَرِكَة الْعِنَان (shirkat al-‘inān): A partnership where each partner contributes capital and labour, with equal or unequal shares, and each acts as an agent but not a guarantor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Shirkat al-‘Inan, if partner A buys goods on credit, from whom can the seller demand payment?
A) Only from partner A, the buyer.
B) From both partners A and B jointly.
C) From either partner at the seller's choice.
D) Only from the partnership fund, not from individuals.

Key Takeaway
In Shirkat al-‘Inan, each partner is solely responsible for the price of what he personally buys, because the contract grants agency but not guarantee.

Partial Capital Contribution in Shirkat al-ʿInān
Ruling on partial capital contribution in ʿinān partnership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partial capital contribution in shirkat al-ʿinān and explain the proof based on the absence of capital equality as a condition.

Core Idea
In ʿinān partnership, you may contribute only part of your wealth – equality is not a condition.

The classical Hanafi text permits partners in a shirkat al-ʿinān to contribute only a portion of their wealth, not the whole. This flexibility stems from the nature of the ʿinān contract, which does not require capital equality. The passage also draws an analogy to mufāwaḍah to support the ruling. Let us unpack the reasoning and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being permitted? Each partner may contract (i.e., form the partnership) using only part of their wealth, leaving the rest outside the partnership. The ruling is that this is jā'iz (permissible) and the partnership is sahīh (valid).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is that equality of capital is not a condition (shart) in ʿinān. The term (لفظ) itself does not require it. Additionally, the author analogizes to mufāwaḍah, which is valid even with partial contribution for a reason already explained.
The dalil is qiyas (analogy) to mufāwaḍah, though the primary basis is the non-conditionality.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase: 'because equality in wealth is not a condition in it, since the term does not require it.' The absence of a requirement in the contract's language means partners are free to agree on any capital amount, including partial contribution.
The analogy to mufāwaḍah reinforces that even a stricter partnership type can allow partial contribution.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Although the passage does not mention disagreement, this ruling is mukhtalaf fih across schools. Some madhāhib may require all capital to be pooled, but the Hanafi school holds that partial contribution is valid.
This flexibility is a distinctive feature of the Hanafi position on ʿinān.
5
Evaluate the practical scope
The ruling applies to shirkat al-ʿinān specifically, not to mufāwaḍah (which has its own conditions). In practice, partners can structure their investment flexibly.
The mufta bihi position is that partial contribution is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَعْقِدَ [؟] كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بِبَعْضِ مَالِهِ دُونَ الْبَعْضِ لِأَنَّ الْمُسَاوَاةَ فِي الْمَالِ لَيْسَ بِشَرْطٍ فِيهِ إِذِ اللَّفْظُ لَا يَقْتَضِيهِ وَلَا يَصِحُّ الْإِيمَا [؟] بَيَّنَا أَنَّ الْمُفَاوَضَةَ تَصِحُّ بِهِ لِلْوَجْهِ الَّذِي ذَكَرْنَاهُ
He said: It is permissible for each one of them to contract with a portion of his wealth and not the whole, because equality in wealth is not a condition in it, since the term does not require it, and the [؟] is not valid. We have explained that al-mufāwaḍah is valid with it for the reason we mentioned.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Qudūrī on shirkat al-ʿinān. The author clarifies that a partner may contribute only part of his capital to the partnership, keeping the rest separate. The proof is that equality of capital is not a condition for ʿinān; the term 'ʿinān' itself implies no such requirement. The same principle applies here as in mufāwaḍah, though the latter has stricter conditions. This ruling is based on the Hanafi position that the contract of ʿinān is founded on agency (wakāla), not on capital equality.

Key Terms
شركة العنان (shirkat al-ʿinān): A partnership of equals where partners are agents for each other but not guarantors, and capital may be unequal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The partners must agree to it explicitly.
B) Equality in wealth is not a condition in ʿinān.
C) The analogy to mufāwaḍah requires it.
D) The term 'ʿinān' implies equal capital.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi shirkat al-ʿinān, partners may contribute any portion of their wealth; capital equality is not a condition.

Validity of Different Currency Types in Shirkat al-ʿInān
Ruling on disparate currencies with dispute from Zufar and Shāfiʿī

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis permit partnership with different currencies and state the grounds of the Shafi'i/Zufar objection.

Core Idea
In Hanafi ʿinān, the contract creates partnership, not physical mixing.

This lesson tackles a common practical question: can two partners form a valid shirkat al-ʿinān when one contributes gold dinars and the other silver dirhams? The Hanafi school answers yes, but the Shafi'i school and the Hanafi scholar Zufar disagree. Understanding the root of this dispute reveals a foundational difference in how each school defines the essence of a partnership contract.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling given in the text: it is permissible (jāʾiz) for one partner to provide dinars and the other dirhams, and similarly for different coin types (e.g., white and black dirhams).
The ruling is explicit: 'وَيَجُوزُ' (it is permissible).
2
Identify the opponents
Note that Zufar (a Hanafi dissenter) and al-Shāfiʿī hold the opposite view: it is not permissible.
Zufar's disagreement is intra-Hanafi; al-Shāfiʿī represents an inter-madhhab difference.
3
Analyze the opponents' proof
Their argument is based on the condition of mixing (khalṭ): they require physical mixing of capital so that it becomes indistinguishable. Different currencies (gold and silver) cannot be mixed, so the condition fails.
The text says 'عَلَى اشْتِرَاطِ الْخَلْطِ' (on the condition of mixing).
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi position implicitly rejects mixing as a condition for ʿinān. The partnership is valid by virtue of the contract (ʿaqd) alone; physical mixing is not required. Therefore, different currencies pose no problem.
The author promises a fuller explanation later: 'سَنُبَيِّنُهُ مِنْ بَعْدُ'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi law, a partnership with different currencies is valid and profits are shared according to the contract; under Shafi'i law, it is invalid unless the currencies are first exchanged into a common type.
This difference affects business arrangements in pluralistic economies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَشْتَرِيَا مِنْ جِهَةِ أَحَدِهِمَا دَنَانِيرُ وَمِنَ الْآخَرِ دَرَاهِمُ وَكَذَا مِنْ أَحَدِهِمَا دَرَاهِمُ بَيْضُ وَمِنَ الْآخَرِ سُودٌ وَقَالَ زُفَرُ وَالشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يَجُوزُ وَهَذَا بِنَاءٌ عَلَى اشْتِرَاطِ الْخَلْطِ وَعَدَمِهِ فَإِنَّ عِنْدَهُمَا شَرْطٌ وَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ ذَلِكَ فِي مُخْتَلِفِي الْجِنْسِ وَسَنُبَيِّنُهُ مِنْ بَعْدُ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى
And it is permissible that they purchase with one of them providing dinars and the other dirhams, and likewise with one providing white dirhams and the other black dirhams. Zufar and al-Shāfiʿī said: it is not permissible. And this is based on the condition of mixing and its absence; for according to them mixing is a condition, and that is not achieved with different types. We will explain it later, God willing.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling and an inter-madhhab dispute. Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar who sometimes differed) and Imam al-Shāfiʿī hold that different currencies cannot form a valid ʿinān partnership because the capital must be mixed (ikhtilāṭ) to constitute joint ownership. Since dinars and dirhams are of different types (gold vs silver) and cannot be physically mixed into one indistinguishable mass, they argue the condition is not met. The Hanafi position (of Abū Ḥanīfa and the majority) is that mixing is not a condition for ʿinān; the partnership is formed by the contract (ʿaqd) itself, not by physical mixing. Therefore, even different currencies are valid. The author promises to elaborate later.

Key Terms
خلط (khalṭ): Physical mixing of capital so that it becomes indistinguishable; a condition some scholars require for partnership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, can shirkat al-ʿinān be formed with one partner contributing gold dinars and the other silver dirhams?
A) No, because they are different currencies.
B) Yes, it is permissible.
C) Yes, but only if they are exchanged first.
D) No, only if both contribute the same currency.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits shirkat al-ʿinān with different currencies because the contract, not physical mixing, establishes the partnership.

Liability for Purchases in Shirkat al-ʿInān and Recourse
Ruling on individual liability and recourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on individual liability for purchases in shirkat al-ʿinān and explain the buyer's right of recourse, citing the principle that ʿinān includes agency only.

Core Idea
In shirkat al-ʿinān, only the buying partner is liable to the seller; the buyer can then recover the partner's share.

This passage from al-Qudūrī clarifies a key point in Hanafi partnership law: when one partner buys goods for the business, only that partner is personally liable to the seller. The other partner is not a surety. However, after paying, the buyer can seek reimbursement from the partner. We'll unpack the legal reasoning and the burden of proof in disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
What exactly is the legal consequence? Find the statement that the buyer alone is demanded the price.
2
Understand the Dalil
Why is the buyer alone liable? The text says ʿinān includes wakāla (agency) not kafāla (suretyship). Explain how agency makes the buyer the principal in the transaction.
3
Trace the Recourse Mechanism
After the buyer pays from his own money, he can reclaim the partner's share. Recognize that this is because the buyer acted as an agent for the partner in that share.
4
Apply the Burden of Proof Rule
If the partner denies knowledge of the purchase or payment, the claimant must provide proof. The denier's statement with oath is accepted.
This is the standard rule for claims and denials.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَا اشْتَرَاهُ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا فِي الشَّرَكَةِ طُولِبَ بِثَمَنِهِ دُونَ الْآخَرِ لِمَا بَيَّنَا أَنَّهُ يَتَضَمَّنُ الْوَكَالَةَ دُونَ الْكَفَالَةِ وَالْوَكِيلُ هُوَ الْأَصْلُ فِي الْحُقُوقِ. قَالَ ثُمَّ يَرْجِعُ عَلَى شَرِيكِهِ بِحِصَّتِهِ مِنْهُ مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا أَدَّى مِنْ مَالِ نَفْسِهِ لِأَنَّهُ وَكِيلٌ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ فِي حِصَّتِهِ فَإِذَا نَقَدَ مِنْ مَالِ نَفْسِهِ رَجَعَ عَلَيْهِ فَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يُعْرَفُ ذَلِكَ إِلَّا بِقَوْلِهِ فَعَلَيْهِ الْحُجَّةُ لِأَنَّهُ يَدَّعِي وُجُوبَ الْمَالِ فِي ذِمَّةِ الْآخَرِ وَهُوَ يُنْكِرُ وَالْقَوْلُ لِلْمُنْكِرِ مَعَ يَمِينِهِ
He said: Whatever each one of them purchases for the partnership, he alone is demanded the price, not the other, because we have explained that [ʿinān] includes agency and not suretyship; the agent is the principal regarding rights. He said: Then he returns to his partner for his share of it. Its meaning: when he pays from his own money because he is an agent on his behalf in his share. So when he pays from his own money, he reclaims from him. If that is only known by his statement, then the proof is upon him because he claims that money is obligatory in the liability of the other, and the other denies it; the statement [of the denier] is accepted with his oath.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage gives a detailed ruling on liability in shirkat al-ʿinān. The author (al-Qudūrī) explains that since ʿinān involves agency (wakāla) but not suretyship (kafāla), each partner is solely responsible for the price of what he purchases for the partnership, even if the purchase is for the joint benefit. The seller may only demand payment from the buying partner. However, after the buyer pays from his own funds, he may recover his partner's share from him because he acted as his agent. If the purchase and payment are disputed (e.g., the partner denies knowledge), the claimant must provide proof (witnesses) because he is asserting a claim against the other's liability. The denier's statement with oath is accepted. This reflects Hanafi principles of agency and burden of proof.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakāla): Agency: one partner acts as agent for the other in the partnership business, but does not assume liability for the other's purchases.
كفالة (kafāla): Suretyship: assuming liability for another's debt. Not present in ʿinān.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In shirkat al-ʿinān, if partner A buys goods for the partnership, who can the seller demand payment from?
A) Both partners jointly.
B) Only partner A.
C) Only partner B.
D) The partnership entity.

Key Takeaway
In shirkat al-ʿinān, the buying partner alone is liable to the seller, reflecting the exclusive presence of agency (wakāla) without suretyship (kafāla).

Capital Destruction Before Purchase Voids Shirkat al-ʿInān
Ruling on voiding partnership if capital lost before first trade

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that destruction of partnership capital before any purchase voids the contract, and apply the qiyas to sale, gift, and bequest.

Core Idea
Destruction of partnership capital before trading voids the contract because capital is the specified subject matter—like a sale where goods perish before delivery.

This passage from al-Hidayah (via al-Quduri) presents a critical rule for Shirkat al-'Inan. It establishes that the partnership is not merely suspended but becomes void ab initio if any part of the capital perishes before any trading takes place. The reasoning hinges on identifying the capital as the subject matter (ma'qud 'alayhi) of the contract, drawing analogies to gift, bequest, and sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The ruling states that if the partnership capital (or one partner's capital) perishes before any purchase, the partnership becomes void. This applies whether both capitals perish or just one.
The ruling is absolute before mixing.
2
Determine the subject matter (ma'qud 'alayhi)
The capital is the subject matter of the partnership contract, just as the gifted item is in a gift or the bequeathed property in a bequest. It becomes specified by the contract itself.
Contrast with mudarabah where subject matter is not specified until possession.
3
Apply the qiyas to sale
Just as a sale is void if the sold item perishes before delivery, the partnership is void if the capital perishes before execution (i.e., before purchase). The underlying 'illa is destruction of the subject matter before implementation.
The qiyas is jaliyy (clear) because the 'illa is directly extracted.
4
Distinguish from mudarabah and wakalah
In mudarabah and isolated wakalah, the capital (price) is not specified by the contract but only by possession. Hence, destruction before possession does not void the contract.
This highlights the importance of specification in determining the effect of destruction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا هَلَكَ مَالُ الشَّرَكَةِ أَوْ أَحَدُ الْمَالَيْنِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَشْتَرِيَا شَيْئًا بَطَلَتِ الشَّرَكَةُ لِأَنَّ الْمَعْقُودَ عَلَيْهِ فِي عَقْدِ الشَّرَكَةِ الْمَالُ فَإِنَّهُ يَتَعَيَّنُ فِيهِ كَمَا فِي الْهِبَةِ وَالْوَصِيَّةِ وَبِهَلَاكِ الْمَعْقُودِ عَلَيْهِ يَبْطُلُ الْعَقْدُ كَمَا فِي الْبَيْعِ بِخِلَافِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ وَالْوَكَالَةِ الْمُفْرَدَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَتَعَيَّنُ الثَّمَنُ فِيهِمَا بِالتَّعْيِينِ وَإِنَّمَا يَتَعَيَّانِ بِالْقَبْضِ عَلَى مَا عُرِفَ وَهَذَا ظَاهِرٌ فِيمَا إِذَا هَلَكَ الْمَالَانِ وَكَذَا إِذَا هَلَكَ أَحَدُهُمَا لِأَنَّهُ مَا رَضِيَ بِشِرْكَةِ صَاحِبِهِ فِي مَالِهِ إِلَّا لِيُشْرِكَهُ فِي مَالِهِ فَإِذَا فَاتَ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يَكُنْ رَاضِيًا بِشِرْكَتِهِ فَيَبْطُلُ الْعَقْدُ لِعَدَمِ فَائِدَتِهِ. وَأَيُّهُمَا هَلَكَ مِنْ مَالِ صَاحِبِهِ إِنْ هَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ فَظَاهِرُ وَكَذَا إِذَا كَانَ هَلَكَ فِي يَدِ الْآخَرِ لِأَنَّهُ أَمَانَةٌ فِي يَدِهِ بِخِلَافِ مَا بَعْدَ الْخَلْطِ حَيْثُ يَهْلِكُ فِي الشَّرِكَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَتَمَيَّزُ فَيَجْعَلُ الْهَلَاكَ مِنَ الْجَمِيعِ
He said: And if the capital of the partnership perishes, or one of the two capitals, before they purchase anything, the partnership becomes void because the subject matter of the contract in the partnership contract is the capital, for it becomes specified in it as in hibah (gift) and wasiyyah (bequest). By the destruction of the subject matter, the contract becomes void, as in sale – unlike muḍārabah and isolated wakālah, because the price is not specified by specification in them, but rather becomes specified by possession, as is known. This is clear when both capitals perish, and likewise when one of them perishes, because he only consented to partnership with his partner in his wealth in order that his partner partner him in his wealth; when that is lost, he is not content with his partnership, so the contract becomes void due to lack of benefit. And whichever of them perishes from the wealth of his owner, if it perishes in his hand it is apparent, and likewise if it perishes in the hand of the other because it is a trust in his hand – unlike after mixing, where it perishes in the partnership because it is not distinguishable, so the destruction is attributed to the whole.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage provides a key ruling on the effect of capital destruction in shirkat al-ʿinān before any trading activity. The author (al-Qudūrī) states that the partnership is voided if the partnership capital or even one partner's share is destroyed before any purchase is made. The reasoning: the capital is the subject matter (maʿqūd ʿalayhi) of the partnership contract, similar to the gifted item in a gift or the bequeathed property in a bequest. Just as a sale is void if the sold item perishes before delivery, so too the partnership contract is void if the capital perishes. This is contrasted with muḍārabah and isolated agency, where the capital is not specified by contract but only by possession; hence loss before possession does not void the contract. The text further explains that even if only one partner's capital perishes, the partnership is void because the other partner only agreed to partnership in exchange for being partnered in the other's wealth; if that is lost, there is no benefit. Moreover, whether the loss occurs in the hand of the owner or in the hand of the other partner (since it is a trust), the partnership is void. However, after mixing the capitals (khalṭ), loss is shared proportionally because the capitals are indistinguishable.

Key Terms
معقود عليه (maʿqūd ʿalayhi): The subject matter of the contract; in partnership, the capital contributed.
خلط (khalṭ): Mixing of capitals so that they become indistinguishable; after mixing, destruction is shared.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In shirkat al-ʿinān, if one partner's capital is destroyed before any purchase is made, what happens to the partnership?
A) The partnership continues with the remaining capital.
B) The partnership becomes void.
C) The partnership is suspended until new capital is contributed.
D) Only the affected partner's share is removed.

Key Takeaway
In Shirkat al-'Inan, the capital is the subject matter of the contract; its destruction before any trade voids the partnership.

Partner's Right to Claim Contribution and Proof
Ruling on partner's right to recover and proof rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal basis for a partner's right to claim contribution and explain the burden of proof in a disputed partnership purchase.

Core Idea
The paying partner recovers as an agent; the denier's oath defeats an unproven claim.

In a partnership, if one partner pays the full price from his own money, he is considered an agent for the other partner regarding his share. This lesson explains that agency basis and the procedural rule that if the purchase is disputed, the claimant must prove it or the denier's word with oath prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states that a partner who paid the full price from his own wealth can recover the other partner's share from him.
2
Understand the legal basis
The paying partner is an agent (wakil) for the other partner regarding the other's share. This agency is implied in the partnership contract.
Agency is the foundation of the right of recourse.
3
Analyze the burden of proof
If the purchase and payment are disputed and only known by the claimant's word, the claimant must provide evidence (al-hujjah).
4
Apply the rule of denier's oath
Since the defendant denies the claim, the word is given to the denier with his oath, based on the principle al-qawlu lil-munkari ma'a yaminih.
This shifts the burden to the claimant to produce evidence first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ ثُمَّ يَرْجِعُ عَلَى شَرِيكَ بِحِصَّتَهِ مِنْهُ مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا أَدَّى مِنْ مَّالِ نَفْسِهِ لِأَنَّهُ وَكِيْلٌ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ فِي حِصّتِهِ فَإِذَا نَقَدَ مِنْ مَالِ نَفْسِهِ رَجَعَ عَلَيْهِ فَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يُعْرَفُ ذَالِكَ إِلَّا بِقَوْلِهِ فَعَلَيْهِ الْحُجَّةُ لِأَنَّهُ يَدَّعِى وُجُوبَ الْمَالِ فِي ذِمَّةِ الاخر وَهُوَ يُنكِرْ وَالْقَولُ لِلْمُنكَرِ مَعَ يَمِينِهِ
ترجمہ پھر قیمت سے جو کچھ بھی ادا کیا ہے اس میں سے دوسرے شریک سے اس کے حصہ کے برابر اس سے واپس مانگ لے گا ۔ اس جملہ کے معنی یہ ہوئے کہ جب ایک شریک نے اپنے مال سے قیمت ادا کی ہو تو اپنے دوسرے شریک سے اس کے حصہ کے برابر واپس لے گا۔ کیونکہ پہلا شریک دوسرے شریک کی طرف سے اس کے حصہ میں وکیل ہے اس لئے جب اس نے اپنے مال سے ادا کر دیا تو وہ دوسرے شریک سے واپس لے گا۔ اور اگر یہ بات کہ کوئی چیز خریدی گئی ہے۔ اور کتنے میں خریدی گئی ہے معلوم نہ ہو سکے ۔ مثلاً جو چیز خریدی ہو وہ موجود نہ ہو حالانکہ شریک یہ کہتا ہے کہ میں نے مثلا ایک غلام خریدا ہے اور اس کی قیمت بھی ادا کر دی ہے بعد میں وہ غلام مر گیا ہے لیکن دوسرا شریک ان باتوں کا انکار کرتا ہو کہ ایسا بالکل نہیں ہوا ہے۔ تو ایسی صورت میں کہنے اور دعوی کرنے والے پر لازم ہو گا اپنے دعوئی کے مطابق گواہ پیش کرے۔ کیونکہ شریک غلام کی خریداری کا دعوی کر کے دوسرے کے ذمہ مال کے واجب ہونے کا دعوی کرتا ہے۔ لیکن اس کا دوسرا شریک اس کا انکار کرتا ہے لہذا منکر کا قول قسم کے ساتھ ہی مقبول ہوگا ۔
He said: Then he recovers from his partner his share from it. Meaning: when he paid from his own wealth, because he is an agent from his side in his share. So when he paid from his own wealth, he recovers from him. But if that is not known except by his statement, then the proof is upon him, because he claims the obligation of wealth in the liability of the other, and he denies. And the statement is of the denier with his oath. Translation: Then whatever price has been paid, from that he will demand back from the other partner equal to his share. This sentence means: When one partner paid the price from his own wealth, he will recover from the other partner an amount equal to his share. Because the first partner is an agent for the other in his share. So when he paid from his own wealth, he recovers from the other. And if the fact that something was bought and for what price is not known - for example, the purchased item is not present although the partner says: I bought a slave and paid its price, then the slave died, but the other partner denies this - in such a case, the claimant must produce witnesses according to his claim. Because the partner claims the purchase of the slave and thereby claims that a sum is due on the other's liability, while the other denies it. Therefore, the denier's word with oath is accepted.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This is a ruling on a partner's right to claim contribution from his co-partner after paying the full price from his own money. The ruling states that the paying partner is considered an agent (wakil) on behalf of the other partner regarding the latter's share. Therefore, if he pays from his own wealth, he can recover the corresponding portion from the other partner. However, a procedural rule is added regarding the burden of proof: if the fact of purchase and payment is disputed and can only be established by the claimant's word, then the claimant (the paying partner) must provide evidence (shuhud) because he is asserting that the other's liability has become due. The denier's statement is accepted with his oath, based on the general principle al-qawlu lil-munkari ma'a yaminih (the word is of the denier with his oath). This is a standard Hanafi rule that shifts the burden of proof to the claimant when the defendant denies the claim. The practical application: if a partner buys an item with his own money and later seeks reimbursement from his partner but the partner denies the purchase or the payment, the paying partner must prove it with witnesses or, failing that, the denier's sworn word prevails.

Key Terms
الرجوع (al-rujū‘): The right of a partner who paid from his own wealth to recover from the other partner the portion of the price corresponding to the other's share.
وكيل (wakīl): An agent; in this context, the partner buying with his own money is considered an agent for the other partner for his share.
الحجة (al-ḥujjah): Proof or evidence; here it means the claimant must provide witnesses to establish his claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal basis for a partner who pays the full price from his own money to recover the other partner's share?
A) He is a guarantor (damin) for the other.
B) He is an agent (wakil) for the other in his share.
C) He is a creditor (dayyin) to the other.
D) He is a trustee (amin) of the common fund.

Key Takeaway
A paying partner recovers from the co-partner as an agent, but if the purchase is disputed, the claimant must provide proof or the denier's oath prevails.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate
6 min
Voidance of Partnership Upon Capital Destruction Before Purchase
Ruling with proof by qiyas on sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that partnership becomes void upon destruction of capital before any purchase, identify the qiyas on sale, and distinguish mudarabah and agency.

Core Idea
Destruction of the subject matter voids the contract, as in sale.

In a capital partnership (shirkat al-mal), the contributed capitals become the specified subject matter of the contract. This lesson examines the legal consequence if that capital is destroyed before any trade occurs. The Hanafi ruling is decisive: the partnership is invalidated, drawing on the analogy of sale and contrasting with mudarabah and agency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Name the act: partnership (shirkah). The ruling: if capital (all or part) is destroyed before any purchase, the partnership becomes void (batil).
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) on sale: just as a sale is void if the sold item is destroyed before delivery, partnership is void if the subject matter (capital) is destroyed before any use.
The subject matter (ma‘qud ‘alayh) is specified in the contract, unlike in mudarabah or agency.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illah) is the specification of the subject matter in the contract. In partnership, capital becomes specified (yata‘ayyan) upon contract, similar to gift and bequest. Destruction of a specified subject matter makes performance impossible.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih. Some schools (e.g., Shafi‘i) may not require specification of capital, so destruction might not void the contract.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative) and relies on the principle that capital is ma‘qud ‘alayh. Even if only one partner's capital is destroyed, the mutual condition fails, voiding the contract.
The loss is borne by the owner; the other partner is not liable because it is a trust (amanah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَ إِذَا هَلَكَ مَالُ الشَّرَكَةِ أَوْ أَحَدُ الْمَالَين قَبْلَ أَنْ يَشَتَرِ يَا شَيْئًا بَطَلَتِ الشَّرُكَةُ لِأنّ المعقودَ عَلَيْهِ فِى عَقْدِ الشَّرُكَةِ الْمَالُ فَإِنَّهُ يُتَعَيَّنُ فِيْهِ كَمَا فِي الْهَةِ وَالْوَصِيَّةِ وَبِهَلَاكِ الْمَعْقُودِ عَلَيْهِ يَبْطُلُ العَقْدُ كَمَا فِى البيع بِخِلَافِ المُضَارَبَةِ وَالْوَكَالَة الْمُفَرَدَةِ لأَنه لا يَتَعَينِ الثَّمَانِ فِيْهِمَا بِالتَّعْيِينِ وَإِنَّمَا يَتَعَيَّنَانِ بِالْقَبْضِ عَلَى مَا عُرِفَ وَهَذَا ظَاهِرُ فِيْمَا إِذَا هَلَكَ الْمَالَان وَكَذَا إِذَا هَلَكَ أَحَدُهُمَا لِأَنَّهُ مَا رَضِيَ بِشِرْكَةِ صَاحِبِهِ فِي مَالِهِ إِلَّا لِيُشْرِكَهُ فِي مَالِهِ فَإِذَا فَاتٌ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يَكُنْ رَاضِبًا بِشِرُكَتِهِ فَيَبْطُلُ الْعَقْدُ لِعَدَمِ فَائِدَتِهِ وَ أَيُّهَا هَلَكَ مِنْ مَّالِ صَاحِبِهِ إِنْ هَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ فَظَاهِرُ وَ كَذَا إِذَا كَانَ هَلَكَ فِى يَدِ الْآخَرِ لِأَنَّهُ أَمَانَةٌ فِي يَدِهِ بِخِلَافِ مَا بَعْدَ الخَلْفِ حَيْثُ يَهْلِكُ الشركة لأنه لا يتميرُ فَيَجْعَلُ الهَلَاكَ من
ترجمہ اگر دونوں شریکوں کی شرکت کا کل مال یا صرف ایک کا مال ہلاک ہو گیا اس سے پہلے کہ شرکت کے مال سے وہ کوئی چیز خریدیں کا تو شرکت ماطل ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ عقد شرکت جس چیز پر ہوتی ہے وہ مال ہے کیونکہ یہ عقد شرکت میں متعین ہو جاتا ہے۔ جیسے حصہ دار کا وصیت میں مال متعین ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور جس چیز پر عقد شرکت قائم ہوئی ہے اگر وہ ہلاک ہو جائے تو عقد ہی باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ معقد بیچ میں ہوتا ہے ۔ مثلا جس بیچ پر معاملہ طے پایا ہے اگر اس کے حوالہ کرنے سے پہلے ہلاک ہو جائے تو بیع باطل ہو جاتی ہے ) بخلاف مضاربت اور تھاوکات کے کیونکہ مضاربت اور تنباد کالت میں ثمن معین کرنے سے معین نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ بلکہ قبضہ ہونے سے ہی متعین ہوتا ہے۔جیسا کہ یہ بات پہلے بھی بتائی جاچکی ہے ۔ (الحاصل مال برباد ہونے سے شرکت باطل ہو جائے گی)۔ پھر اس صورت میں جبکہ دونوں مال ہلاک ہو جائیں تو اس میں شرکت کا باطل ہونا تو ظاہر ہے۔ اور اگر صرف ایک کا مال ضائع ہو تو بھی شرکت باطل ہوگئی ۔ کیونکہ جس کا مال ضائع نہیں ہوا ہے وہ اپنے مال میں دوسرے کو شریک کرنے پر صرف اس طرح سے راضی ہوا تھا کہ وہ خود بھی اس مال میں شریک ہو۔ اور اب جبکہ اس کا مال ہی باقی نہ رہا تو یہ اپنے مال میں شریک کرنے پر راضی نہیں ہوگا۔ لہذا عقد شرکت باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اس کا باقی رہنا بے فائدہ ہوگا ۔ اور دونوں میں سے جس کسی کا مال ضائع ہوگا اسی کا مال ضائع ہو گا یعنی دوسرا شخص اس کا ضامن بالکل نہیں ہوگا) کیونکہ اگر خود اس کے قبضہ میں رہتے ہوئے ضائع ہوا جب تو بات واضح ہے ۔ اور اگر دوسرے شریک کے قبضہ میں رہتے ہوئے ضائع ہوا تو بھی ضمان لازم نہیں آئے گا کیونکہ وہ مال اس کے قبضہ میں بطور امانت تھا۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر دونوں کا مال ملا دیا گیا اس کے بعد وہ ہلاک ہوا تو اس صورت میں اس کی بربادی بھی مشترک یعنی دونوں شریکوں کے مال سے مشترکہ ہلاک سمجھا جائے گا کیونکہ مال میں کوئی امتیاز نہیں رہتا ہے کہ کس کا ہلاک ہوا اور کس کا باقی رہا۔ اس لئے دونوں مالوں سے ہی ہلاک ہونا کہا جائے گا۔
He said: And if the capital of the partnership or one of the two capitals is destroyed before they purchase anything, the partnership becomes void, because the subject matter of the contract in the partnership contract is the capital; it becomes specified therein, as in gift and bequest. And with the destruction of the subject matter, the contract becomes void, as in sale. Unlike mudarabah and individual agency, because the price is not specified by designation in them; rather, they become specified by possession, as is known. This is obvious when both capitals are destroyed. Similarly, when one of them is destroyed, because the owner of the surviving capital only consented to partnership in his capital on the condition that the other would also make him a partner in his capital. So when that is lost, he is not consenting to his partnership, so the contract becomes void due to lack of benefit. And whichever of them his capital is destroyed, if it is destroyed in his hand, it is obvious. Similarly, if it is destroyed in the hand of the other, because it is a trust in his hand, unlike after mixing, when the partnership capital is destroyed, because no distinction is possible, so the destruction is attributed to both. Translation: If the entire partnership capital or only one partner's capital is destroyed before they buy anything with the partnership capital, the partnership becomes void. Because the subject matter of the partnership contract is the capital; it becomes specified in it, just as a share in bequest becomes specified. And if the subject matter of the contract is destroyed, the contract becomes void, as in sale – for example, if the item of sale is destroyed before delivery, the sale is void. Unlike mudarabah and individual agency, because in mudarabah and individual agency, the price is not specified by designation; rather, it becomes specified by possession, as has been explained. (Summary: destruction of capital voids the partnership). Then, in the case where both capitals are destroyed, the voidance is obvious. And if only one capital is destroyed, the partnership still becomes void, because the one whose capital is not destroyed only consented to making the other a partner in his capital on the understanding that the other would also make him a partner in his capital. Now that the other's capital is gone, he is not consenting to partnership in his own capital alone. So the contract becomes void due to lack of benefit. And whichever partner's capital is destroyed, it is his own loss – the other partner is not liable at all. Because if it was destroyed while in his own possession, it is clear. And if it was destroyed while in the other partner's possession, there is also no liability, because the capital was in his possession as a trust. Contrary to after mixing, when the partnership capital is destroyed, then the destruction is attributed to both partners jointly because no distinction remains as to whose capital was destroyed and whose remains.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of the destruction (halak) of partnership capital before any trading activity. The ruling states that if all or part of the capital is destroyed before any purchase, the partnership is voided (tabtul al-shirkah). The reasoning is that the subject matter (ma‘qud ‘alayh) of the partnership contract is the capital itself, which becomes specified (yata‘ayyan) in the contract, similar to a specific gift (hibah) or a bequest (wasiyyah). The destruction of the subject matter voids the contract by analogy (qiyas) with sale (bay‘): if the sold item is destroyed before delivery, the sale is invalid. This is distinguished from mudarabah (profit-sharing partnership) and independent agency (wakalah mufradah), where the capital is not specified by designation but only by possession (qabd). The passage then explains that even if only one partner's capital is destroyed, the partnership becomes void because the surviving partner only agreed to partnership on the mutual condition of shared capital; the benefit (fa'idah) of the contract is lost. Additionally, the destroyed capital is borne only by its owner; the other partner is not a guarantor (damin) because the capital in his hand is a trust (amanah). However, after mixing (khalat) the capitals, if destruction occurs, it is apportioned jointly since the capitals are indistinguishable. This is a fundamental Hanafi principle in shirkat al-mal (capital partnership).

Key Terms
المعقود عليه (al-ma‘qūd ‘alayh): The subject matter of the contract; in partnership, it is the capital contributed.
يتعين (yata‘ayyan): Becomes specified; the capital is designated in the contract, unlike in mudarabah where it is not specified until possession.
أمانة (amānah): Trust; the capital in the hand of the other partner is a trust, so no liability for destruction without negligence.
الخلط (al-khalṭ): Mixing of capitals; after mixing, individual ownership is indistinguishable, so destruction is shared.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if one partner's capital is destroyed before any purchase, what happens to the partnership?
A) The partnership continues with the remaining capital.
B) The partnership becomes void because the mutual condition is lost.
C) The other partner must compensate the loss.
D) The partnership is suspended until new capital is introduced.

Key Takeaway
Destruction of partnership capital before any trading voids the contract because the capital, as the specified subject matter, is analogous to the sold item in a sale.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate
8 min
Purchase by One Partner After Other's Capital Destroyed: Shared Ownership
Intra-Hanafi dispute on classification of partnership after capital loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shirkat 'aqd and shirkat milk in a scenario where one partner's capital is destroyed before a purchase, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Partnership rights vest at the time of purchase; subsequent loss of capital does not undo joint ownership.

Partnership law often tests the moment when rights attach. In this scenario, one partner buys with his own money after the other's capital is destroyed. Does the purchased item belong solely to the buyer or jointly? The Hanafi school holds it joint, but disagrees on the type of partnership formed. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
Two partners have a contract partnership. One partner's capital is destroyed. Before the destruction, a purchase was made with the other partner's capital. The question: is the purchased item jointly owned?
Key temporal point: purchase occurs after destruction, but before any dissolution.
2
State the general Hanafi ruling
The purchased item is jointly owned according to their prior condition because at the moment of purchase, the partnership existed (qiyam al-shirkah). Destruction after purchase does not change the vested ownership.
This is the agreed principle among Hanafis.
3
Introduce the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad holds this to be a shirkat 'aqd (contract-partnership with agency). Hasan ibn Ziyad considers it a shirkat milk (mere co-ownership without agency). Identify each position.
Imam Muhammad's view is from Zahir al-Riwayah; Hasan ibn Ziyad's from Nawadir.
4
Analyze the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under shirkat 'aqd, any partner can sell the entire item. Under shirkat milk, each can sell only his share. This affects the ability to transact with third parties.
The mufta bihi is Imam Muhammad's view, giving full agency to each partner.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Given the mufta bihi, state the legal consequences if one partner sells the item without the other's explicit permission.
This tests understanding of agency in shirkat 'aqd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ إِنِ اشْتَرى أَحَدُهُمَا بِمَالِهِ وَ هَلَكَ مَالُ الآخَرِ قَبْلَ الشَّرَاءِ فَالْمُشْتَرى بَيْنَهُمَا عَلَى مَاشَرَطًا لِأَنَّ الْمِلْكَ حِيْنَ وَقَعَ وَقَعَ مُشْتَرَكا بَيْنَهُمَا القِيَامِ الشَّرْكَةِ وَقتَ الشَّرَاءِ فَلَا يَتَغَيَّرُ الْحُكْمُ بِهَلَاكِ مَالِ الْآخَرِ بَعْدَ ذَالِكَ ثُمَّ الشركة شركة عَقْدٍ عِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ خِلَا فَالِلحَسَنِ ابْنِ زِيَادٍ حَتَّى أَنَّ أَيُّهُمَا بَاعَ جَازَ بَيْعُهُ لِأَنَّ الشَّرَكَةَ قَدَّتَمَّتْ فِي الْمُشْتَرى فَلَا يَنْتَقِضُ بِهَلَاكِ الْمَالِ بَعْدَ تَمَامِهَا
ترجمہ اور اگر دونوں میں سے ایک نے اپنے مال سے کچھ خریدا لیکن اس کے خریدنے سے پہلے ہی دوسرے کا مال ضائع ہو گیا تو جو چیز خریدی گئی ہو وہ ان دونوں میں ان کی شرط کے مطابق مشترک ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ جس وقت اس پر ملکیت ثابت ہوئی ہے وہ اس وقت دونوں میں مشترک تھی اس لئے اس کے بعد دوسرے کا مال ضائع ہو جانے سے پہلا حکم نہیں بدلے گا ۔ پھر امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک یہ شرکت عقد ہو گی اسی لئے ان دونوں شریکوں میں سے جو کوئی بھی اسے فروخت کرے گا وہ فروخت صحیح ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ خریدی ہوئی چیز میں شرکت پوری ہو چکی تھی ۔ اس لئے اس کے پورا ہو جانے کے بعد دوسرے کا مال ضائع ہو جانے سے شرکت میں فرق نہیں آئے گا بلکہ شرکت باقی رہے گی ۔ (حاصل کلام یہ ہوا کہ خریدی ہوئی چیز دونوں کی مشترکہ ملکیت ہے۔ اگر چہ اس کی قیمت صرف ایک شریک نے ادا کی ہے۔
And if one of them buys with his own capital, and the other’s capital is destroyed before the purchase, then the purchased item is between them according to their condition, because the ownership when it occurred, occurred as shared between them due to the existence of the partnership at the time of purchase. So the ruling does not change by the destruction of the other’s capital after that. Then, according to Muhammad, this partnership is a contract-partnership (shirkat ‘aqd), unlike al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, so that whichever of them sells, his sale is valid, because the partnership has completed in the purchased item, so it is not annulled by the destruction of the capital after its completion. Translation: And if one of them buys something with his own capital, but before his purchase the other’s capital is destroyed, then the purchased item will be shared between them according to their condition. Because at the moment ownership was established, it was shared between them due to the existence of the partnership at the time of purchase. Therefore, the subsequent destruction of the other’s capital does not change the initial ruling. Then, according to Imam Muhammad, this partnership is a contract-partnership (shirkat ‘aqd), unlike Hasan ibn Ziyad. Therefore, whichever partner sells it, his sale is valid, because partnership in the purchased item was completed. So the destruction of the capital after that does not affect the partnership; it remains intact. (Conclusion: the purchased item is jointly owned by both, even though only one partner paid the price.)
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage addresses a nuanced scenario: one partner makes a purchase with his own capital, but before he does so, the other partner’s capital is destroyed. The ruling holds that the purchased item is jointly owned (mushtarak) between them according to their prior condition (shart) in the partnership contract. The reasoning is that at the moment ownership (milk) attached to the purchased item, the partnership was still in effect, so the purchase inures to the common benefit. The subsequent destruction of the other’s capital (after the purchase) does not change that because the ownership vested at the time of purchase. An intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is noted: Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) considers this to be a shirkat ‘aqd (partnership by contract) such that each partner has the authority to sell the whole item on behalf of both, while Hasan ibn Ziyad may consider it a shirkat milk (co-ownership without agency) where each can sell only his share. Muhammad’s view is that since the partnership was completed in the purchased item, the contract-partnership remains intact, and the destruction of the other’s capital does not dissolve it. The practical consequence: the buying partner can recover his share of the price from the other partner (as will be elaborated in the next ruling). This upholds the principle that rights vest at the time of transaction, and subsequent events affecting one party do not retroactively undo vested rights.

Key Terms
شركة عقد (shirkat ‘aqd): A partnership by contract where each partner is an agent for the other in trading and disposition.
شركة ملك (shirkat milk): Co-ownership without agency; each owner can only dispose of his own share.
القيام الشركة (qiyām al-shirkah): The existence of the partnership at the time of purchase.
التمام (al-tamām): Completion; the partnership in the purchased item is perfected and cannot be undone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what type of partnership is created when one partner buys with his own capital after the other's capital is destroyed?
A) Shirkat milk (co-ownership)
B) Shirkat 'aqd (contract-partnership)
C) The partnership is void
D) It is a mudarabah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, if a partner purchases with his own capital while the other's capital is lost, the item is jointly owned as a shirkat 'aqd, allowing any partner to sell the whole.

Paying Partner's Recourse in Voided Partnership with Explicit Agency
Clarifies the paying partner's recourse against the other for a share of the price when explicit agency exists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that an explicit agency clause in a partnership survives the voiding of the contract, allowing the paying partner to recover his share and creating co-ownership.

Core Idea
Explicit agency in a partnership can survive the voiding of the contract, creating co-ownership (shirkat milk).

This passage addresses a critical scenario in Hanafi partnership law: what happens when one partner pays the full price from his own money after the other partner's capital is destroyed? The text clarifies that if the partners explicitly stated an agency clause in the partnership contract, the paying partner can still recover the other partner's share from him, even if the partnership contract itself is voided. The basis is that the explicit agency creates a separate legal relationship that results in co-ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the paying partner's claim for reimbursement. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) — the partner can recover the share from the co-partner.
Focus on the legal effect: the paying partner has a right of recourse.
2
Locate the basis of the ruling
The basis (dalil) is agency (wakālah). The paying partner bought the item partly as an agent for the other partner, having paid the full price from his own wealth. Thus, he is entitled to reimbursement for the portion belonging to the other.
The proof is rational (dalīl ‘aqlī) based on the principle that an agent who pays from his own funds can reclaim from the principal.
3
Distinguish the two scenarios
Scenario (a): One partner buys with one of the two capitals (e.g., the common fund) after the other’s capital is destroyed – this has been explained earlier. Scenario (b): The other partner’s capital is destroyed first, then the remaining partner buys using the other’s capital, but *if they explicitly stated agency in the contract*, the purchase is jointly owned.
The key is the presence of an explicit agency clause (tashrīḥ bil-wikālah).
4
Determine the outcome and type of ownership
Even if the partnership contract is voided (due to loss of capital), the explicit agency remains valid. Consequently, the purchased item becomes co-owned (shirkat milk) by virtue of agency, and the paying partner can recover his share from the other.
This shows that explicit agency can create shared ownership independent of the voided partnership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيَرْجِعُ عَلَى شَرِيكِهِ بِحِصَّةٍ مِنْ ثَمَنِهِ لانَّهُ اشْتَرى نِصْفَهُ بِوَكَالَتِهِ وَنَقَدَ الثَّمَنَ مِنْ مَالِ نَفْسِهِ وَقَدْ بَيَّنَاهُ هَذَا إِذَاشْتَرى أَحَدُهُمَا بِأَحَدِ الْمَالَيْنِ أَو لَا تُمَّ هَلَكَ مَالُ الْآخَرِ أَمَّا إِذَا هَلَكَ مَالُ أَحَدِهِمَا ثُمَّ اشْتَرَى الْأَخَرُ بِمَالِ الأخرانُ صَرَّحَا بِالْوَكَالَةِ فِي عَقدِ الشَّرُكَةِ فَالْمُشْتَرَى مُشْتَرَك بَيْنَهُمَا عَلى مَاشَرَطًا لِأَنَّ السّرُكَةَ إِنْ بَطَلَتْ فَالْوَكَالَةُ الْمُصَرَّحُ بِهَا قَائِمَةً فَكَانَ مُشْتَرَكًا بِحُكْمِ الْوَكَالَةِ وَيَكُونُ شِرْكَةُ مِلْکَ وَيَرْجِعُ عَلَى شَرِيكَ بِحِمَّتِهِ
He said: And he recovers from his partner the share from its price, because he bought half of it by his agency and paid the price from his own wealth – and we have explained it. This is when one of them buys with one of the two capitals, or when the other’s capital is destroyed. However, if the capital of one of them is destroyed, then the other buys with the other’s capital, and they explicitly stated agency in the partnership contract, then the purchased item is shared between them according to their condition, because even if the partnership is voided, the explicitly stated agency remains, so it is shared by virtue of agency, and it is co-ownership (shirkat milk), and he recovers from his partner his share.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This final passage reiterates the rule of recourse (rujū‘): the partner who paid the price from his own money can claim the corresponding share from his co-partner. The basis is that he bought the item partly as an agent (wakīl) for the other partner, having paid the full price out of his own pocket; thus he is entitled to reimbursement for the portion belonging to the other. The text distinguishes two scenarios: (1) where one partner buys with one of the two capitals (presumably the common fund or his own) and the other’s capital is destroyed after the purchase – this has been explained earlier. (2) Where one partner’s capital is destroyed first, and then the other partner buys using the *other’s* capital, but *if they explicitly included an agency clause* (tashrīḥ bil-wikālah) in the partnership contract, then even if the partnership contract may be voided (due to loss of capital), the explicit agency survives. Consequently, the purchased item is jointly owned by them as co-ownership (shirkat milk) by virtue of agency, and the buying partner can still recover his share from the other. This shows that explicit agency can create a shared ownership independent of the voided partnership contract. The ruling underscores the importance of explicit terms in partnership contracts.

Key Terms
الرجوع بحصة (al-rujū‘ bi-ḥiṣṣah): To reclaim the proportional share of the price from the co-partner.
وكالة مصرح بها (wakālah muṣarraḥ bihā): Agency explicitly mentioned in the contract; it remains valid even if the main contract is voided.
شركة ملك (shirkat milk): Co-ownership without agency; partners own shares but cannot bind each other in further transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one partner's capital is destroyed and then the other buys using the remaining capital, but they had explicitly stated agency in the contract, what type of ownership is created?
A) Shirkat 'aqd (contract partnership)
B) Shirkat milk (co-ownership)
C) No ownership; the purchase is void
D) Sole ownership by the buyer

Key Takeaway
Explicit agency in a partnership can survive the voiding of the main contract, enabling the paying partner to recover his share and establishing co-ownership.

Partnership Void When Capital Destroyed
Statement on partnership dissolution upon loss of capital.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that partnership becomes void when capital is destroyed, and explain the conditions under which the loss is borne by the owner versus shared.

Core Idea
If the capital of one or both partners is lost, the partnership dissolves; the owner bears the loss unless the capitals were mixed.

In this passage, we examine a key ruling in Hanafi partnership law: the effect of capital destruction. The author explains that the contract becomes void if any partner's capital is lost, and clarifies who bears the loss. Understanding this requires grasping the distinction between mixed and unmixed capital, and the trust nature of property in a partner's hands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Determine the legal status of a partnership when capital is destroyed. The text states that partnership becomes void (batil) whether one or both capitals are lost.
2
Understand the reasoning
The remaining partner's consent was conditional on mutual contribution. Without the other's capital, he would not agree to share his own capital alone, so the contract becomes useless.
3
Apply the loss liability rule
The owner of the destroyed capital bears the loss; the other partner is not a guarantor because the property was held as a trust (amanah). This applies whether the capital was lost in the owner's possession or the partner's.
4
Distinguish the mixed capital exception
If capitals were mixed before destruction, the loss is shared proportionally because the property is indistinguishable. The partnership still becomes void, but liability is joint.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
The distinction between mixed and unmixed capital is crucial for determining liability in dissolution. In modern partnerships, this affects how losses are allocated when assets are commingled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحاصل مال برباد ہونے سے شرکت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ پھر اس صورت میں جبکہ دونوں مال ہلاک ہو جائیں تو اس میں شرکت کا باطل ہونا تو ظاہر ہے۔ اور اگر صرف ایک کا مال ضائع ہو تو بھی شرکت باطل ہوگئی۔ کیونکہ جس کا مال ضائع نہیں ہوا ہے وہ اپنے مال میں دوسرے کو شریک کرنے پر صرف اس طرح سے راضی ہوا تھا کہ وہ خود بھی اس مال میں شریک ہو۔ اور اب جبکہ اس کا مال ہی باقی نہ رہا تو یہ اپنے مال میں شریک کرنے پر راضی نہیں ہوگا۔ لہذا عقد شرکت باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اس کا باقی رہنا بے فائدہ ہوگا۔ اور دونوں میں سے جس کسی کا مال ضائع ہوگا اسی کا مال ضائع ہو گا یعنی دوسرا شخص اس کا ضامن بالکل نہیں ہوگا) کیونکہ اگر خود اس کے قبضہ میں رہتے ہوئے ضائع ہوا جب تو بات واضح ہے۔ اور اگر دوسرے شریک کے قبضہ میں رہتے ہوئے ضائع ہوا تو بھی ضمان لازم نہیں آئے گا کیونکہ وہ مال اس کے قبضہ میں بطور امانت تھا۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر دونوں کا مال ملا دیا گیا اس کے بعد وہ ہلاک ہوا تو اس صورت میں اس کی بربادی بھی مشترک یعنی دونوں شریکوں کے مال سے مشترکہ ہلاک سمجھا جائے گا کیونکہ مال میں کوئی امتیاز نہیں رہتا ہے کہ کس کا ہلاک ہوا اور کس کا باقی رہا۔ اس لئے دونوں مالوں سے ہی ہلاک ہونا کہا جائے گا۔
The result: Partnership becomes void upon the destruction of capital. In the case where both capitals are destroyed, the invalidity of partnership is obvious. And if only one person's capital is lost, still the partnership becomes void. Because the one whose capital is not lost had consented to make the other a partner in his capital only on the condition that he himself would also be a partner in that capital. And now when his own capital no longer remains, he will not agree to make the other a partner in his capital alone. Therefore, the contract of partnership becomes void because its continuation would be useless. And whichever of the two loses his capital, that loss is incurred by him alone, meaning the other person is not at all a guarantor for it. Because if it was lost while in his own possession, it is clear. And if it was lost while in the possession of the other partner, still guarantee does not become necessary because that property was in his possession as a trust. Contrary to this, if both capitals were mixed together and then destroyed, in that case its destruction is considered joint, meaning from the combined wealth of both partners, because there remains no distinction as to whose was destroyed and whose remained. Therefore, it is said to be destroyed from both capitals.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the dissolution of partnership when capital is destroyed. The author explains that partnership becomes void when either one or both capitals are lost. The reasoning is that the partner whose capital remains intact only agreed to share profits on condition of mutual contribution; if the other's capital is gone, he would not consent to share his own capital alone. The loss falls solely on the owner of the destroyed capital, even if it was in the other partner's possession as a trust (amanah). However, if the capitals were mixed (khalit) before destruction, the loss is shared proportionally because the property is indistinguishable. This distinction between mixed and unmixed capital is crucial for determining liability.

Key Terms
شرکت (shirkah): A partnership contract where two or more persons contribute capital and share profits.
امانت (amanah): A trust; property held by a person without liability for loss unless negligence occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one partner's capital is destroyed while in the other partner's possession, who bears the loss?
A) The partner in whose possession it was
B) The owner of the capital
C) Both partners equally
D) The partnership as a shared loss

Key Takeaway
Partnership becomes void when capital is destroyed; the owner bears the loss unless capitals were mixed.
