Purchase After One Partner's Capital Lost: Agency and Joint Ownership
Ruling on joint ownership after capital loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when one partner purchases goods after the other's capital is destroyed, and explain the difference between explicit and implied agency in determining joint ownership.

Core Idea
Joint ownership of a purchase is determined at the time of acquisition; subsequent capital loss does not undo it.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific partnership scenario: one partner's capital is lost, and then the other buys with his own money. The ruling turns on whether the purchase occurred while the partnership contract was still valid, and whether agency was explicitly stated. Understanding this distinction clarifies the nature of partnership (shirkat al-'aqd vs. shirkat al-milk) and the effect of agency within it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The first scenario: Partner A buys after Partner B's capital was destroyed before the purchase. Ruling: the purchased item is joint according to their condition.
This is the main ruling of the passage.
2
Identify the proof (dalil) for joint ownership
Ownership at the time of purchase was joint because partnership existed. The destruction of capital later does not change the ruling.
The proof is the existence of partnership at the time of purchase.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad considers it a contractual partnership (shirkat al-'aqd), meaning each can sell independently. Hasan ibn Ziyad considers it an ownership partnership (shirkat al-milk), requiring joint consent.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is who can sell the item.
4
Apply to the second scenario and distinguish based on agency
If capital is destroyed first, then the other buys: if explicit agency was stated, the item is joint (shirkat al-milk). If only general partnership without explicit agency, the purchase belongs solely to the buyer.
Explicit agency survives the dissolution of the partnership; implied agency does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ إِنِ اشْتَرى أَحَدُهُمَا بِمَالِهِ وَ هَلَكَ مَالُ الآخَرِ قَبْلَ الشَّرَاءِ فَالْمُشْتَرى بَيْنَهُمَا عَلَى مَاشَرَطًا لِأَنَّ الْمِلْكَ حِيْنَ وَقَعَ وَقَعَ مُشْتَرَكا بَيْنَهُمَا القِيَامِ الشَّرْكَةِ وَقتَ الشَّرَاءِ فَلَا يَتَغَيَّرُ الْحُكْمُ بِهَلَاكِ مَالِ الْآخَرِ بَعْدَ ذَالِكَ ثُمَّ الشركة شركة عَقْدٍ عِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ خِلَا فَالِلحَسَنِ ابْنِ زِيَادٍ حَتَّى أَنَّ أَيُّهُمَا بَاعَ جَازَ بَيْعُهُ لِأَنَّ الشَّرَكَةَ قَدَّتَمَّتْ فِي الْمُشْتَرى فَلَا يَنْتَقِضُ بِهَلَاكِ الْمَالِ بَعْدَ تَمَامِهَا قَالَ وَيَرْجِعُ عَلَى شَرِيكِهِ بِحِصَّةٍ مِنْ ثَمَنِهِ لانَّهُ اشْتَرى نِصْفَهُ بِوَكَالَتِهِ وَنَقَدَ الثَّمَنَ مِنْ مَالِ نَفْسِهِ وَقَدْ بَيَّنَاهُ هَذَا إِذَاشْتَرى أَحَدُهُمَا بِأَحَدِ الْمَالَيْنِ أَو لَا تُمَّ هَلَكَ مَالُ الْآخَرِ أَمَّا إِذَا هَلَكَ مَالُ أَحَدِهِمَا ثُمَّ اشْتَرَى الْأَخَرُ بِمَالِهِ فَإِنْ صَرَّحَا بِالْوَكَالَةِ فِي عَقدِ الشَّرُكَةِ فَالْمُشْتَرَى مُشْتَرَك بَيْنَهُمَا عَلى مَاشَرَطًا لِأَنَّ الشَّرَكَةَ إِنْ بَطَلَتْ فَالْوَكَالَةُ الْمُصَرَّحُ بِهَا قَائِمَةً فَكَانَ مُشْتَرَكًا بِحُكْمِ الْوَكَالَةِ وَيَكُونُ شِرْكَةُ مِلْکَ وَيَرْجِعُ عَلَى شَرِيكَ بِحِمَّتِهِ مِنَ الشَّمَنِ لِمَابَيْنَاهُ وَإِنْ ذَكَرَ امُجَرَّدَ الشَّرَكَةِ وَلَمْ يَمُمَّا عَلَى الْوَكَالَةِ فِيهَا كَانَ الْمُشْتَرى لِلَّذِى اشْتَرَاهُ خَاصَّةً لأنَّ الوقوع عَلَى الشَّرَكَةِ حُكُمُ الْوَكَالَةِ الَّتِي تَضَمَنتْهَا الشَّرُكَةُ فَإِذَا بَطَلَتْ يَنْظُلُ مَافِي ضِمْنِهَا بِخِلَافِ ما إذا صَرَحَ بِالْوَكَالَةِ لِأَنَّهَا مَقْصُودَةٌ
And if one of them buys with his own capital, and the other's capital was destroyed before the purchase, then the purchased item is between them according to their condition, because ownership at the time it occurred was joint between them due to the existence of partnership at the time of purchase. So the ruling does not change by the destruction of the other's capital after that. Then the partnership is a contract of partnership according to Muhammad, contrary to Hasan ibn Ziyad, such that whichever of them sells, his sale is valid, because partnership has been completed in the purchased item, so it is not broken by the destruction of capital after its completion. He said: And he will recourse against his partner for a share of its price, because he bought half of it by his agency and paid the price from his own money. And we have explained this. This is when one of them bought with one of the two capitals and then the other's capital was destroyed. As for when the capital of one of them was destroyed, then the other bought with his capital: if they explicitly stated agency in the contract of partnership, then the purchased item is joint between them according to their condition, because even if the partnership becomes void, the explicitly stated agency remains. So it becomes joint by virtue of the agency, and it will be a partnership of ownership (shirkat al-milk). And he will recourse against his partner for his share of the price, as we explained. And if they mentioned mere partnership and did not explicitly mention agency in it, then the purchased item belongs specifically to the one who bought it, because the occurrence of partnership is a ruling of the agency that was implied in the partnership. So when the partnership becomes void, what was implied falls. Contrary to when they explicitly mentioned agency, because it is intended.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute. It addresses the scenario where one partner buys an item with his own capital after the other partner's capital has been destroyed prior to the purchase. The text rules that the purchased item is jointly owned according to their agreed profit-sharing condition, because ownership was established at the time of purchase when the partnership was still valid. Subsequently, the destruction of the other partner's capital does not affect the joint ownership. According to Imam Muhammad, this type of partnership is a contract of partnership (shirkat al-'aqd), as opposed to the position of Hasan ibn Ziyad who considered it a partnership of ownership. Consequently, either partner may sell the item because the partnership in the purchased item has been perfected. The text then explains the recourse: the buying partner can claim a share of the price from the other partner proportionate to his share, as he bought the other's share as an agent. A further distinction is made: if the other's capital was destroyed first and then the remaining partner buys, the outcome depends on whether agency was explicitly mentioned. If explicit agency was stated, the purchased item becomes joint property by virtue of the agency (which survives the dissolution of the partnership), but it is a partnership of ownership (shirkat al-milk) not a contractual partnership. If no explicit agency was mentioned, the purchase belongs solely to the buyer because the implied agency in the partnership contract falls when the partnership becomes void.

Key Terms
شركة عقد (shirkat al-'aqd): A partnership established by contract, where each partner is an agent for the other in trading.
شركة ملك (shirkat al-milk): Joint ownership of an asset without a contract of agency for further trade.
وکالت (wakalah): Agency; one partner authorizes the other to act on his behalf in purchases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if one partner's capital is destroyed and then the other buys with his own capital without explicit agency, who owns the purchased item?
A) Both partners jointly
B) Only the buyer
C) The partner whose capital was destroyed
D) It is divided according to profit-sharing ratio

Key Takeaway
Joint ownership of a purchase is determined at the time of acquisition; explicit agency preserves joint ownership even after partnership dissolves, while implied agency does not.

Shirkah — Partnership

Partnership Valid Without Mixing Capital: Hanafi View
Ruling and proof that partnership does not require mixing of capital.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the necessity of mixing capital in partnership and explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) used, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i and Zufar's view.

Core Idea
Partnership is valid without mixing capital because the contract itself creates the sharing, not the physical mixing.

This lesson examines a fundamental dispute in partnership law: is physical mixing of capital a prerequisite for a valid partnership? The Hanafi school, supported by a rational proof, holds that the contract alone suffices. We will explore the opposing view of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i, understand their reasoning, and see how the Hanafi response relies on the nature of currency and the essence of partnership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
Read the first sentence of the passage to extract the clear Hanafi position on mixing capital.
The matn states: 'Partnership is permissible even if they do not mix the capital.'
2
Identify the opposing view and its proponents
Note who disagrees and what they require: Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) and al-Shafi'i require mixing.
The text says: 'Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: Partnership is not permissible except after mixing.'
3
Understand the opponents' rationale
The opponents argue that the subject matter of partnership is capital, so it must be common; they also analogize to mudarabah. The text outlines their position.
They also derive further conditions: unity of type, mixing, no disparity in profit with equal capital, and invalidity of service partnerships.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school provides two rational proofs: (1) Partnership in profit is based on the contract, not on capital; (2) Dirhams and dinars are fungible, so profit derives from trade, not from the capital itself.
The text states: 'Partnership in profit is based on the contract, not on capital, because the contract is called partnership.' And 'dirhams and dinars are not specific, so profit is not derived from the capital itself.'
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical consequences: if mixing is not required, partnerships in services (shirkat al-a'mal) become valid, as they involve no capital to mix.
The opponents reject service partnerships due to lack of capital; the Hanafis accept them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيَجُوزُ الشّركَةُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَحْلُطَ الْمَالَ وَقَالَ زُفَرَ وَ الشَّافِعِى لَا يَجُوزُ الشَّرُكَةُ إِلَّا بَعْدَ الْخَلْطِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ المَحَلَّ هُوَ المَالُ وَلهذا يُضَافُ تَعِينُ رَأْسِ الْمَالِ بِخِلَافِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ لِأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ بِشِرُكَةٍ وَإِنَّمَا هُوَ يَعْمَلُ لِرَبِّ الْمَالِ فَيَسْتَحِقُ الرّبعَ عَمَّا عَلَى عَمَلِهِ أَمَّاهُنَا بِخِلَافِه وَهَذا أَصَلُّ كَبِيرٌ لَهُمَا حَتَّى يُعتبر اتِّحَادُ الْجِنْسِ وَيُشْتَرَطُ الخلطُ وَلاَ يَجُوزُ التَّفَاضُلُ في الربح مَعَ السَّسَاوِي فِى الْمَالِ وَلَا يجوز شركَةُ التَقَبلِ وَالْاِعْمَالِ لاِنْعِدَامِ الْمَالِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الشَّرَكَةِ فِي الربح مُسْتَيْدَةَ إِلَى الْعَقْدِ دُونَ الْمَالِ لِأَنَّ العَقْدَيُسَمَّى شِرُكَةً فَلَابُدَّ مِنْ تَحَقَّقِ مَعْنى هذَا الْإِسْمِ فِيهِ فَلَمْ يَكُن الخَلْطُ شَرُطًا وَلانَّ الدَّرَاهِم وَالدَّنَانِيرَ لَا يَتَعَيَّنَانِ فَلَا يُسْتَفَادُ الرَّبْحُ بِرأْسِ الْمَالِ وَإِنَّمَا يُسْتَفَادُ بِالتَّصَرُّفِ لِأَنَّهُ فِي النِّصْفِ
He said: Partnership is permissible even if they do not mix the capital. And Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: Partnership is not permissible except after mixing. And this is because the subject matter is capital, and for this reason the capital is specified (unlike mudarabah). Because mudarabah is not a partnership; rather, the worker works for the owner of capital and becomes entitled to a share (quarter) of the profit for his work. Here it is different. And this is a major principle for them: they require that the type be unified, mixing is a condition, disparity in profit with equality in capital is not allowed, and partnership in acceptance and labor is not allowed due to lack of capital. And our (Hanafi) argument is that partnership in profit is based on the contract, not on capital, because the contract is called partnership, so the meaning of this name must be realized in it. Thus mixing is not a condition. Also, dirhams and dinars are not specific, so profit is not derived from the capital itself; rather it is derived from transaction, because it is in half.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the necessity of mixing capital (khalit) for a valid partnership. The Hanafi position, attributed to the author (and the matn), states that partnership is valid even without physically mixing the capital. Opponents are Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar who differed) and Imam al-Shafi'i. They argue that mixing is essential because the subject of partnership is the capital, and it must be indistinguishable for joint ownership. They also draw an analogy with mudarabah (silent partnership), but the text distinguishes mudarabah from shirkah. The opponents' position leads to further conditions: unity of type (jins), mixing, no disparity in profit with equal capital, and invalidity of partnerships in services (shirkat al-a'mal) and acceptance (shirkat al-taqabbul) due to lack of capital. The Hanafi proof is twofold: First, partnership in profit is established by the contract itself, not by the capital. The term 'shirkah' implies sharing, which is realized by the agreement. Second, dirhams and dinars are fungible (non-specific) goods; profit arises from trading activities, not from the capital itself. Therefore, mixing is not a prerequisite.

Key Terms
خلط المال (khalit al-mal): Physically mixing the capital contributions of partners so they become indistinguishable.
شركة الأعمال (shirkat al-a'mal): Partnership in providing services, where partners contribute labor rather than capital.
مضاربة (mudarabah): A silent partnership where one partner provides capital and the other provides labor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof for partnership being valid without mixing capital?
A) Quranic verses on trade
B) Partnership in profit is based on the contract, not on the capital itself
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Customary practice of merchants

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require physical mixing of capital for a valid partnership; the contract itself establishes the sharing arrangement.

Shirkah — Partnership

Purchase After Partner's Capital Lost: Implicit vs Explicit Agency
Ruling on purchase after partner's capital lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between explicit and implicit agency in a void partnership and determine whether a purchase is shared or solely the buyer's property.

Core Idea
In a void partnership, only explicit agency preserves shared ownership; implied agency falls with the partnership.

When a partner loses his capital before a purchase, the validity of the partnership is broken. But what happens if the remaining partner buys something? The Hanafi school gives a nuanced answer depending on whether the partners had explicitly appointed each other as agents or merely relied on the implied agency that comes with partnership. This lesson unpacks that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline scenario
Assume a partnership where one partner's capital is lost before the other partner makes a purchase with his own money. The partnership is now void (fāsid) because the capital condition is not met.
2
Recognize the two sub-scenarios
The text divides cases: (1) partners explicitly declared agency (wakāla ṣarīḥa) in their contract, and (2) they only mentioned partnership without explicit agency, relying on the implied agency (ḍimniyya) that partnership contains.
3
Apply the ruling to explicit agency
If explicit agency was stated, the purchase is shared (shirkat al-milk) between both partners, and the buyer can claim reimbursement for the other's share. Reason: explicit agency is an independent contract that survives the void partnership.
Explicit agency is maqṣūda (intended for its own sake).
4
Apply the ruling to implicit agency only
If only partnership was mentioned, the purchase belongs solely to the buyer. The implied agency falls when the partnership becomes void, because it was dependent on the partnership.
The implied agency is a ruling of the partnership; when the partnership is void, its rulings fall.
5
Distill the principle
The key legal principle: an explicit contract (wakāla) is independent and does not automatically terminate with a void partnership, whereas an implied authority derived from the partnership vanishes with it.
This is based on rational reasoning: the explicit is intended, the implied is incidental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الَّذِي أَدَّى الثَّمَنَ لِمَابَيْنَاهُ وَإِنْ ذَكَرَ امُجَرَّدَ الشَّرَكَةِ وَلَمْ يَمُمَّا عَلَى الْوَكَالَةِ فِيهَا كَانَ الْمُشْتَرى لِلَّذِى اشْتَرَاهُ خَاصَّةً لِأَنَّ الوُقُوعَ عَلَى الشَّرَكَةِ حُكُمُ الْوَكَالَةِ الَّتِي تَضَمَنْتَهَا الشَّرُكَةُ فَإِذَا بَطَلَتْ يَنْظُلُ مَافِي ضِمْنِهَا بِخِلَافِ ما إذا صَرَّحَ بِالْوَكَالَةِ لِأَنَّهَا مَقْصُودَةٌ
ترجمہ پھر جس شریک نے مال کی قیمت ادا کی ہے وہ اپنے دوسرے شریک سے اس کے حصہ کے برابر اس کی قیمت سے وصول کر لے گا۔ کیونکہ اس شریک نے وکیل کے طور پر دوسرے شریک کا نصف حصہ خریدا ہے۔ لیکن پوری قیمت اپنی جیب سے ادا کر دی تھی ۔ اس مسئلہ کو ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ یہ حکم اس صورت میں ہو گا جبکہ ایک شریک نے اپنے مال سے کوئی چیز خرید لی اس کے بعد دوسرے کا مال ضائع ہو گیا ہو ۔ اور اگر یہ صورت ہو کہ ایک شریک کا مال پہلے ہی ضائع ہو گیا پھر دوسرے شریک نے اپنے مال سے کوئی چیز خریدی تو اس میں دو صورتیں ہیں،
ا۔ ایک یہ کہ عقد شرکت میں دونوں نے وکالت کی تصریح کردی ہو تو اس صورت میں خریدی ہوئی چیز دونوں شریکوں کے درمیان مقررہ شرط کے مطابق مشترک ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اگر شرکت باطل ہوتی تو صراحت کے ساتھ وکیل بنادینے کی بات اب بھی موجود ہے ۔ اسی لئے وہ چیز وکالت کی بناء پر دونوں میں مشترک ہو گئی ۔ لیکن یہ شرکت ملک ہوگی یعنی شرکت عقد نہ ہوگی اور خریدنے والا اپنے شریک سے اس کے حصہ کے مطابق قیمت واپس لے لے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ شخص دوسرے شریک کا وکیل تھا اور اپنا ذاتی رو پید اس کی خریداری میں دیا ہے۔
اور دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ دونوں نے صرف عقد شرکت کا ذکر کیا اور اس میں ایک دوسرے کو وکیل بنانے کی تصریح نہیں کی ۔ پس اس صورت میں جو چیز خریدی گئی ہے وہ خاص اس کے خریدنے والے کی ہوگی کیونکہ ایسی خریداری میں شرکت اسی وکالت میں ہوتی ہے جو عقد شرکت کے ضمن میں ہو مگر جب شرکت ہی باطل ہوئی ہو تو اس کے ضمن میں جو وکالت پائی جاتی ہو وہ بھی باطل ہو جاتی ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر وکالت کو ضمنا نہیں بلکہ صراحت کے ساتھ بیان کیا ہو تو وہ باطل نہیں ہوتی ہے کیونکہ وہ تو ارادہ اور قصد کے ساتھ بیان ہوئی ہے اور ضمنی نہیں ہوئی ہے۔
Then the one who paid the price... as we explained. And if they mention merely the partnership and do not mention agency in it, the purchase is for the one who bought it specifically, because the occurrence [of the purchase] on the basis of partnership is a ruling of the agency that the partnership contained. So when [the partnership] becomes void, what is implied in it falls. Contrary to when they explicitly mention agency, because it is intended [separately].
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage states the ruling when one partner buys goods with his own money after the other partner's capital is lost. The author explains two scenarios: First, if the partners explicitly appointed each other as agents (wakala) in the partnership contract, then even if the partnership is void, the purchase is still shared between them as a joint ownership (shirkat al-milk) because the explicit agency remains valid. The buyer can recover from the other partner his share of the price. Second, if they only agreed on partnership without explicit agency, then the purchase belongs solely to the buyer because the implied agency from the partnership falls when the partnership is void. The key distinction is whether agency was explicitly intended or merely implied.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakāla): Agency; authorization to act on behalf of another in a transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a partnership is void (fāsid) but the partners had explicitly appointed each other as agents (wakāla ṣarīḥa) before purchasing, what is the status of goods purchased by one partner with his own money after the other's capital was lost?
A) The goods belong solely to the buying partner.
B) The goods are shared (shirkat al-milk) between both partners.
C) The partnership is revived automatically.
D) The goods are considered a loan from the buyer to the other partner.

Key Takeaway
Explicit agency is an independent contract that survives a void partnership, while implied agency falls with the partnership — this determines shared or sole ownership of a purchase.

Partnership Without Mixing Capital: Hanafi vs. Zufar/Shafi'i
Dispute on whether mixing capital is a condition for valid partnership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on mixing capital in partnership and evaluate the opposing proof based on the capital-profit analogy.

Core Idea
Mixing capital is not required for a valid partnership; partnership is a contract, not property co-ownership.

In the Hanafi school, a partnership contract (shirkat al-ʿaqd) is valid even if the partners do not physically mix their capital. This lesson examines the dispute between the Hanafi majority and Imam Zufar (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafiʿi, who require mixing as a condition. We will explore the proof structures on both sides and understand the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the text: partnership is valid even without mixing capital. Note that this is the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
The Hanafi position is based on the nature of the contract.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam Zufar (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafiʿi require mixing of capital. Understand their analogy: profit is a branch of capital, so mixing the original is necessary.
This is a classic ikhtilaf within and across madhahib.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Trace the opponent's reasoning: profit is attributed to capital (thamarat al-māl), hence sharing profit requires sharing capital through mixing. This is supported by the custom of specifying capital.
The opponent also argues that in mudaraba mixing is not required because it is not a true partnership.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) Profit is attributed to the contract (ʿaqd) and to transaction (taṣarruf), not to capital itself. (2) Dirhams and dinars are fungible and not specified in a contract, so profit is not tied to specific coins. The partnership in transaction (through agency) suffices for sharing profit.
Hanafis also analogize to mudaraba, where mixing is not required, to show consistency.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequences: If mixing is not required, partnerships are easier to form, and forms like shirkat al-taqabbul (partnership of acceptance) become valid. Also, equality of profit is not required when capital is unequal.
This shows how the dispute affects actual contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيَجُوزُ الشّركَةُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَحْلُطَ الْمَالَ وَقَالَ زُفَرَ وَ الشَّافِعِى لَا يَل : المال ولا ) عَلَى الشَّرُكَةِ إِلَّا بَعْدَ الشَّرُكَةِ فِي الْأَصْلِ وَإِنَّهُ بِالْخَلْطِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ المَحَلَّ هُوَ المَالُ وَلهذا يُضَافُ ، تَعِينُ رَأْسِ الْمَالِ بِخِلَافِ الْمُضَارَبَةِ لِأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ بِشِرُكَةٍ وَإِنَّمَا هُوَ يَعْمَلُ لِرَبِّ الْمَالِ فَيَسْتَحِقُ الرّبعَ عَمَّا عَلَى عَمَلِهِ أَمَّاهُنَا بِخِلَافِه وَهَذا أَصَلُّ كَبِيرٌ لَهُمَا حَتَّى يُعتبر اتِّحَادُ الْجِنْسِ وَيُشْتَرَطُ الخلطُ وَلاَ يَجُوزُ التَّفَاضُلُ في الربح مَعَ السَّسَاوِي فِى الْمَالِ وَلَا يجوز شركَةُ التَقَبلِ وَالْاِعْمَالِ لاِنْعِدَامِ الْمَالِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الشَّرَكَةِ فِي الربح مُسْتَيْدَةَ إِلَى الْعَقْدِدُونَ الْمَالِ لِأَنَّ العَقْدَيُسَمَّى شِرُكَةً فَلَابُدَّ مِنْ تَحَقَّقِ مَعْنى هذَا الْإِسْمِ فِيهِ فَلَمْ يَكُن الخَلْطُ شَرُطًا وَلانَّ الدَّرَاهِم وَالدَّنَانِيرَ لَا يَتَعَيَّنَانِ فَلَا يُسْتَفَادُ الرَّبْحُ بِرأْسِ الْمَالِ وَإِنَّمَا يُسْتَفَادُ بِالتَّصَرُّفِ لِأَنَّهُ فِي النِّصْفِ أصيل وفى التصفِ وَكِيلُ وَإِذَا تَحَقَّقَتِ الشَّرْكَةُ فِي التَّصَرُّفِ بِدُونَ الْخَلْطِ تَحَقَّقَتُ فِى الْمُسْتَفَادِيه وَهُوَ الرّبْحُ بِدُونِه وَصَارَ كَالْمُضَارَبَةِ فَلَا يَشْتَرَطَ اِتِّحَادُ الْجِنْسِ وَالسَّسَاوِى فِى الرّبْحِ وَتَصحُ شِرُكَةُ التَّقَدِل
ترجمہ اور قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ ۔ دو شریکوں نے اگر چہ مال خلط ملط نہ کیا ہو پھر بھی اس میں شرکت جائز ہوگی با یہی قول امام مالک واحد رحمہما اللہ کا بھی ہے ) اور امام زفر و شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہما نے کہا ہے کہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ شرکت میں مال اصل اور اس کا نفع اس کی فرع ہے۔ فرع اس وقت مشترک ہوگی جبکہ اصل مشترک ہو جائے۔ اور اصل اس وقت مشترک ہوگی جبکہ مال مخلوط ہو اور نفع کو مال کے لئے فرع کہنا اس بناء پر ہے کہ اس کا محل مال ہے۔ اسی لئے نفع کو مال کی طرف منسوب اور مضاف کرتے ہیں۔ جیسا کہ کہا جاتا ہے کہ مالی شرکت کرنے سے مال کا یہ نفع ہوا ہے۔ لیکن اس میں راس المال (اصلی پونجی ) کو متعین کر لینا ایک شرط ہے۔ بخلاف مضاربت کے کہ وہ مال کو خلط ملط کئے بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ اس میں شرکت نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ مضارب صرف مال کے مالک کے لئے کام کرتا ہے اس کے بعد اس کا نفع میں سے اپنی محنت اور مزدوری پانے کا مستحق ہوتا ہے۔ اور یہاں اس کے برخلاف ہے کیونکہ اس میں ہر ایک شریک پوری محنت کرتا ہے۔ یہ بات امام زفر و شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہا کے واسطے بڑی اصل ہے یہاں تک کہ جنس کے ایک اور متحد ہونے کا بھی اعتبار ہے۔ اور دونوں کے مال کو ملا کر رکھنا شرط ہے۔ اسی طرح مال برابر ہونے کے باوجود نفع میں کمی و بیشی جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور شرکت کی قسموں میں سے ایک قسم جو شرکت تقبل واعمال ہے جس کا بیان عنقریب آنے والا ہے وہ بھی اسی قاعدہ اور اصل کی بناء پر جائز نہیں ہے ۔ کیونکہ اس میں مال نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نفع میں شرکت کا ہونا عقد کی طرف نسبت کرنے کی وجہ سے ہے۔ مال کی طرف اضافت کرنے کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے کیونکہ عقد اور معاملہ ہی کو شرکت کہتے ہیں۔ اس لئے اس نام کے معنی کا اس میں پایا جانا ضروری ہے اس بناء پر خلط ملط کرنا شرط نہ ہوا۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ درہم و دینار ایسی چیز نہیں ہے جو عقد میں متعین ہو اس لئے نفع حاصل ہونا راس المال سے نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ اس تصرف سے ہے جو راس المال میں ہوتا ہے یعنی راس المال کے ذریعہ سے کام کرنے پر نفع ملتا ہے۔ کیونکہ ہر شر یک آدھے مال میں اصیل اور دوسرے آدھے میں وکیل ہوتا ہے۔ اور جب خلط ملط کئے بغیر تصرف اور تجارت کے کاموں میں شرکت پائی گئی تو اس محنت اور تصرف سے جو کچھ حاصل ہوا یعنی نفع اس میں بھی خلط کے بغیر ہی شرکت پائی گئی۔ اور یہ بھی مضاربت کے مثل ہو گئی ۔ اس طرح خلاصہ کلام یہ ہوا کہ امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک نفع کی نسبت رأس المال کی طرف ہے ۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک عقد اور معاملہ کے مطابق جو کچھ کاروباری کام کرنے پڑتے ہیں اس کی طرف ہے ) پس ہمارے نزدیک مالوں کے جنس کا متحد ہونا۔ اور برابر مالوں میں نفع کا بھی برابر ہونا کچھ شرط نہیں ہے۔ اور لوگوں کے کام قبول کرنے میں عقد شرکت کرنا صحیح ہے۔
He said: Partnership is valid even if they do not mix the capital. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: It is not valid except after mixing the capital and this because the subject is capital and therefore the specification of capital is required, contrary to mudaraba because it is not a partnership but rather he works for the owner of capital and deserves a share for his work. Here it is otherwise, and this is a great principle for them such that unification of type is considered and mixing is required, and inequality in profit is not allowed with equality in capital, and partnership of acceptance and actions is not valid due to lack of capital. Our proof: Partnership in profit is attributed to the contract, not to the capital, because the contract is called partnership, so the meaning of this name must be realized in it, so mixing was not a condition. And because dirhams and dinars are not specified, so profit is not obtained by capital but rather by transaction, because he is an owner in half and an agent in half. When partnership is realized in transaction without mixing, it is realized in the obtained (profit) without it, and it becomes like mudaraba, so unification of type and equality in profit are not required, and partnership of acceptance is valid.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage presents the dispute about whether mixing (khalat) the capital of two partners is a condition for a valid partnership (shirkat al-ʿaqd). Imam Muhammad (the author) states the Hanafi position that mixing is not required. Zufar and al-Shafiʿi require mixing because they argue that profit is a fruit of capital (thamarat al-māl), so if capital is not mixed, profit cannot be shared. The Hanafi rebuttal is that partnership is a contract (ʿaqd) that itself creates sharing in profit, and profit is earned through mutual effort and transaction (taṣarruf), not from the capital itself. They analogize to mudāraba where mixing is not required. The Hanafis conclude that mixing is not a condition, and thus unified type of capital (jins) and equality of shares are not required, and partnerships of acceptance (shirkat al-taqabbul) are valid.

Key Terms
خلط (khalṭ): Mixing of two partners' capitals physically so that they become indistinguishable.
شركة العقد (shirkat al-ʿaqd): Partnership based on contract, as opposed to joint ownership (shirkat al-milk).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for a valid partnership (shirkat al-ʿaqd)?
A) Both partners contribute capital of the same type (jins).
B) The capital is physically mixed (khalat).
C) Both partners have legal capacity to contract.
D) The profit-sharing ratio is clearly specified.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require mixing of capital for a valid partnership; the partnership contract itself creates sharing in profit through mutual agency.
